# TennoWorth — End-to-End Onboarding Friction Audit
> Generated 2026-06-23 by the `smoothest-onboarding` loop-until-dry workflow (run `wf_4eeb0eaf-a77`, 6 rounds, 225 agents). Discovery-only pass — **no code was changed.** Every finding below survived an adversarial skeptic-verify pass.

## How to read this
- **158 findings confirmed**, deduplicated by the synthesizer into **77 ranked actions** across **9 themes**.
- Severity of the raw 158: **34 major**, **96 minor**, **28 polish**.
- **The loop did NOT converge.** It ran to the 6-round cap with a *flat* per-round yield (~25 new confirmed/round), meaning the onboarding friction space is genuinely deep at this granularity — this is a thorough snapshot, not an exhausted one. Prioritise by the ranked list below rather than chasing raw count.

### Round log
- round 1: 49 fresh -> 42 confirmed (total 42)
- round 2: 26 fresh -> 23 confirmed (total 65)
- round 3: 22 fresh -> 20 confirmed (total 85)
- round 4: 28 fresh -> 25 confirmed (total 110)
- round 5: 30 fresh -> 22 confirmed (total 132)
- round 6: 32 fresh -> 26 confirmed (total 158)

## The single highest-leverage fix
Write the entire login → serve → connect listing flow into the install-path onboarding AND the in-app Companion tab: a 3-line getting-started block (`wfm-fetch-inventory login` once, then `serve` in a real terminal, then paste the printed `http://127.0.0.1:<random>?token=…` — not 5173) plus a `serve` is-terminal guard that prints an actionable message on the os-error-6 TTY failure. This single block resolves the deepest structural gap (the entire order-management half of the product is undiscoverable and gated behind two undocumented subcommands), the #1 confirmed live blocker (serve TTY passphrase crash), and the 5173-vs-random-port confusion at once.

## Ranked punch list
_Themes ordered by aggregate severity; items within a theme by impact × reach._

### The listing half (login → serve → connect) is undiscoverable and the serve step crashes
*18 items — 8 major, 9 minor, 1 polish*

- **[🔴 major] serve dies on 'reading passphrase / os error 6' outside a real TTY with no detection, hint, or doc**  
  _Who:_ linux; any user launching serve from a non-TTY context (IDE run button, nohup, systemd, pipe, some multiplexers); on Windows from a non-console host  
  _Friction:_ The confirmed live blocker: user finished login successfully, runs serve, and it crashes with a raw libc errno and no next step; the --passphrase-stdin escape hatch exists but is documented in zero user-facing places.  
  _Fix:_ In run_serve, guard with std::io::stdin().is_terminal() before rpassword and bail with 'serve needs a real terminal to read your passphrase, or pipe it: echo … | wfm-fetch-inventory serve --passphrase-stdin'; map os-error-6 to the same message. Document --passphrase-stdin in the README/connect panel. Cheap win on the message; the guard is small.
- **[🔴 major] No surface anywhere states the install → login → serve → connect ORDER**  
  _Who:_ all users wanting to list on WFM (the differentiator over browse.wf/warframe.me)  
  _Friction:_ Each subcommand is described in isolation (or not at all); the dependency chain (login writes the JWT serve needs) is reverse-engineerable only by hitting CLI bails in sequence. README documents only fetch; install 'Next steps' stop at drop-in; serve appears once as a placeholder.  
  _Fix:_ Add one ordered checklist (install → login once → serve, leave running → paste printed URL) to the Companion connect panel's not-connected state, the installer Next-steps, and a new FAQ entry. Make login's success message name the next command. Cheap, high-leverage copy work.
- **[🔴 major] Companion-connect tab says 'Required to list on WFM' but offers no on-ramp and no recovery for the two live serve failures**  
  _Who:_ all users; the TTY-failure half and port-confusion half land precisely here  
  _Friction:_ The connect strip shows only 'Not connected · paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' + a 'http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…' placeholder; no command, no 'run in a real terminal', no note the port is random and NOT 5173, no link to learn serve. (Confirmed live.)  
  _Fix:_ Add inline help under the input: the literal login→serve commands, 'run serve in a real terminal', 'the port is random — not the website's 5173', and what os-error-6 means. Optionally special-case a pasted :5173 in parseCompanionUrl with a tailored error.
- **[🔴 major] Onboarding stepper + both installers stop at 'drop it in' and teach 'Run it once' — actively foreclosing the persistent serve lifecycle**  
  _Who:_ all users; reinforced by InstallWidget 'One command — paste and go' and README 'One-shot — doesn't keep running'  
  _Friction:_ The taught 3-step model is fetch→drop→read; the listing half needs a long-running daemon and two more subcommands, so users finish believing the product is read-only and later close the serve terminal because they were told it's one-shot.  
  _Fix:_ Add an optional 4th stepper step / post-load nudge ('Want to list in bulk? login then serve, leave it running'), and scope the README 'one-shot' claim to fetch only (serve runs until Ctrl-C). Cheap copy fix.
- **[🔴 major] In-app FAQ has zero entries on obtaining/connecting the serve URL despite the connect box demanding it**  
  _Who:_ all users who open the FAQ (the natural help destination) to learn how to list  
  _Friction:_ Six FAQ entries cover ban-safety/data/prices/sync/Overwolf/rivens; none mention serve, login, the passphrase, or how to get the connect URL.  
  _Fix:_ Add a single FAQ entry 'How do I connect the companion to list items?' walking login → serve (in a terminal) → copy the printed URL → paste, noting the port/token change every run and the TTY requirement. Cheap win.
- **[🔴 major] Connect shows green 'Connected' for a wrong/stale token because /health is unauthenticated; the authed probe's 401 is swallowed**  
  _Who:_ all users; especially returning users (serve mints a new token every run) and on auto-verify at page load  
  _Friction:_ verifyCompanion pings only /health (no token), or calls the authed getPendingPlan and discards its 401, so the app reports green against a stale/wrong token, then fails opaquely with 'missing or invalid X-Session-Token' only after the user hand-tunes a 50-item batch and hits Send.  
  _Fix:_ Make verifyCompanion treat a 401 from the token-bearing probe as a connect failure ('wrong token — re-copy the full URL; the token changes every serve restart') instead of swallowing it; only show green after an authed call succeeds. Cheap (stop swallowing the existing call).
- **[🔴 major] Companion/login/serve appear in zero install-path or README onboarding**  
  _Who:_ all users; a cold-start user following README+installer+widget has no path to the listing payoff  
  _Friction:_ companion/README.md documents only fetch (login and serve are entirely absent); install.sh/install.ps1 'Next steps' and InstallWidget never mention them.  
  _Fix:_ Add a Subcommands section (fetch/login/serve) to companion/README.md and a 'To list on WFM' stanza to the installer Next-steps + InstallWidget. Overlaps the ordered-checklist fix; do once.
- **[🔴 major] Every companion escape-hatch flag (--port, --pid, --passphrase-stdin, --platform-tag, --jwt-path) exists only in --help**  
  _Who:_ all users who hit the exact failures the flags fix (port collision, TTY passphrase death, wrong process picked, mis-detected platform)  
  _Friction:_ The binary ships the fix for each known failure but the user can't discover it short of running --help, which nothing tells them to do.  
  _Fix:_ Reference the relevant flag in each failure's error text (bind-failed → --port; passphrase prompt failure → --passphrase-stdin; no-creds → --pid) and add a flags table to companion/README.md. Cheap, high-payoff.
- **[🟡 minor] Wrong/empty passphrase on serve aborts the whole process instead of re-prompting**  
  _Who:_ all users; a single typo means re-running serve (and possibly re-fighting the TTY issue)  
  _Friction:_ decrypt_jwt failure exits the binary with no retry loop.  
  _Fix:_ Wrap the interactive passphrase prompt + decrypt in a 3-attempt retry loop. Cheap.
- **[🟡 minor] Listing tabs (Companion, My orders) only render after an inventory is loaded; cold-start page hides them entirely**  
  _Who:_ all users; a user who installed specifically to manage listings sees no path until they drop a file  
  _Friction:_ The connect surface is gated behind a successful inventory drop, coupling two logically independent steps and hiding the differentiator on first visit.  
  _Fix:_ Expose a lightweight 'Connect companion' entry (or a stepper teaser) on the cold-start page, or state on the landing that connecting requires loading inventory first.
- **[🟡 minor] Saved companion URL+token persists across sessions but the token regenerates every serve restart, with no copy warning it's per-process**  
  _Who:_ all returning users who restart serve (reboot, rebuild, closed terminal)  
  _Friction:_ 'Paste it once' + durable localStorage train the user the connection is permanent; on the next visit the saved URL is silently dead (new random port + token).  
  _Fix:_ In serve stdout and the connect panel, note 'this URL changes every restart — re-paste after restarting serve'; label the saved connection accordingly.
- **[🟡 minor] verifyCompanion auto-runs on every page load and surfaces a raw 'Failed to fetch' / red dot for returning users whose serve isn't running**  
  _Who:_ all returning users who only want to read the sell list  
  _Friction:_ A dead loopback port on reload is the normal case, but it's rendered as an error (red nav dot everywhere; raw fetch exception on the Companion tab).  
  _Fix:_ Treat a clean connection-refused on a saved config as the neutral 'companion offline — start serve and reconnect' state, not a red error; add a short fetch timeout.
- **[🟡 minor] connectCompanion clears the input before verify runs, so a failed connect leaves an empty box + disabled button with no one-click retry**  
  _Who:_ all users on a first/failed connect attempt  
  _Friction:_ On verify failure the input is already blank and Connect is disabled (needs non-empty input), forcing a full re-paste of the URL every retry.  
  _Fix:_ Only clear companionInput after verify succeeds, and add a Retry button in the error state that re-verifies the still-saved config.
- **[🟡 minor] Companion-connect input only accepts the full ?token= URL; copying the bare 'listening on' line or host:port dead-ends**  
  _Who:_ all users; serve prints multiple address-ish lines and the most prominent one lacks the token  
  _Friction:_ The natural copy ('Companion listening on http://127.0.0.1:PORT') has no token, so the paste fails validation.  
  _Fix:_ Have serve print only ONE 'paste THIS' line (already partly labeled 'In the web app, set the companion URL to:'), and make the missing-token error point at 'the line ending in ?token=…, not the listening-on line'.
- **[🟡 minor] serve front-loads two blocking WFM calls after the passphrase prompt but before printing a URL**  
  _Who:_ all users on offline / expired-JWT / Cloudflare-1015; bites returning users at the catalog/me fetch  
  _Friction:_ If the saved JWT expired or the network blips, serve dies with a raw status after the user already typed the passphrase, and no URL is ever printed.  
  _Fix:_ Bind the port and print the URL first, then warm the catalog / resolve /me lazily on first authed request; special-case 401→'run login again' and 1015→'rate-limited, retry'.
- **[🟡 minor] Expired JWT surfaces as raw 'WFM HTTP 401' on the Orders tab / serve startup with no 'log in again' pointer**  
  _Who:_ all returning users (months later, when the JWT expires); not first-run  
  _Friction:_ The orders auto-load (or serve startup /me) relays a bare 401; the only copy explaining re-login lives in a terminal closed weeks ago.  
  _Fix:_ Map 401/403 from /me and order routes to 'Your WFM login expired — run wfm-fetch-inventory login again', both at serve startup and in relayed per-order errors.
- **[🟡 minor] Per-item rejections, 409 'plan already running', visibility failures, and slug-mismatch refusals surface as raw text or dead-end the modal**  
  _Who:_ all users at the bulk-list action; double-submit, thin markets, mid-batch failures  
  _Friction:_ 409 is transient but treated as terminal with no retry-after; a makeAllVisible failure flips to phase='error' and wipes the created-listings table; 'slug mismatch — refusing' shows raw multiplier math.  
  _Fix:_ Disable Send while in-flight; special-case 409 with a Retry-after-wait; surface visibility failures inline (keep the results table) with a Retry; translate 'slug mismatch' to plain language ('price looks far below market — likely matched the wrong item; skip it').
- **[⚪ polish] The word 'companion' overloads three concepts (binary, install anchor, connect tab); 'login' overloads game-login vs the login subcommand**  
  _Who:_ all users navigating between install, fetch, and connect  
  _Friction:_ 'Open the Companion' is ambiguous; every visible 'login' string means the game title screen, so users don't suspect a separate login subcommand exists.  
  _Fix:_ Rename the connect tab ('Connect / List on WFM') and reserve 'login' in copy for the WFM login subcommand ('past the title screen' for the game prerequisite).

### inventory.json discoverability — the dropzone points at the wrong place
*5 items — 3 minor, 2 polish*

- **[🟡 minor] DropZone 'saves it next to itself' sends the stuck user to the binary dir, not ~/Downloads**  
  _Who:_ all users; worse on Windows where %LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv is a hidden folder  
  _Friction:_ The one piece of copy attached to the action a confused user is performing (finding the file) misdirects them to ~/.local/bin / %LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv; every other surface and the CLI success line say Downloads. (Confirmed live, DropZone.svelte:64.)  
  _Fix:_ Change DropZone.svelte:64 to 'saves it to your Downloads folder' to match main.rs/App.svelte/FAQ. One-line cheap win, highest in-app misdirection at the moment of need.
- **[🟡 minor] FAQ + dropzone show the unix path '~/Downloads' to Windows users**  
  _Who:_ windows users hunting for the file  
  _Friction:_ App.svelte:1523 (and the dropzone) print '~/Downloads', a tilde path that doesn't resolve in Explorer/PowerShell; the binary writes to C:\Users\you\Downloads.  
  _Fix:_ Make the copy OS-neutral: 'your Downloads folder (C:\Users\you\Downloads on Windows, ~/Downloads on Linux)'. Cheap.
- **[🟡 minor] No success checkpoint between fetch and the dropzone; the in-app step never reflects fetch state**  
  _Who:_ all users, especially CLI novices who don't parse stderr  
  _Friction:_ fetch confirmation lives only in stderr; the browser shows the same idle stepper, so the user can't tell step 02 worked.  
  _Fix:_ Add a one-line 'How do I know it worked? Look for "Wrote …/Downloads/inventory.json" in the terminal' note under step 02. Cheap.
- **[⚪ polish] fetch falls back to CWD silently when ~/Downloads is absent (and ignores OneDrive redirection on Windows)**  
  _Who:_ edge: minimal Linux homes without ~/Downloads; windows with OneDrive-redirected Downloads  
  _Friction:_ default_out_path writes to current_dir() with no distinct warning; on Windows it assembles %USERPROFILE%\Downloads rather than the known-folder API, so OneDrive redirection can miss.  
  _Fix:_ On CWD fallback print a distinct 'Downloads not found — wrote to <cwd> instead'; on Windows resolve Downloads via SHGetKnownFolderPath/UserDirs::download_dir.
- **[⚪ polish] No explicit 'loaded inventory.json (N items)' confirmation; only a small sidebar filename pin, with no real inventory-age signal**  
  _Who:_ all users; especially anyone with several inventory.json copies in Downloads  
  _Friction:_ On load the app jumps to the Sell view with only inventoryName in the sidebar; the 'saved N ago' pin reflects app-load time, not the inventory's true age, so a stale/wrong file goes unnoticed.  
  _Fix:_ Show a brief load confirmation (filename + owned/sellable counts); since inventory.json carries no fetch timestamp, at least warn if the picked file's mtime is days old.

### Stale market data is too quiet for a 'sell right now' tool
*5 items — 1 major, 3 minor, 1 polish*

- **[🔴 major] Per-surface staleness (Baro/relics/vault/sets) is shipped in market.json (surface_fetched_at) but never read; the dot keys only on updated_at**  
  _Who:_ all users during warframestat upstream outages; especially the Baro countdown, which can render actively-wrong times under a green dot  
  _Friction:_ updated_at is rewritten every cron run even when a surface rides preserved data for days; the prototype ignores surface_fetched_at, so a frozen Baro/relic/vault surface reads green/current.  
  _Fix:_ Read surface_fetched_at in the Baro/relic/vault/set views; show 'schedule/data N days old' (or hide the surface) when its stamp lags updated_at past a threshold. Producer already computes it — consumer just needs to honor it.
- **[🟡 minor] Stale-data warning is a single aria-hidden color dot with no qualitative word and no banner**  
  _Who:_ all users (screen-reader users get nothing); the dot is the only fresh-vs-stale distinction beyond a neutral relative time  
  _Friction:_ The freshness dot is aria-hidden="true" with no aria-label and no 'fresh/aging/stale' word; there's no red-state banner, so weeks-stale prices read like fresh ones at a glance. (Confirmed live; the visible 'N ago' text does carry age, so info isn't entirely absent.)  
  _Fix:_ Add a qualitative word next to the time ('29 min ago · fresh' / '18 d ago · stale'), drop aria-hidden (give the dot an aria-label or sr-only phrase), and show a 'prices may be outdated' banner above the Sell table when stale. Cheap-ish, high trust value.
- **[🟡 minor] Freshness cue exists only on the Sell view; Baro/Relics/Sets show prices with no staleness signal**  
  _Who:_ all users who navigate to Baro/Relics/Sets to make plat decisions  
  _Friction:_ The dot+time render only inside effectiveView==='sell'; equally price-driven surfaces give zero freshness indication.  
  _Fix:_ Lift the freshness indicator to a global location (sidebar or workspace header) so it shows on every price-bearing view.
- **[🟡 minor] FAQ 'How current are the prices?' hard-asserts a 2-hour refresh and lives in a collapsed accordion on another view**  
  _Who:_ all users who consult the FAQ when prices look odd; the decoder ring for the dot is two navigations + a click away  
  _Friction:_ The only color-code legend is buried; the copy states the 2h cadence as unconditional fact, falsely reassuring during a pipeline stall, and isn't adjacent to the dot it explains.  
  _Fix:_ Add a title/tooltip on the dot with the thresholds, reframe the FAQ to say the cron CAN stall and point to the displayed age as source-of-truth, and add a 'data looks old / dot is red?' entry.
- **[⚪ polish] No absolute snapshot timestamp anywhere; missing updated_at renders a neutral dot + em-dash with no 'unknown' state**  
  _Who:_ edge: a partial/corrupt market.json (no documented pipeline produces this); all users wanting to cross-check freshness  
  _Friction:_ The 'Market data' stat has no title= revealing the real date; a missing updated_at falls through to the base gray dot with no '.dot.unknown' style and a bare '—'.  
  _Fix:_ Add title={new Date(market.updated_at).toLocaleString()} on the stat; add a .dot.unknown rule + 'freshness unknown' text for the missing-timestamp case. Cheap.

### Returning-user and bad-input failure modes dead-end the whole app
*6 items — 4 major, 1 minor, 1 polish*

- **[🔴 major] A valid-but-non-inventory JSON resolves to 0 owned and dumps the user into the full app with no diagnosis**  
  _Who:_ all users; easy to hit since the dropzone invites foreign exports (market.json, AlecaFrame, warframe-api-helper) or empty accounts  
  _Friction:_ flattenInventory never throws on a wrong shape; phase becomes 'done' with owned=0, and emptyReason bails when owned.size===0, so the Sell pane shows 'Owned 0' and nothing else — indistinguishable from 'you own nothing'.  
  _Fix:_ After resolve, if owned.size===0 on a non-trivial input, keep the landing and show 'No tradeable items found in <name> — is this really an inventory.json from the companion? (We read Suits/LongGuns/Recipes/… keys.)'
- **[🔴 major] Error phase hides BOTH the stepper and the dropzone, leaving a dead-end error card with no retry**  
  _Who:_ all users whose first action fails (offline, market.json 404, catalog fetch error, wrong-shape file)  
  _Friction:_ phase==='error' renders only 'Error: {error}'; the DropZone they were using vanishes, and a full page reload is the only recovery.  
  _Fix:_ Render the DropZone (and stepper) in the error phase with the error as a non-fatal banner, or add a 'Try another file' button that reopens the picker.
- **[🔴 major] Returning user offline is dumped to the cold-start landing and loses their restored inventory**  
  _Who:_ all returning users opening the app offline or during a transient market.json 404  
  _Friction:_ onMount restores the snapshot then awaits loadMarket(); a fetch failure sets phase='error', which renders only the landing — the restored owned map is in state but unreachable, with a cryptic 'Failed to fetch'.  
  _Fix:_ On the restore path treat a market load failure as non-fatal: keep phase='done', render from the restored snapshot, and show a dismissible 'couldn't refresh prices — showing last-known data / offline' banner.
- **[🔴 major] Empty-state diagnosis ignores the preset/tag/vault clauses that actually zeroed the table**  
  _Who:_ all users who click a non-default preset (Vaulted/Trending) or a tag chip and own nothing matching  
  _Friction:_ emptyReason walks only price/owned/type/kept; clicking 'Vaulted' with no vaulted primes yields a blank table whose card blames the price threshold and offers a fix (relaxFilters) that can't work for tag-distinguished presets (Ducats/Sets).  
  _Fix:_ Extend emptyReason to count vaultOnly/minVol/minMedian/activeTags like computeResults does, with branches ('You own no vaulted prime parts', etc.) and a 'Back to Default preset' action that resets the preset rather than nudging a no-op slider.
- **[🟡 minor] market.json load failure shows a dev-only 'run csv_to_market_json.py' hint (or raw 'Failed to fetch') with no retry**  
  _Who:_ all users on a hosted site during CDN blip / half-deploy / offline; not the healthy path (market.json is committed same-origin)  
  _Friction:_ The only recovery instruction tells an end user to run a Python build script; a true no-network case shows a raw 'Failed to fetch' card with no Retry.  
  _Fix:_ Gate the Python hint behind import.meta.env.DEV; for production show 'Couldn't reach the price snapshot — check your connection and retry' with a Retry button.
- **[⚪ polish] No-match name filter dead-ends to a blank table with no message and no clear-filter button**  
  _Who:_ all users who type a name filter that matches nothing  
  _Friction:_ ResultsTable renders an empty tbody with '0 rows · sorted by Score' and no empty state; emptyReason only covers upstream price/owned/type/kept exclusions. (Confirmed live with 'zzzzznomatch'.)  
  _Fix:_ Add an {:else} empty-row state in ResultsTable: 'No items match "<query>" — clear filter' with a clear button.

### Install / first-build friction
*13 items — 1 major, 10 minor, 2 polish*

- **[🔴 major] Windows .exe is unsigned — SmartScreen/Defender blocks it on first run with no doc or 'Run anyway' guidance**  
  _Who:_ windows users (post-publish); manual-download route trips the full-screen prompt that the piped installer's IWR write avoids  
  _Friction:_ release-companion.yml has no signing; nothing in install.ps1/InstallWidget/FAQ/SECURITY.md prepares the user for 'Windows protected your PC' on an unsigned memory-scanning binary — many will assume malware and abandon.  
  _Fix:_ Sign the release (even a cheap Authenticode cert builds reputation) or add an explicit 'Windows will warn you this is unsigned — More info → Run anyway, here's why we can't sign yet' section to the FAQ + install.ps1 Next-steps + an Unblock-File note for the manual route.
- **[🟡 minor] setcap is wiped on every rebuild/reinstall; the rebuild-companion skill doesn't re-apply it**  
  _Who:_ linux from-source / dev users on every rebuild cycle  
  _Friction:_ The capability the user explicitly granted vanishes on the next cargo build, failing fetch — though the reactive ptrace error already prints the exact copy-pasteable setcap line and the rebuild caveat.  
  _Fix:_ Have the rebuild-companion skill / a cargo wrapper re-apply setcap (or print a one-line reminder) immediately after build. The reactive recovery message already exists, so this is the one genuine gap.
- **[🟡 minor] Step-02 / InstallWidget setcap line hardcodes ~/.local/bin, but the only pre-release path (cargo build) puts the binary at companion/target/release**  
  _Who:_ linux from-source users (the only kind pre-release) who copy the in-app setcap command  
  _Friction:_ setcap ~/.local/bin/wfm-fetch-inventory fails with 'No such file or directory' against a path the source build never created.  
  _Fix:_ Make the setcap snippet path-agnostic: sudo setcap cap_sys_ptrace=eip "$(command -v wfm-fetch-inventory)", or show the target/release path for the source path. Runtime ptrace error already self-corrects via current_exe().
- **[🟡 minor] Stepper step 02 teaches a bare 'wfm-fetch-inventory' that won't be on PATH in the same session**  
  _Who:_ all users; Linux where ~/.local/bin isn't on PATH yet, Windows where the PATH change applies only to future shells  
  _Friction:_ The website snippet assumes the happy PATH case the installers themselves warn may not hold; user gets 'command not found' with no in-stepper recovery (the caveat is in installer stderr that scrolled away).  
  _Fix:_ Show the path-qualified form (~/.local/bin/wfm-fetch-inventory) or add a one-line 'command not found? open a fresh terminal / run the full path' note adjacent to the snippet.
- **[🟡 minor] Three docs disagree on the Linux run method (companion README leads with sudo; everything else leads with setcap)**  
  _Who:_ linux users; whichever doc they land on changes their privilege posture  
  _Friction:_ companion/README.md headlines 'Easiest: sudo wfm-fetch-inventory' (root-owned writes, chowned back) while install.sh/CLAUDE.md/InstallWidget lead with setcap.  
  _Fix:_ Flip the README to setcap-first, demote sudo to the explicit fallback, and align the invocation form. Cheap.
- **[🟡 minor] The sudo fallback prints a bare 'sudo wfm-fetch-inventory' that secure_path strips**  
  _Who:_ linux users who choose the no-setcap path on Debian/Ubuntu/Fedora/Arch (secure_path excludes ~/.local/bin)  
  _Friction:_ install.sh:110 prints 'sudo $BIN_NAME' bare, which fails 'command not found' even though the non-sudo line two lines up worked.  
  _Fix:_ Make it absolute: sudo "$DEST/$BIN_NAME" (mirror the setcap line). One-line cheap win.
- **[🟡 minor] No guidance on how a non-technical Windows user opens PowerShell; execution-policy not addressed for save-then-run**  
  _Who:_ windows non-technical users (AlecaFrame's core audience)  
  _Friction:_ The only Windows instruction is the iwr|iex one-liner; nothing says 'press Win, type PowerShell, Enter', and a saved-then-run install.ps1 hits the disabled-scripts policy.  
  _Fix:_ Add a 'Open PowerShell (press Win, type PowerShell)' preamble to the Windows tab; note the piped form is the supported one or document -ExecutionPolicy Bypass for the save path.
- **[🟡 minor] In-app step 02 omits the 'open the trade/profile screen to force an auth call' prerequisite every other surface carries**  
  _Who:_ all users who follow the on-page stepper rather than installer stderr; reliability booster, not always required  
  _Friction:_ Step 02 says only 'past the login screen'; without a recent authed network call the accountId/nonce may not be resident, yielding 'No accountId/nonce pair found' on the first run.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'open the trade or profile screen once (forces an auth call), then run:' to step 02, matching install.sh/README. The CLI error already prints the fix, so this is self-recovering — cheap copy parity.
- **[🟡 minor] Windows OpenProcess error names 'same user / pid' but omits the dominant elevation/integrity-mismatch cause; install.ps1 actively nudges the wrong way**  
  _Who:_ windows users who deviate to an elevated terminal (often after install.ps1's own 'try elevated' hint)  
  _Friction:_ ERROR_ACCESS_DENIED is commonly an integrity mismatch (game non-elevated, terminal elevated); the error points at the wrong fix and install.ps1:92 steers users to escalate, worsening it.  
  _Fix:_ Reword the OpenProcess error to lead with 'run this terminal at the SAME elevation as Warframe — normally a non-admin PowerShell'; remove/qualify install.ps1's 'try elevated' suggestion.
- **[🟡 minor] install.ps1 corrupts a fresh user PATH with a leading semicolon when no user Path exists**  
  _Who:_ windows users on a clean profile with no user-scoped Path  
  _Friction:_ GetEnvironmentVariable returns null, so the write produces ';C:\Users\…\wfminv' — an empty PATH segment (parsed as CWD) persisted permanently; the dedupe guard doesn't self-heal it.  
  _Fix:_ Guard the null case: split on ';', drop empties, append $Dest only if absent, re-join. Cheap.
- **[🟡 minor] Manual-download link + pipe-install asset names hardcode OWNER/REPO**  
  _Who:_ all users (post-publish prep); the piped path aborts honestly, only the manual <details> GitHub link 404s silently  
  _Friction:_ Until the repo is registered, the 'download manually' link is a guaranteed 404; the piped installer fails gracefully with a build-from-source hint.  
  _Fix:_ Tracked in CLAUDE.md open items — replace OWNER/REPO in install.sh/install.ps1/InstallWidget in one pass at publish; until then mirror the installer's honest 'not published yet' message in the manual <details>.
- **[⚪ polish] macOS visitors get the Linux installer (hard-exits) and an InstallWidget with no active/detected tab**  
  _Who:_ edge: detected-Mac users (an unsupported, non-viable platform — Warframe has no native Mac client)  
  _Friction:_ commands.mac maps to install.sh which exits 1 with a Linux/Windows-only message; with activeOs='mac' neither tab highlights, so the widget looks broken.  
  _Fix:_ Clamp activeOs to 'linux' for mac and add a small 'macOS: build from source / no native client' note, or have install.sh print a Mac-specific message.
- **[⚪ polish] install.ps1 leaves a stray temp file on every download/checksum failure (no try/finally; Linux installer has a trap)**  
  _Who:_ windows users on flaky network / pre-release (every placeholder-abort leaks one)  
  _Friction:_ New-TemporaryFile is created before the throw paths and never cleaned up; %TEMP% accumulates orphans across retries.  
  _Fix:_ Wrap download+verify+move in try { … } finally { if (Test-Path $Tmp) { Remove-Item -Force $Tmp } }. Cheap.

### The what-to-sell payoff — trust and correctness of the differentiator
*16 items — 5 major, 8 minor, 3 polish*

- **[🔴 major] Score-explainer formula doesn't match the scores (clamp divergence) and the same wrong formula is repeated in the column ? tooltip**  
  _Who:_ all users; concentrated on the clamped troll-undercut rows that float to the top of the Score sort  
  _Friction:_ Banner + Score-header tooltip both say min(owned, vol_48h/2) × low_sell, but scoreRow uses clampedPrice (clearingPrice clamps a cheap ask up to the 90d median); a skeptic who does the published arithmetic on a top row (e.g. Meso W5: 21 vs shown 70) can't reconcile it — undercutting the exact trust the tool sells.  
  _Fix:_ Make the formula honest in both places: '× clearing price (lowest live ask, clamped to the 90-day median for troll/lone asks)', or add a one-line note on rows where clearingPrice != low_sell. Cheap copy fix, high trust value.
- **[🔴 major] 'List N on WFM' acts on the unfiltered global top-50, not the rows the user filtered in the table**  
  _Who:_ all users who narrow the table (name or pill filter) then click List  
  _Friction:_ The name + pill filters are component-local to ResultsTable and never propagate; the CTA/modal stage results.slice(0,50), so a curated 'only peaks' view lists different items than shown — the user posts listings they never intended.  
  _Fix:_ Lift the name/pill filters to App (or emit the filtered set upward) so the CTA stages exactly what the table shows; failing that, label it 'List top 50 (all rows)' and disable/relabel when a table-local filter is active.
- **[🔴 major] Relics dominate the top of Sell while the Relic planner says crack them — two unreconciled verbs for the same items**  
  _Who:_ all users with relic stashes; the #2-ranked 'sell' item can be one the app elsewhere says to crack, and the one-click CTA can list it  
  _Friction:_ Sell ranks relics by sell_score (list them); the planner ranks intact relics by expected plat per crack — different relics, no cross-reference, and ListingReviewModal will queue relics for sale.  
  _Fix:_ On relic rows in Sell, show a 'relic — see planner' pill linking to Relics (and conversely show the relic's list price in the planner); at minimum exclude relics from the default 'List N on WFM' selection.
- **[🔴 major] Set-completion recs tell users to spend plat to flip a set with zero liquidity check, unlike the relic planner which warns**  
  _Who:_ all users acting on a 'Complete X for +Np' card — the only rec that spends real plat  
  _Friction:_ deriveSetRecos uses raw low_sell with no vol gate (and treats an unbuyable low_sell=0 part as free), so on a thin set market the advertised +Np may be unrealizable — user buys parts and holds a dead set.  
  _Fix:_ Gate near-complete recs on a minimum set 48h volume (and the missing parts'), or annotate low-volume cards with the existing 'patience' framing; ideally reuse clearingPrice so the set math inherits the anti-manipulation clamp.
- **[🔴 major] Relic planner hard-caps at 3 cards with no total count and no 'show more'**  
  _Who:_ all users with more than 3 relic types (most end-game players)  
  _Friction:_ deriveRelicPlan slices to 3; the lede says 'Top 3 relics' with no 'of N', no pagination — silently discarding the bulk of a core differentiating surface (unlike the paginated Sell table).  
  _Fix:_ Raise the cap and paginate (or collapsible 'show N more'); at minimum change the lede to 'Top 3 of N relics, ranked by expected plat per crack'.
- **[🟡 minor] Set picks and Relics value parts at raw low_sell, bypassing the troll-ask clamp the Sell table uses — same item, different worth per tab**  
  _Who:_ all users; parts carrying an outlier (troll/fantasy) ask on secondary surfaces  
  _Friction:_ set-recos.ts and relic-planner.ts read me.low_sell directly while sell-score routes through clearingPrice, so a single 1p/2,999p ask skews set net and relic EPP in exactly the way the clamp was built to prevent.  
  _Fix:_ Reuse clearingPrice() for component/reward valuation in set-recos.ts and relic-planner.ts so all three value surfaces agree.
- **[🟡 minor] Relic planner silently excludes non-Intact relics and the empty state falsely says 'No relics in your inventory'**  
  _Who:_ all users who refine relics to Radiant before cracking (common end-game); a persisted relics view shows the false message  
  _Friction:_ relic-planner drops Exceptional/Flawless/Radiant; a user holding 50 Radiant relics gets no Relics tab or a 'No relics' message that's plainly false.  
  _Fix:_ Rank refined relics too (use the matching refinement's drop table), or at minimum show 'You own N refined relics; the planner currently models Intact drops only'.
- **[🟡 minor] 'Potential' headline stat is the metric the tool itself labels 'not realistic'**  
  _Who:_ all users; the first big number anchors them on owned×avg, the misconception the product exists to correct  
  _Friction:_ The headline sums owned×avg (disclaimed as 'optimistic upper bound') while there's no headline aggregate of the trustworthy sell_score.  
  _Fix:_ Lead with a realistic aggregate (sum of sell_score / est. plat/day) and label 'Potential' as 'optimistic ceiling' inline.
- **[🟡 minor] Headline stats (Sellable / Potential) and the Sell nav badge silently rescope with the active preset and ignore the table's name/pill filters**  
  _Who:_ all users who click a preset or filter the table  
  _Friction:_ The big 'Potential 12,289p' collapses to 69p on the Vaulted preset (and the nav badge swings 405→217) with no scope label, and stays unchanged when the table is name/pill-filtered — two numbers on screen contradict each other.  
  _Fix:_ Either keep the headline stats inventory-wide (independent of preset/filter) with the filtered count only in the table toolbar, or add a scope label ('Potential in view') plus tooltips.
- **[🟡 minor] The only inline sell-score formula is dismiss-once-forever; the differentiator's explanation can vanish permanently on one stray click**  
  _Who:_ all users; a near-reflex × click on a dismissible card  
  _Friction:_ dismissScoreExplainer writes localStorage permanently; the only remaining explanation is the column ? tooltip.  
  _Fix:_ Make the dismissal session-scoped, or add a persistent 'How scoring works' link/help icon that reopens the banner.
- **[🟡 minor] The first-session score banner stays put on presets that don't sort by Score**  
  _Who:_ all users who land on or click Trending/Ducats  
  _Friction:_ The banner explains the Score column verbatim even when the list is ordered by Δ90d or p/100d, attaching the differentiator explanation to the wrong sort.  
  _Fix:_ Re-word/suppress the banner by activePreset (Trending→explain Δ90d, Ducats→p/100d), or keep it Default-only.
- **[🟡 minor] Default preset renders 14–15 columns and pushes the differentiator signals (Vol 48h, Δ90d, Demand) off-screen behind horizontal scroll**  
  _Who:_ all users on first look (the sell-score Score column IS visible and default-sorted; the supporting evidence columns are not)  
  _Friction:_ Default has no curated columns key so everything renders; common widths show ~6 columns (Item/Own/Score/Avg/Low sell/Top buy) with volume/trend clipped.  
  _Fix:_ Give Default a curated columns list that keeps sell_score/low_sell/volume_48h/delta_90d_pct/ratio on screen, like the other presets; move long-tail columns behind a toggle.
- **[🟡 minor] Unresolved-items notice shows raw internal category names that read like a parse failure**  
  _Who:_ all users on first load (live observation: 'Recipes:322' etc.)  
  _Friction:_ A prominent 'Recipes:322' with internal bucket names reads as 'the tool failed to parse a third of my inventory' rather than 'these aren't tradable'; the reassurance is hover-only.  
  _Fix:_ Lead with meaning ('N items not tradable — quest/resource/new content') and demote the per-category breakdown to a tooltip/disclosure.
- **[⚪ polish] Category facet chip list is ~150 chips, pushing the table below the fold on first load**  
  _Who:_ all users on first load (live observation)  
  _Friction:_ One chip per weapon/warframe family (down to 'akjagara 1') is powerful but visually overwhelming as the first thing under the presets.  
  _Fix:_ Collapse the per-family chips behind a 'more categories' disclosure or group them, keeping the high-value facet chips (peak/hold/patience/vaulted/aug) prominent.
- **[⚪ polish] 'Trending' preset ranks low-value percentage spikes above genuinely valuable movers**  
  _Who:_ all users who click Trending; recoverable by re-sorting  
  _Friction:_ Trending sorts purely by delta_90d_pct, so a +426% blip on a cheap item outranks a higher-plat mover; the floors already exclude the worst penny-junk.  
  _Fix:_ Tie-break/pre-rank by a value floor (require sell_score above a threshold) or a blended momentum×value score.
- **[⚪ polish] Relic planner and the Sell table give two different unreconciled 'best relics' answers**  
  _Who:_ all users who compare the Relics pane against relics in the Sell top  
  _Friction:_ Planner ranks by single-crack EPP, Sell ranks the same relics by sell_score; neither acknowledges the other, so a user can't tell which action the tool recommends.  
  _Fix:_ On relic Sell rows add a 'see Relic planner' affordance and show the relic's list price in the planner, framing 'sell for X' vs 'crack for ~Y' explicitly.

### Discovery / positioning — the landing never differentiates from browse.wf / warframe.me
*5 items — 4 minor, 1 polish*

- **[🟡 minor] No top-level README — the repo's front door for a cold-start contributor/cloner is missing**  
  _Who:_ developers/cloners arriving at the raw repo; also the 'inspect before piping' trust path lands on a directory with no orientation  
  _Friction:_ ls README* is empty; the pitch lives only in index.html noscript and CLAUDE.md (agent-facing).  
  _Fix:_ Add a root README with the pitch (no-Overwolf, Win+Linux equal, what-to-sell), the install one-liners, and the fetch→login→serve→drop-in runbook. Overlaps the listing-flow doc fix.
- **[🟡 minor] The JS-rendered landing never names the differentiator or the competitors; the crisp pitch lives only in noscript/meta**  
  _Who:_ all JS users on the landing (i.e. everyone who can actually use the app); especially incumbents already on warframe.me  
  _Friction:_ The rendered header says only 'rank what's worth selling' — identical to the competitors; liquidity-weighting, Baro timing, set-vs-parts, Linux-equal/Steam Deck, and the names browse.wf/warframe.me are absent from rendered copy.  
  _Fix:_ Promote one sentence of the noscript/meta differentiator into the rendered header ('we weight by 48h trade volume + flag Baro hold/peak timing — on Windows and Linux equally'); add a 'Why not just browse.wf / warframe.me?' FAQ entry naming them and the concrete edge. Cheap, high conversion value.
- **[🟡 minor] Landing promises 'everything happens in your browser' then immediately tells the user to run a native memory scanner; serve runs a local server + hands out a token**  
  _Who:_ privacy-cautious cold-start users (the no-account audience the pitch targets)  
  _Friction:_ The absolute 'nothing leaves your browser' claim is contradicted by a native binary that scans process memory + hits DE's API, and later by serve's local server + token — whiplash at the install-trust moment.  
  _Fix:_ Scope the claim ('the ranking happens entirely in your browser — your inventory is never uploaded to us') and pre-announce the optional local relay ('listing uses a local-only companion server on 127.0.0.1, never the internet').
- **[🟡 minor] FAQ competitor entry is framed defensively ('why no Overwolf') and concedes parity ('the same insights')**  
  _Who:_ the few newcomers who open the FAQ to decide whether to switch  
  _Friction:_ The only competitor entry answers an integration question nobody asked and says 'the same insights', throwing away the genuine functional edge.  
  _Fix:_ Retitle to 'How is this different from warframe.me / browse.wf / AlecaFrame?' and state the concrete edge (liquidity-weighted ranking, Baro timing, set-vs-parts, one-click listing); drop 'the same insights'.
- **[⚪ polish] Landing header drops the cross-platform / Steam Deck hook that meta + noscript lead with**  
  _Who:_ linux / Steam Deck visitors (the highest-intent newcomers) on first paint  
  _Friction:_ 'Windows + Linux equal · Steam Deck' appears in noscript/meta and the post-load sidebar, but never in the pre-install JS header.  
  _Fix:_ Add 'Windows + Linux · no Overwolf · runs on Steam Deck' to the rendered landing header. Cheap.

### Console / platform edge cases (small population, real harm)
*5 items — 1 major, 3 minor, 1 polish*

- **[🔴 major] login hard-defaults --platform pc and never reconciles with the fetch path's auto-detected platform; console players list against the wrong market**  
  _Who:_ edge: Switch/PS/Xbox players using login+serve (small but real; PC dominates WFM)  
  _Friction:_ The documented login invocation bakes 'pc' into the JWT; serve reuses it for /me, orders, and POST order, so listings target the wrong platform with no error at login time.  
  _Fix:_ Default login's platform from the same memory-scanned ct the fetch path detects (mapping STM/ME→pc, NS→switch, etc.), or prompt/confirm at login and warn on disagreement; surface the active platform in the serve banner.
- **[🟡 minor] --platform appears in zero first-run surfaces and the post-connect label defaults its display to 'pc', hiding the mismatch**  
  _Who:_ edge: console players  
  _Friction:_ No doc mentions the flag, and companionPlatform ?? 'pc' renders 'pc' even when null/wrong, so the mismatch is invisible until orders silently target the wrong market.  
  _Fix:_ Document --platform if login is documented; render the connected platform without the silent 'pc' fallback (show 'unknown' / a warning when null).
- **[🟡 minor] Zero guidance for Steam Proton / Flatpak Steam — the dominant Linux launch method**  
  _Who:_ linux users; native Steam/Proton/Lutris work as-is, Flatpak Steam is the uncertain case  
  _Friction:_ No doc acknowledges the launch method; a not-found or permission failure under a sandbox gives the user no breadcrumb (mechanism is less catastrophic than once feared — Flatpak Steam doesn't unshare PIDs by default).  
  _Fix:_ Add a short 'Running Warframe via Steam/Proton/Flatpak' note to the README/install Next-steps and name the case in find_wf_pid's not-found message.
- **[🟡 minor] find_wf_pid returns an arbitrary HashMap match when several processes match; --pid is undocumented; bare 'Warframe.exe' can match the DE launcher**  
  _Who:_ edge: users with a lingering launcher / stale zombie game process  
  _Friction:_ Iteration order is unspecified, so the scan can hit a creds-less process yielding 'No accountId/nonce pair found' on one run and success the next, with --pid documented nowhere; on Windows bare 'Warframe.exe' can grab the launcher.  
  _Fix:_ Prefer Warframe.x64.exe, pick the largest-RSS candidate when several match, and on a no-creds failure list candidate PIDs with the --pid hint (the chosen PID is already printed).
- **[⚪ polish] Controlled Folder Access can block fetch's Downloads write with no CFA hint or documented --out escape**  
  _Who:_ edge: windows users with Defender CFA enabled (off by default) AND willing to run an unsigned binary  
  _Friction:_ fetch fails with a generic 'writing inventory to …' permission error and no CFA framing.  
  _Fix:_ On a Windows write-permission failure add 'Controlled Folder Access may be blocking writes to Downloads — allow this app or use --out'; document --out.

### Two-passphrase mental model + minor copy hygiene
*4 items — 1 minor, 3 polish*

- **[🟡 minor] Cloudflare 1015 / bot-block at signin and catalog load dumps raw HTML/status with no 'rate-limited, wait and retry' framing**  
  _Who:_ all users whose residential IP gets flagged at login despite the browser UA (lower-probability)  
  _Friction:_ Bootstrap GET is Cloudflare-aware, but the signin POST and /v2/items bails show a raw 400-char body / bare status with no 1015 hint.  
  _Fix:_ Detect 429/403 + 'error code: 1015' / cloudflare markers and emit 'warframe.market is rate-limiting this IP (Cloudflare 1015) — wait a few minutes and retry' at the signin and catalog call sites.
- **[⚪ polish] Two unrelated secrets both called 'passphrase' (export/backup vs companion login/JWT) are never disambiguated**  
  _Who:_ all users who set up both the companion login and the device-sync export  
  _Friction:_ Both use AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2 600k and the identical word 'passphrase' with different length rules (12 vs 4), inviting reuse/confusion about which unlocks what.  
  _Fix:_ Name them distinctly ('WFM login passphrase' vs 'export/backup passphrase') and add 'unrelated to the companion login passphrase — pick anything' to the Export dialog.
- **[⚪ polish] Three different Windows invocation strings for the same command across README, installer, and stepper**  
  _Who:_ windows users cross-referencing surfaces  
  _Friction:_ README shows .\wfm-fetch-inventory.exe (correct for a build dir), installer/stepper show bare wfm-fetch-inventory; the .exe-vs-no-.exe and .\-vs-bare inconsistency reads as carelessness.  
  _Fix:_ Pick one canonical post-install invocation (bare, in a fresh terminal) and use it identically; label the build-from-source form as 'run from the build dir'.
- **[⚪ polish] SECURITY.md PowerShell verify snippet prints a bare True/False with no False-handling or success string (Linux block is narrated)**  
  _Who:_ windows users verifying a manual download  
  _Friction:_ The block ends at $expected -eq $actual with no 'if False, do not run it'.  
  _Fix:_ Mirror the Linux block: show expected True, add 'if False, do not run — re-download', point back to install.ps1 for placement.

## Coverage gaps — what this audit did NOT exercise
- Login step (Step 3) network/auth happy path not exercised live — the live walkthrough could not run the real companion (Playwright sandbox blocked reading ~/Downloads), so login success, the passphrase-set UX, and the JWT encryption flow were inspected only by reading code, not observed.
- serve / connect flow never observed end-to-end live — the os-error-6 TTY crash and the 5173-vs-random-port confusion are confirmed from code + prior session reports, but no live serve→connect→list cycle was run in this audit.
- Bulk-listing path (ListingReviewModal, batch create, make-visible, My orders) was reviewed only in code; no real listing was pushed to WFM, so the actual end-to-end act-on-the-sell-list payoff is unverified live.
- Windows journey is entirely code/doc inference — no Windows machine was tested. SmartScreen/Defender behavior, Controlled Folder Access, PowerShell execution policy, OneDrive Downloads redirection, integrity-level OpenProcess failures, and PATH-in-same-session are predicted, not observed.
- macOS is out of scope as a real target (no native Warframe client) — findings there are about a confusing dead-end for an unsupported visitor, not a usable flow.
- Pre-release blockers (OWNER/REPO placeholder, no published GitHub release, unsigned binary) mean the actual download→run install path cannot be exercised by any real user today; install findings are about the future published state.
- Steam Deck / gamepad / touch-only interaction was not tested despite being a named first-class target — the dense facet-chip UI and hover-only tooltips may behave differently with touch/controller input.
- Accessibility was assessed only for the specific aria-hidden freshness dot; no full screen-reader, keyboard-navigation, or color-contrast pass was performed.
- Multi-account / re-fetch workflows (loading a second inventory, the Replace flow, snapshot delta highlighting) were not exercised live.
- Live test fidelity caveat: the uploaded inventory was a pre-existing snapshot from a different account than the fresh ~/Downloads file (md5 differs); all UI/UX findings are inventory-agnostic, but anything depending on a specific account's items was not validated against the canonical fetch output.
- Cron/pipeline staleness was reasoned about from code (surface_fetched_at, reconcile preserve-on-outage) but no actual stalled-pipeline or warframestat-outage state was reproduced in the running app.

---

## Appendix — all confirmed findings with evidence
_Raw verified findings (pre-dedup), grouped by area. Each carries the file:line evidence and the verifier's note._

### `companion-build` (4)

#### [🔴 major] Windows .exe is unsigned — SmartScreen/Defender will block it, and no doc warns the user or tells them how to get past it
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 2: obtaining/running the binary after install.ps1 downloads it
- **Evidence:** .github/workflows/release-companion.yml has zero signing steps (grep for sign/authenticode/codesign/certificate = no matches); SECURITY.md:50-53 advertises only SHA256SUMS, never an Authenticode signature. install.ps1 downloads wfm-fetch-inventory-windows-x86_64.exe (install.ps1:11,43) and drops it in %LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv with no mention of the SmartScreen/Defender prompt that an unsigned, low-reputation .exe reliably triggers on first run.
- **Why it's friction:** A non-technical Windows user double-clicks or runs the freshly-downloaded unsigned binary and hits 'Windows protected your PC' (SmartScreen) or a Defender quarantine. Nothing in install.ps1, the InstallWidget, the FAQ, or SECURITY.md prepares them for this or explains 'More info -> Run anyway'. Many users will assume the tool is malware and abandon. This is the single biggest first-run wall on Windows.
- **Suggested fix:** Either sign the Windows release (Authenticode cert, even a cheap one builds reputation over time), or at minimum add an explicit 'Windows will warn you this is unsigned — click More info -> Run anyway, here's why we can't sign yet' section to the FAQ and the install.ps1 Next-steps block, plus point to the SHA256SUMS verification as the trust substitute.
- **Verifier note:** Severity over-rated as "blocker"; it's a "major" first-run wall, not an absolute block. (a) SmartScreen is bypassable via "More info -> Run anyway" — there is a path forward, unlike a true blocker. (b) The Windows download path is currently unreachable by any real user: install.ps1:10,24-31 hard-fails on the OWNER/REPO placeholder and the GitHub repo/release does not exist yet (pre-release, per branding memory), so no one downloads the .exe today. Also a minor technical nuance: install.ps1 places the binary via PowerShell Move-Item (line 73), not a browser download, so Mark-of-the-Web tagging differs from the "double-click a freshly-downloaded exe" scenario the finder describes — but SmartScreen's app-reputation check still fires on first execution of an unknown unsigned binary, so the friction stands. All three cited evidence points are accurate: no signing in release-companion.yml, SECURITY.md:51-53 advertises only SHA256SUMS, install.ps1 Next-steps (lines 84-94) and InstallWidget.svelte (218 lines, no matches) say nothing about SmartScreen/Defender.

#### [🟡 minor] Manual-download path eats the SmartScreen wall the piped installer dodges — the two install routes have opposite Mark-of-the-Web behavior, undocumented
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 2 — obtaining the binary (InstallWidget 'Prefer to download manually?' vs the iwr|iex one-liner)
- **Evidence:** install.ps1:20/49/73 downloads via `Invoke-WebRequest -OutFile $Tmp` (a `.tmp`) then `Move-Item -Force $Tmp $Bin` — a PowerShell IWR write does NOT attach a Zone.Identifier / Mark-of-the-Web, so the installed exe runs with no Unblock prompt. The manual route in InstallWidget.svelte:106-114 (`<a href=...GitHub releases>`) is a *browser* download, which DOES stamp MotW and trips the full-screen 'Windows protected your PC' SmartScreen on first launch.
- **Why it's friction:** The already-logged 'unsigned exe / SmartScreen' item treats SmartScreen as uniform. It isn't: a user who pipes install.ps1 sails through, but the more cautious user who follows the widget's own 'inspect before piping' advice and downloads manually hits the scariest possible wall. The doc gives no hint that the safer-feeling path is the harder one, and offers no Unblock recovery, so the careful user is punished and may conclude the binary is malware.
- **Suggested fix:** In the InstallWidget 'advanced' <details>, add one line for the manual route: after download, right-click the .exe → Properties → check 'Unblock' (or `Unblock-File .\wfm-fetch-inventory-windows-x86_64.exe`), then expect a SmartScreen 'More info → Run anyway' on first launch. Note that the piped installer avoids this.
- **Verifier note:** The technical mechanism is accurate and verified, but the finder over-rates it as "major" and leans on a non-existent prior item. Corrections: (1) The cited "already-logged 'unsigned exe / SmartScreen' item" does not exist anywhere in the repo — grep across all *.md, SECURITY.md, README, and the memory/ dir for smartscreen|unsigned|unblock|signed-exe returns nothing. So there is no existing item that "treats SmartScreen as uniform"; the finder invented the baseline it claims to correct. (2) Line cites are slightly loose: the GitHub releases <a> is at InstallWidget.svelte:109 inside the <details> block 105-120 (finder said 106-114); install.ps1 IWR/Move-Item are at :49 and :73 (the :20 cite is New-TemporaryFile, not a download). The substance of the evidence holds. (3) Severity: this hits only the minority, advanced path — the manual download is hidden behind a <details> summary "Prefer to download the binary manually?", while the default/promoted route is the one-liner that paste-and-go users take. The asymmetry is real but the harder path is opt-in and self-selected by the cautious, not forced on the typical user, so "major" is too high; minor fits. (4) Whole thing is pre-release and currently inert: $Repo='OWNER/REPO' (install.ps1:10) and the releases href is github.com/OWNER/REPO (InstallWidget.svelte:109), and install.ps1:24-31 hard-throws refusing to run on the placeholder repo, so today neither path yields a runnable exe. It is a valid future-state design gap, not a live blocker. The core asymmetry claim (iwr -OutFile attaches no Zone.Identifier/MotW so no SmartScreen wall, vs browser download stamps MotW and trips the full-screen prompt on an unsigned exe) is technically correct.

#### [🟡 minor] The in-app stepper's only Windows line is a bare reassurance ("no admin needed") and never positively explains the unsigned-binary warning a Windows user WILL hit
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 1-2 transition — the landing stepper a JS-visible Windows visitor reads before downloading
- **Evidence:** prototype/src/App.svelte:919-924: '...Windows: no admin needed. Linux: grant ptrace once (...) and it runs without sudo forever.' That is the entirety of the Windows guidance in the onboarding stepper. No mention of SmartScreen, Defender, or unsigned-binary prompts anywhere in App.svelte (repo-wide grep for smartscreen/defender returns zero hits).
- **Why it's friction:** The stepper spends a full clause teaching Linux users about ptrace/setcap (a real but Linux-only hurdle) and gives Windows users a single comforting half-sentence — yet the dominant first-run Windows obstacle is the unsigned-EXE SmartScreen/Defender block (the build is unsigned; release-companion.yml:26-29 produces a plain msvc .exe with no signtool step). The asymmetry means a Windows user is told the thing that ISN'T their problem ('no admin') and told nothing about the thing that IS. When SmartScreen fires, they have no in-app context that this is expected, and the most common reaction to an unexpected 'Windows protected your PC' on a memory-scanning tool is to delete it as malware. This converts a one-click 'More info -> Run anyway' into an abandonment.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a Windows-specific line to the stepper (parallel to the Linux ptrace line): note the binary is unsigned, that Windows will show a SmartScreen warning on first run, that this is expected for a small open-source tool, and the exact click path (More info -> Run anyway) or the `Unblock-File` command. Honesty here is a trust win, not a deterrent.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate (App.svelte:919-924 is verbatim; repo-wide grep for smartscreen/defender/unsigned/unblock returns zero across prototype, README absent, SECURITY.md, install scripts; release-companion.yml does build a plain msvc .exe with no signtool step, so the binary is genuinely unsigned). But the finder over-rates severity at "major". Corrected to minor: (1) this is onboarding copy / a trust gap, not a functional blocker — after SmartScreen the binary still runs via "More info -> Run anyway"; (2) the Windows distribution path is still pre-release — install.ps1 keeps the OWNER/REPO placeholder and hard-aborts with "No public release exists yet", so no real Windows user can hit this until a release is actually published; (3) the finder implies Windows guidance is absent everywhere, but install.ps1's "Next steps" does give Windows-specific run guidance (covers "Access is denied"/elevation) — it just omits SmartScreen specifically. The asymmetry observation (Linux ptrace clause vs. one Windows half-sentence) and the unsigned-binary fact are both correct; the abandonment-on-SmartScreen reasoning is plausible. Net: a real, unmitigated minor onboarding/trust gap, not a major one.

#### [⚪ polish] SECURITY.md's PowerShell release-verification snippet prints a bare boolean and stops — no install step, no guidance on a False
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 2 — verifying a manually-downloaded Windows binary before running it
- **Evidence:** SECURITY.md:82-86 ends the PowerShell block at `$expected -eq $actual`, which emits `True`/`False` to the console and nothing else. The Linux block above it uses `sha256sum -c` and documents the expected 'OK' output; the PowerShell equivalent documents neither the success string nor what to do, and never says 'now move it onto your PATH / into %LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv'.
- **Why it's friction:** A Windows user who took the manual path specifically because they're cautious gets a one-word `False`/`True` with no interpretation and is then stranded — the doc verified the file but never tells them where to put it or that `False` means STOP. The asymmetry with the fully-narrated Linux snippet again reads as Windows-as-afterthought.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the Linux block: show the expected `True`, add an explicit 'if False, do not run it — re-download', and a final line moving the verified exe into `%LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv` and adding it to PATH (or just point them back at install.ps1).
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is factually accurate (SECURITY.md:82-86 ends at `$expected -eq $actual` with no success-string or False-handling comment; the Linux block at 74-78 documents `OK`), so the asymmetry is real and severity is correctly rated polish. But the finder's IMPACT framing is inflated and partly wrong: (1) This is the section titled "How to verify a release" (line 70), not an install section. The "stranded — never told where to put it / PATH" complaint asks a checksum-verification snippet to do the install flow's job. install.ps1 already fully handles placement (%LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv, lines 12-13, 73-74), PATH (78-82), and next steps (84-94). The suggested fix would duplicate install.ps1 into a verify-only snippet. (2) The user comparing two SHA-256 hashes via PowerShell already understands equal=match; interpreting True/False on an equality test is near-zero cognitive load. So this is a genuine but trivial doc-narration nit, not friction that blocks or meaningfully annoys a real user.

### `companion-fetch` (18)

#### [🔴 major] In-app 'Run it once' snippet shows a bare `wfm-fetch-inventory` command that fails with command-not-found when ~/.local/bin isn't on PATH — the PATH caveat exists only in the installer's terminal output, not on the website
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** Step 2 — running the binary after a website-driven install

They have no breadcrumb connecting that to the install location, and the step that would explain it scrolled off-screen during the pipe-install.

(1) The finder cites InstallWidget at "InstallWidget.svelte:93"; the file actually lives at prototype/src/components/InstallWidget.svelte (not src/lib/), and the "Installs to ~/.local/bin" text is at line 93 there — content correct, path label wrong. (2) The finder undersells an in-step partial mitigation: App.svelte:922, the very next line in the same step 02, already shows the full path `sudo setcap cap_sys_ptrace=eip ~/.local/bin/wfm-fetch-inventory`, so an observant user has a breadcrumb to the install location within the same step — the inconsistency the finder flags (bare at 918, full-path at 922) is real and is itself the strongest part of the case, but it also means the user isn't entirely without a clue. The core claim holds: App.svelte:918 shows a bare `wfm-fetch-inventory`, install.sh:14 installs to ~/.local/bin, the PATH warning lives only in installer stdout (install.sh:92-99), and neither the website stepper nor InstallWidget (line 93) repeats it. On Arch (a first-class target and the explicit Linux wedge) and on any setup where ~/.local/bin wasn't on PATH at login, the bare command fails with command-not-found.

#### [🟡 minor] DropZone primary hint sends the user to the WRONG directory for inventory.json
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — new user looks for the file they just generated to drop into the app

Every other surface says Downloads, so the dropzone is the single contradicting voice — and it's the loudest one in context.

And "next to itself" is concretely wrong: install.sh:14 installs to ~/.local/bin, so it points the user at a directory with no inventory.json. main.rs:6, install.sh:111, App.svelte:920, and App.svelte:1523 all correctly say Downloads. But two of those correct surfaces (App.svelte:920 "Writes inventory.json to your Downloads folder", and the FAQ at App.svelte:1523) live in the same web app the user is already in, so the contradiction is partly self-correcting and the file lands in a reflex-checked OS folder. This is misleading copy causing recoverable seconds-of-confusion, not a broken action path — minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] DropZone 'saves it next to itself' points Windows users to %LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv, but fetch writes to Downloads — the misdirection is worse on Windows where that folder is hidden
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6: finding inventory.json to drop into the web app

One nit: the cited path is wrong — the file is prototype/src/components/DropZone.svelte, not src/lib/components/. The impact is bounded: fetch already prints the absolute output path prominently on every run (main.rs:206-211: "Wrote <full path> (N bytes)\nDrop that file into the web UI..."), which the finder itself notes. A user who just ran the command sees exactly where the file went in their terminal, on BOTH platforms (Windows iwr|iex installs run in a terminal too). The dropzone hint is also secondary copy under "Don't have one yet?" — aspirational guidance for users who have NOT yet run the tool, not the pointer a stuck user relies on. The "sent hunting in a hidden directory" scenario requires ignoring the terminal output that names the real path. Real consistency bug worth fixing, but it's confusing copy, not a blocker.

#### [🟡 minor] 'Warframe not running' / 'not past login' guidance is correct in the CLI but never reaches a user who runs serve before fetch, or skips the login step

But these are eprintln/anyhow strings only visible to someone watching the terminal. - **Why it's friction:** A user who installs via the web app's copy-paste widget and runs fetch without opening a trade screen hits the 'No accountId/nonce pair found' path. The message is good if they read the terminal, but the in-app onboarding never warns them, so it reads as a tool failure rather than a missing prerequisite.

Also, the no-creds path is not guaranteed for a web-first user: by the time someone is loaded past login and playing, network calls have usually already fired and the accountId/nonce is often already resident in memory, so opening a trade/profile screen is a reliability booster rather than an always-required step. That lowers the population who actually hit "No accountId/nonce pair found" below what the why_friction implies. Severity minor is correct.

The dominant outcome is copy inconsistency / mild confusion, not a user stranded in ~/.local/bin. #### [🟡 minor] Windows OpenProcess failure text omits the dominant real cause (integrity-level/elevation mismatch) and there is no SmartScreen 'Run anyway' or Unblock-File guidance for the manual-download route
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** step 4: first fetch run on Windows
- **Evidence:** companion/src/main.rs:1837 — OpenProcess error reads 'OpenProcess failed — not running as same user, or pid is wrong'. The most common Windows ERROR_ACCESS_DENIED here is an integrity-level mismatch: Steam launches Warframe non-elevated while the user (following generic 'run as admin' advice) opens an elevated PowerShell, so a medium-IL game process can't be opened from a high-IL caller cleanly, and vice versa. The message names neither elevation nor integrity level. Separately, the manual-download .exe (InstallWidget.svelte:109-111) carries Mark-of-the-Web; nothing in install.ps1, SECURITY.md, or companion/README.md mentions Unblock-File or SmartScreen's hidden 'More info -> Run anyway'.
- **Why it's friction:** When fetch fails on Windows the binary's own diagnostic points the user at the wrong fixes ('same user' and 'pid'), while the actual remedy is to match elevation between game and terminal (usually: run BOTH non-elevated). Combined with install.ps1 line 92 already nudging users toward an elevated terminal on Access denied, a stuck user will escalate privileges and make the mismatch worse. The manually downloaded exe additionally needs an Unblock-File / 'Run anyway' the docs never give.
- **Suggested fix:** Reword the OpenProcess error to lead with elevation: 'Access denied opening the game process. Run this terminal at the SAME elevation as Warframe — if you launched the game normally via Steam, use a normal (non-admin) PowerShell.' Add an Unblock-File/'Run anyway' note to the manual-download section of the widget and SECURITY.md's verify-a-release block.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence verified and holds. companion/src/main.rs:1837 reads exactly "OpenProcess failed — not running as same user, or pid is wrong" — names "same user" and "pid", not elevation or integrity level. The integrity-level/elevation mismatch is a genuine ERROR_ACCESS_DENIED cause for OpenProcess with PROCESS_VM_READ, and notably the repo's own prototype/public/install.ps1:91-92 actively steers a stuck user the wrong way ("If you see 'Access is denied', try an elevated terminal."), which can CREATE the mismatch — a real self-inflicted contradiction. SmartScreen/MOTW half also confirmed: the manual-download block (components/InstallWidget.svelte:105-120, finder cited stale path src/lib/InstallWidget.svelte and line 109-111 — the file actually lives at prototype/src/components/InstallWidget.svelte) and SECURITY.md's "How to verify a release" block (line 70, with Get-FileHash for the Windows .exe) give no Unblock-File / SmartScreen "Run anyway" guidance; companion/README.md and install.ps1 likewise omit it. Two corrections to the finder's framing: (1) integrity-level mismatch is NOT the "dominant" cause — a new user on the happy path (Steam non-elevated + install.ps1's "No admin needed" non-elevated install) has matched integrity and fetch SUCCEEDS; the mismatch only bites after a user deviates or follows install.ps1's bad elevated-terminal nudge, i.e. a secondary/stuck-user path. (2) The manual-download route is the minority path (the advertised route is the piped install.ps1), so the SmartScreen gap doesn't block the typical Windows user. Downgrading major -> minor: real, well-evidenced friction on deviation/minority paths, but not a blocker for the primary new-Windows-user journey.

#### [🟡 minor] The 'run a single fetch with sudo' fallback uses a bare command name that sudo's secure_path strips
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** setcap / first fetch (the no-setcap fallback path)
- **Evidence:** prototype/public/install.sh:110 prints `sudo $BIN_NAME` (bare `wfm-fetch-inventory`); the binary installs to `$HOME/.local/bin` (install.sh:14). install.sh:108 immediately above runs the SAME bare name successfully *without* sudo, so the user has just proven to themselves it is 'on PATH'.
- **Why it's friction:** sudo ships `Defaults secure_path` (a fixed `/usr/...:/bin` list that excludes `~/.local/bin`) on Debian/Ubuntu/Fedora and the stock Arch/CachyOS /etc/sudoers. So `sudo wfm-fetch-inventory` fails with `sudo: wfm-fetch-inventory: command not found` even though the non-sudo line two lines up worked. A new user who chose the sudo path (explicitly 'rather not' grant setcap) hits a flat contradiction: the tool says it is installed and runnable, sudo says it does not exist. The ptrace runtime error (main.rs:1801-1802) avoids this by emitting a full path via current_exe(), so the installer's guidance is strictly worse than the binary's own.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the sudo fallback an absolute path: `sudo "$DEST/$BIN_NAME"` (mirrors the setcap line on 107). Apply the same fix in App.svelte/InstallWidget wherever a `sudo wfm-fetch-inventory` form could appear.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is fully accurate and verified: install.sh:14 installs to ~/.local/bin, :108 runs the bare name (no sudo), :110 prints `sudo $BIN_NAME` (bare), while :107 directly above uses the absolute `"$DEST/$BIN_NAME"` — and main.rs:1792-1802 emits an absolute `sudo {bin}` via current_exe(), so the installer's line 110 is indeed strictly worse than the binary's own guidance. sudo's secure_path default (Debian/Ubuntu/Fedora + stock Arch/CachyOS) excludes ~/.local/bin, so `sudo wfm-fetch-inventory` will fail with "command not found". The finder OVERSTATES severity at major on two counts. (1) The "flat contradiction" (line 108 works, line 110 fails) only fully holds when ~/.local/bin is already on the user's interactive PATH; for a fresh install where it is NOT, install.sh:96-98 already prints a PATH warning and the bare line 108 would ALSO fail — so the most jarring framing applies to a narrower subset than implied. (2) This is the explicitly secondary, non-recommended branch ("Rather not?"); the script leads with setcap, which is correct. The finder's claim that the same form "could appear" in App.svelte/InstallWidget is unsupported: App.svelte:922 and InstallWidget.svelte:95 use the absolute ~/.local/bin path for setcap and present NO bare `sudo wfm-fetch-inventory` fallback at all, so the bug is confined to install.sh:110. Real, reproducible, trivially fixable (mirror :107 → `sudo "$DEST/$BIN_NAME"`), but minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] Zero guidance for Steam Proton / Flatpak Steam — the dominant way Linux players run Warframe
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** first fetch (locating + reading the game process)
- **Evidence:** grep for proton|steam|wine|flatpak|lutris|bottles across companion/, prototype/src, prototype/public, SECURITY.md returns nothing. find_wf_pid (main.rs:215-242) matches the Wine process name `Warframe.x64.exe`, which works for native-Steam/Lutris, but there is no doc acknowledging the launch method at all.
- **Why it's friction:** Almost every Linux Warframe install is Steam Proton (or Lutris/Bottles/Heroic). Flatpak Steam in particular runs the game inside a bwrap sandbox with its own PID namespace, so a host-installed companion either cannot see the game's `/proc/<pid>/mem` or sees a PID it cannot attach to even with CAP_SYS_PTRACE — surfacing as the generic 'Warframe doesn't appear to be running' (main.rs:128) or a permission-denied that the setcap advice won't fix. The product positions itself as the equal-first-class Linux alternative to a Windows-only tool, yet the single most common Linux runtime is undocumented, leaving the affected user with no breadcrumb that the sandbox is the cause.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a short 'Running Warframe via Steam/Proton/Flatpak' note to companion/CLAUDE.md and the install.sh next-steps: native Steam/Lutris work as-is; Flatpak Steam needs the companion run inside the sandbox (`flatpak run --command=... com.valvesoftware.Steam`) or a host-Steam install. Detect the bwrap/Flatpak case in find_wf_pid's not-found message and name it.
- **Verifier note:** Doc gap is real but mechanism and severity overstated. No user-facing launch-method note exists (grep across companion/, prototype/src, prototype/public, SECURITY.md is clean; only an internal comment at main.rs:233). matches_warframe (main.rs:226-242) handles native Steam/Proton/Lutris/Wine via name prefix and exe path, so the dominant Steam+Proton runtime works as-is. The finder's core mechanism is wrong: Flatpak does not unshare the PID namespace by default and com.valvesoftware.Steam does not unshare PIDs, so a CAP_SYS_PTRACE host binary can generally read the game's /proc/<pid>/mem under Flatpak Steam too; the asserted cannot-see-PID catastrophe is unsupported. Existing errors (ptrace setcap path main.rs:1796-1804, ptrace_scope=3 main.rs:1810-1813, not-running main.rs:128-129) already cover realistic Steam/Proton failures. Minor docs polish, not a major first-fetch blocker. Downgrade major to minor.</correction>
</invoke>


#### [🟡 minor] find_wf_pid picks an arbitrary process from a HashMap when several match, and no --pid hint is surfaced anywhere
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** first fetch (auto-detecting the PID)
- **Evidence:** find_wf_pid (main.rs:215-224) iterates `sys.processes()` — a `&HashMap`, so iteration order is unspecified — and returns the FIRST match. matches_warframe (main.rs:226-242) matches both `Warframe.x64*` and any exe path containing `Warframe.x64.exe`. The `--pid` override exists (FetchArgs, main.rs:61-62) but is never mentioned in install.sh, InstallWidget, App.svelte, or any FAQ.
- **Why it's friction:** Proton/Steam often have more than one process whose exe path contains `Warframe.x64.exe` (the game plus a launcher/helper, or a stale zombie from a prior crash). Because the match comes from unordered HashMap iteration, the companion can non-deterministically scan the wrong process — yielding 'No accountId/nonce pair found' (main.rs:1676) on one run and success on the next, with no explanation. The escape hatch (`--pid`) that a stuck user needs is documented nowhere a newcomer can see.
- **Suggested fix:** Collect all matches, prefer the one with a readable /proc/<pid>/mem and the largest RSS (the real game, not a helper), and on a no-creds failure list the candidate PIDs with the `--pid N` hint. Surface `--pid` in the not-running/no-creds error text.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code facts are all accurate (find_wf_pid main.rs:215-224 returns the first match from an unordered HashMap; matches_warframe main.rs:226-242 matches name prefix OR exe-path-contains "Warframe.x64.exe"; --pid exists at main.rs:61-62 and is surfaced in no user-facing doc/script/UI, only in clap --help). But the finder OVERSTATES the impact in two ways. (1) The "non-deterministic, works on one run / fails on the next" framing is the weak part: under Steam/Proton the DX launcher (Warframe.exe) normally exits once Warframe.x64.exe spawns, so at fetch time (game running, past login) there is typically exactly ONE match. Even when a second matching process exists, scanning the non-game process yields a CONSISTENT "No accountId/nonce pair found" — not flaky alternation. True alternation requires two persistent live matching processes AND the HashMap order to flip between runs, which is an edge-of-an-edge, not "often" as claimed. (2) The real, narrow friction is: a user who does hit a multi-match case (a lingering launcher or a stale/zombie instance still in the process table) gets a no-creds error with no hint that --pid exists or which PIDs are candidates. That is genuine but low-frequency. Severity minor is acceptable but on the generous side given the overstated determinism story — the realistic impact is closer to polish/low-minor.
