#### [🟡 minor] In-app step 02 omits the "open the trade/profile screen to force an auth call" prerequisite that every other surface states, so a website-first newcomer's first fetch likely fails with "No accountId/nonce pair found"
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 4 (first fetch) — but the failure is seeded at the on-page onboarding stepper a website-first user reads instead of the terminal next-steps
- **Evidence:** prototype/src/App.svelte:917 step 02 says only "With Warframe past the login screen, run:" then `wfm-fetch-inventory`. Every OTHER surface adds the credential prerequisite: prototype/public/install.sh:105 and install.ps1:88 ("Open the trade or profile screen once (forces an auth call)."), companion/README.md:12-13, and the CLI's own failure text companion/src/main.rs:1677-1679 ("Make sure you're past the login screen and a recent network call has fired (opening the trade or profile screen is reliable)."). Past the login screen alone does NOT guarantee accountId/nonce are resident in memory.
- **Why it's friction:** A newcomer who discovered the tool via the website follows the on-page 01/02/03 stepper, not the installer's terminal output (which scrolls away) or the README. The on-page path is the ONE surface that drops the auth-call prerequisite. They launch the game, sit at the main menu, run the command, and hit a raw bail "No accountId/nonce pair found" on their very first action — the exact moment a cold-start user decides whether the tool works. The fix the CLI error suggests is the prerequisite that step 02 should have stated up front.
- **Suggested fix:** Add the one-line prerequisite to App.svelte step 02 to match the other four surfaces: "With Warframe past the login screen, open the trade or profile screen once (this fires the auth call we read), then run:". Keep the wording identical to install.sh/README so the surfaces don't drift again.
- **Verifier note:** Severity overstated as major; the CLI bail at main.rs:1677-1679 prints the exact fix at failure time, enabling fast self-recovery, so this is a papercut not a dead-end. Rest of claim accurate.

#### [🟡 minor] matches_warframe() matches bare "Warframe.exe" — on Windows that's the DE launcher, which holds no session creds
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 4 (fetch) — auto-detecting the game PID on Windows
- **Evidence:** companion/src/main.rs:230 `if name.starts_with("Warframe.x64") || name == "Warframe.exe"` and main.rs:237 `s.ends_with("/Warframe.exe")`. On Windows the actual game is `Warframe.x64.exe`; `Warframe.exe` is DE's updater/launcher (`<Steam>/steamapps/common/Warframe/Tools/Launcher.exe` is one form, but the bootstrap `Warframe.exe` is the other). find_wf_pid (main.rs:218) returns the first HashMap match in arbitrary order.
- **Why it's friction:** If the launcher is still resident (it commonly is — it stays open to relaunch the game) and HashMap iteration hits it first, the scan runs against a process that never had accountId/nonce in memory. The user gets a zero-credential scan or 'Inventory endpoint not happy' with no hint that the wrong process was picked. The Linux comm-truncation comment (main.rs:227) explains why the prefix match exists but doesn't acknowledge that on Windows the exact `Warframe.exe` arm can grab the launcher.
- **Suggested fix:** On Windows prefer `Warframe.x64.exe` and only fall back to `Warframe.exe` if no x64 match exists; or when multiple candidates match, pick the one with the largest working set / most committed memory (the running game dwarfs the launcher). At minimum, when several Warframe-named PIDs exist, log which one was chosen and how to override with --pid.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code is accurate (main.rs:230 the OR with `name == "Warframe.exe"`, main.rs:237 `s.ends_with("/Warframe.exe")`, and find_wf_pid at main.rs:218-222 returning the first HashMap match in non-deterministic order). But the finder over-rates this as "major" and overstates the impact on two counts:

1. Contestable premise. The load-bearing claim — that a creds-less `Warframe.exe` is commonly co-resident with the running game on Windows — is asserted, not evidenced, and is shaky. The 32-bit `Warframe.exe` game client was retired years ago; the modern resident updater/relauncher is itself `Warframe.x64.exe`, which the `starts_with("Warframe.x64")` arm already catches. DE's bootstrap shim that may be named `Warframe.exe` is a download-then-handoff process that typically EXITS once `Warframe.x64.exe` launches, so it is usually NOT resident during a fetch. In the overwhelmingly common case only `Warframe.x64.exe` is alive and is matched correctly. The wrong-process race therefore fires only in an uncommon configuration.

2. "No hint which process was picked" is wrong. main.rs:134 prints `PID {pid} — scanning Warframe memory...` before the scan, so the chosen PID IS surfaced. And a `--pid` override already exists (FetchArgs.pid, main.rs:60-62, `--pid`) and appears in --help as "Override the auto-detected Warframe PID." Part of the finder's own suggested_fix ("at minimum log which one was chosen and how to override with --pid") is already satisfied: the PID is logged and the override flag exists.

What does land: if the wrong (creds-less) process is ever picked, the resulting error at main.rs:1676 — "No accountId/nonce pair found in WF memory. Make sure you're past the login screen..." — misdirects the user toward a login problem rather than a wrong-PID problem, and there is no Windows-specific preference for `Warframe.x64.exe` over the bare `Warframe.exe` arm. That is a genuine, if narrow, papercut. Real but minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] On Windows, fetch's CWD fallback when Downloads is absent drops inventory.json into a fresh shell's start dir (profile root or System32)
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 4 (fetch) — output path fallback
- **Evidence:** default_out_path (main.rs:244-253): if `downloads.is_dir()` is false it falls back to `std::env::current_dir()`. On Windows a freshly opened PowerShell starts in %USERPROFILE% (or System32 for an elevated cmd), and real_user_home() always returns None on Windows (main.rs:275-277) so `home` comes from `directories::UserDirs` — if that fails too, home is `.`.
- **Why it's friction:** A Windows user whose Downloads was redirected to OneDrive (extremely common — OneDrive moves the Downloads known-folder) may fail the plain `home.join("Downloads").is_dir()` check if directories resolves the non-redirected path, and the file then lands silently in the profile root or, for an elevated terminal, System32 — with no in-binary message distinguishing the fallback from the happy path. The success line just prints wherever it landed.
- **Suggested fix:** On Windows resolve Downloads via the SHGetKnownFolderPath(FOLDERID_Downloads) known-folder API (which honors OneDrive redirection) rather than assuming %USERPROFILE%\Downloads; and when falling back to CWD, emit a distinct 'Downloads folder not found — wrote next to the current directory: <path>' note instead of a bare path.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code is all accurate: default_out_path (main.rs:244-253) does home.join("Downloads") and falls back to current_dir() then ".", real_user_home() is None on Windows (275-277), dirs_home() uses directories::UserDirs (279-283), and the code never calls UserDirs::download_dir() (which would honor OneDrive redirection) — it manually assembles %USERPROFILE%\Downloads. So the OneDrive-redirect-then-fall-back-to-CWD path is genuinely reachable. But the finder overstates the harm: the success line at main.rs:206-208 prints the FULL absolute out_path on every run (`Wrote {path} ({bytes})`), so the file does NOT land "silently" — the user is always told exactly where it went; what's missing is only a *distinct* 'fell back to CWD' callout, not the path itself, so "no in-binary message" / "lands silently in the profile root or System32" is misleading. The System32/elevated-cmd angle is effectively moot too: Windows fetch needs no elevation (companion/CLAUDE.md: "No elevation needed if running as the user that launched WF"), so an elevated terminal isn't part of the normal journey. A --out override exists (main.rs:64-66) as an escape hatch.

#### [🟡 minor] No success checkpoint between fetch and the dropzone: nothing tells the user fetch worked except CLI stderr they may not read, and the in-app step never reflects fetch state
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 4→6 — after running fetch, before dropping the file
- **Evidence:** fetch confirmation lives only in companion stderr (main.rs:206-211 'Wrote ... / Drop that file into the web UI'). The web app step 02 'Run it once' (App.svelte:916-924) is static text that never changes based on whether a file now exists; the only state the app tracks is whether inventory has been *dropped* (phase idle/loading, App.svelte:900). There is no 'did it work?' affordance bridging CLI output and the dropzone.
- **Why it's friction:** A first-time CLI user often doesn't parse multi-line stderr — they see the prompt return and tab back to the browser. The browser still shows the same idle stepper, giving zero feedback that step 02 succeeded or failed. The user is left guessing whether to look in Downloads, re-run, or check for an error, and there's no single place that says 'fetch writes one success line; if you saw it, your file is in Downloads — drag it here.' The handoff between the two tools has no shared status.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a one-line 'How do I know it worked? Look for "Wrote .../Downloads/inventory.json" in the terminal' note under step 02, mirroring the exact success string the binary prints.
- **Verifier note:** Cited evidence is accurate (main.rs:206-211 stderr-only confirmation; App.svelte:916-924 static step 02; DropZone/App phases never reflect filesystem state). But the why_friction overstates one point: it implies there's no in-app pointer to where the file lands. There is — step 02 itself says "Writes inventory.json to your Downloads folder" (App.svelte:920), the DropZone hint says the companion "saves it next to itself" (DropZone.svelte:61-66), and the FAQ says it writes to ~/Downloads (App.svelte:1522-1523). So the "user is left guessing whether to look in Downloads" half is softened by existing text. The accurate core remains: there is no state-reflecting "did it work?" checkpoint that changes based on whether fetch ran — the stepper is static until a file is dropped.

#### [⚪ polish] Default fetch writes to ~/Downloads but falls back to CWD silently when ~/Downloads is absent
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** fetch -> locate inventory.json -> drop into web UI
- **Evidence:** default_out_path() (main.rs:244-253): if ~/Downloads is not a directory it writes inventory.json into std::env::current_dir() with no notice that the documented path (everywhere: install.sh:111, README:35, the app copy) was not used. Many minimal Linux setups (server installs, custom XDG layouts, fresh user homes) have no ~/Downloads.
- **Why it's friction:** Every piece of onboarding copy promises ~/Downloads. A user without that folder gets the file dropped wherever they happened to run the command, then hunts in ~/Downloads (per the docs) and finds nothing. The final-line 'Wrote <path>' message (main.rs:206-209) is the only cue, and it scrolls past the more prominent 'Drop that file into the web UI' line.
- **Suggested fix:** Either create ~/Downloads when missing (it's a standard XDG dir) or, when falling back to CWD, print a distinct warning ('~/Downloads not found — wrote to the current directory instead') so the docs' promise and reality stay reconciled.
- **Verifier note:** Code evidence is accurate (default_out_path falls back to CWD silently, main.rs:244-253; docs over-promise ~/Downloads at install.sh:111 and companion/README.md:6/35/77). But the friction is overstated on two counts. (1) Output ORDER is reversed from the claim: "Wrote {absolute path}" prints FIRST (main.rs:206-209), then "Drop that file into the web UI" (main.rs:211) — these are the last two lines of output, so the real path is NOT buried above a more-prominent line; it is right there, fresh in the terminal. The user only fails if they ignore the printed path and trust the docs instead. (2) The affected population is small: this tool memory-scans a RUNNING Warframe game, so the user is on a gaming desktop with a full DE where xdg-user-dirs creates ~/Downloads near-universally. "Server installs / minimal homes" cited as the at-risk group do not run Warframe. So this is a marginal real issue, not a minor one.

#### [⚪ polish] No mention that Windows Controlled Folder Access can block fetch writing inventory.json to Downloads
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 4: fetch writing the output file on Windows
- **Evidence:** main.rs:201 write_restricted falls back to a plain fs::write on non-unix (main.rs:583-587) into <Downloads>/inventory.json. No Windows-specific handling or doc note for Controlled Folder Access, which (when enabled, common on security-conscious setups) blocks non-allowlisted processes from writing to Downloads/Documents.
- **Why it's friction:** On a machine with Defender's Controlled Folder Access on, the fetch write to Downloads fails with a permission error from an unsigned binary the user already half-distrusts (see SmartScreen finding). The error surfaces as a generic 'writing inventory to ...' context with no hint about CFA, so the user can't self-diagnose.
- **Suggested fix:** Catch the write-permission failure on Windows and add a hint ('Windows Controlled Folder Access may be blocking writes to Downloads — allow this app or use --out to a different folder'). Document --out as the escape hatch.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate: main.rs:201-203 writes inventory.json with the generic context "writing inventory to {path}", main.rs:583-587 is a plain fs::write fallback on non-unix, the default target is Downloads, and there is no CFA/Defender note nor any documentation of --out as an escape hatch anywhere (grep of *.md/*.sh/*.ps1/*.rs found no "controlled folder", "defender", "smartscreen", or user-facing --out for fetch). The --out arg does exist (main.rs:66, :81). However the finder overstates impact: Controlled Folder Access is OFF by default on Windows — it is an opt-in Defender feature, so "common on security-conscious setups" is the finder's own admission that this is a narrow edge, not a typical new-user path. The blocked write is also not silent: fs::write returns a permission error that surfaces WITH the full path ("writing inventory to <Downloads>/inventory.json"), and a user who deliberately enabled CFA is positioned to self-diagnose a Downloads-permission failure. Severity should be polish, not minor — it is a doc nicety for a non-default-feature corner case affecting a small intersection of users (CFA-on AND willing to run an unsigned memory-scan binary), not something that blocks or meaningfully annoys a normal first-run.

#### [⚪ polish] The 'no setcap needed on Windows' asymmetry is implied but never positively stated, so Windows users hunting for a permission step have nothing to confirm they can skip it
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** step 2->4: reconciling install instructions against the in-app stepper
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:921-923 states the ptrace/setcap step as a Linux requirement and says 'Windows: no admin needed', but the prominent install.ps1 next-step (line 91-92) immediately hedges with 'If you see "Access is denied", try an elevated terminal', and companion/README.md:28-33 frames Windows as 'no elevation required IF running as the same user'. A Windows reader sees a setcap line dominating the Linux path and conditional admin caveats on theirs, with no single clear 'Windows needs no permission grant at all — just run it as the same user' statement.
- **Why it's friction:** Permission setup is the scariest part of this onboarding (memory scanning sounds invasive). Linux gets an explicit one-time grant; Windows gets only negations and an 'if it fails, elevate' caveat that contradicts the no-admin claim. A cautious Windows user is left unsure whether they missed a step, and the conflicting 'try elevated' advice undermines the otherwise-correct 'no admin' message.
- **Suggested fix:** State the Windows path positively and once: 'Windows needs no permission grant and no admin — just run it from a normal PowerShell as the same Windows user that launched Warframe.' Remove or strongly qualify the 'try an elevated terminal' suggestion so it does not contradict that, given elevation usually breaks OpenProcess rather than fixing it.
- **Verifier note:** All three citations are accurate, but the finder overstates the impact and partly misreads install.ps1. The claim's thesis — Windows users have "nothing to confirm they can skip" a permission step — is too strong: install.ps1:91 DOES give a positive, actionable Windows instruction at exactly the right moment ("run as the same user that's running Warframe"), and it is the very next step shown to anyone who runs the Windows installer. So a Windows user is not left in a vacuum; they get a working positive instruction. The genuine defect is narrower and purely cosmetic: (a) App.svelte:921 phrases the Windows path as a negation ("no admin needed") rather than positively, and (b) install.ps1:92's "if you see Access is denied, try an elevated terminal" mildly contradicts "no admin needed" and is in fact bad advice — companion/CLAUDE.md confirms Windows needs the SAME user (not elevation), and running elevated changes the user/integrity context and can break OpenProcess rather than fix it. That contradictory hint is the only real wart. Severity is polish, not minor: nothing blocks or meaningfully annoys a real Windows user, who runs install.ps1, reads the positive next-step, runs the command, and it works. This is a doc-tone/consistency nit, and the most defensible concrete fix is dropping or strongly qualifying the "try an elevated terminal" line.

#### [⚪ polish] Every Windows-facing data-location string says the unix path "~/Downloads", which doesn't exist on Windows
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 4→6 — user hunts for the written inventory.json on Windows
- **Evidence:** default_out_path resolves the REAL Downloads via `home.join("Downloads")` (main.rs:246) so the file lands correctly at e.g. C:\Users\me\Downloads. But the in-app pointer App.svelte:1523 says 'to your <code>~/Downloads</code>' and SECURITY-adjacent FAQ copy reuses the same `~/Downloads`. install.ps1:93 ('your Downloads folder') is correct; the app contradicts it.
- **Why it's friction:** A Windows user reading '~/Downloads' sees a literal path with a tilde that doesn't resolve in Explorer or PowerShell, making them think the tool wrote somewhere unusual or failed. The one place that correctly says 'Downloads folder' (the installer) scrolls off before they reach the dropzone, so the app's wrong unix path is what they're staring at when stuck.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the in-app/FAQ copy OS-aware (the InstallWidget already detects OS): show 'your Downloads folder' generically, or '%USERPROFILE%\Downloads' for detected Windows and '~/Downloads' for Linux. Don't print a unix tilde to a Windows visitor.
- **Verifier note:** The cited file:line facts are individually true (main.rs:246 resolves the real Windows Downloads; App.svelte:1523 literally contains `~/Downloads`; install.ps1:93 correctly says "Downloads folder"), but the finding's central framing is wrong. It claims "EVERY Windows-facing data-location string says ~/Downloads" and that the app's only Downloads pointer is the wrong tilde'd one. False: the PRIMARY in-app onboarding pointer is App.svelte:920 — "Writes inventory.json to your Downloads folder" — which is OS-generic and correct, and it sits inside numbered onboarding step 02, directly above the dropzone (step 03 "Drop it below"). That is the copy a stuck Windows user actually reads. The only `~/Downloads` in the whole app is App.svelte:1523, which lives inside a collapsed-by-default <details> FAQ ("Where does my inventory data actually go?", no `open` attribute, confirmed) that is a data-PRIVACY blurb, not a file-location pointer, and requires a click to even see. The finding's why_friction ("the one place that correctly says 'Downloads folder' is the installer, which scrolls off, so the app's wrong path is what they're staring at") is therefore incorrect — the app's own correct generic pointer is right next to the dropzone. Net: a genuine but cosmetic unix-ism in one hidden privacy FAQ line, not the data-location pointer users rely on.

### `companion-login` (6)

#### [🔴 major] The entire login -> serve -> list-on-WFM half of the product has zero onboarding from the install path
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** after fetch: login -> serve (the 'actually sell' differentiator)
- **Evidence:** install.sh 'Next steps' (lines 101-115) ends at 'inventory.json lands in ~/Downloads — drop it into the web UI' and never mentions login, serve, or the passphrase. InstallWidget.svelte mentions only download + setcap (lines 91-103); grep for 'serve|login|passphrase' in it returns nothing. companion/README.md documents only fetch (login/serve absent). A new user reaches a read-only sell list and is given no path to the listing feature that makes TennoWorth 'measurably better at what to sell right now' than browse.wf/warframe.me.
- **Why it's friction:** The product's whole justification over warframe.me/browse.wf is acting on the sell list (bulk-listing via the companion). The first-run journey documented to the user stops one step short of that capability. The companion-connect UI then assumes the user already has a serve URL in hand, with no breadcrumb back to how to get one.
- **Suggested fix:** Extend install.sh 'Next steps' and the InstallWidget to a second stanza: 'To list items on warframe.market from the app: wfm-fetch-inventory login (one time), then wfm-fetch-inventory serve, paste the printed URL into the Companion tab.' Add login + serve sections to companion/README.md.
- **Verifier note:** The finder slightly overstates "zero onboarding" and "no breadcrumb back." There IS one thin breadcrumb the finder missed: the in-app Companion view (prototype/src/App.svelte:1462-1466) tells the user to "paste the URL the `serve` subcommand printed" and shows a `http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…` placeholder. So `serve` is named in exactly one place. However this does not refute the claim's substance: that breadcrumb (a) only appears if the user navigates to the Companion tab, which nothing in the install path or hero steps 01-03 points them to; (b) never mentions `login` is a prerequisite of `serve`; (c) never mentions the passphrase; (d) gives no command to type. The three cited install-path artifacts check out exactly: install.sh "Next steps" (lines 101-115) ends at "drop it into the web UI" with no login/serve/passphrase; InstallWidget.svelte (lines 91-103) covers only download+setcap (grep for serve/login/passphrase is empty); companion/README.md documents only the one-shot fetch (login and serve are entirely absent from its Run / "What it does" sections). The hero onboarding (App.svelte:905-937, steps 01 get companion / 02 run fetch / 03 drop file) confirms the documented first-run journey stops at the read-only list. There is no root README at all. Net: the listing half of the product has effectively no install-path onboarding; the lone in-app `serve` mention is incomplete and unreachable from the documented flow.

#### [🔴 major] login hard-defaults --platform pc and never reconciles it with the platform the fetch path auto-detects; console players silently authenticate against the wrong WFM market
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** step 3 (login) → step 5 (serve), order management half of the journey
- **Evidence:** companion/src/main.rs:84 (`#[arg(long, default_value = "pc")] platform`), :480 (`encrypt_jwt(&jwt, &passphrase, &args.platform)` bakes pc into the JWT blob), :745 (`let platform = blob.platform.clone()`), and every serve WFM call reuses it: :1114/:1221/:1256/:1591 (`.header("Platform", &state.platform)`). Meanwhile the fetch path auto-detects platform from memory: :147 (`args.platform_tag.unwrap_or_else(|| info.ct.clone())`) with ct = STM/ME/NS/etc. The two paths never cross-check.
- **Why it's friction:** A new player on Switch/PS/Xbox runs `wfm-fetch-inventory login` (the documented invocation has no flags), gets pc baked in, and from then on /v2/me, /v2/orders/user, and POST /v2/order all target the pc platform. The fetch subcommand already solved platform detection from game memory; the login path silently ignores that solved problem and defaults to pc instead of reusing the detected ct. Listings either land on the wrong platform's market or fail in confusing ways well after onboarding, with no error at login time.
- **Suggested fix:** Default login's platform from the same memory-scanned ct the fetch path uses (map STM/ME→pc, NS→switch, etc.), or at minimum prompt/confirm platform at login and warn when blob.platform disagrees with the ct seen during the most recent fetch. Surface the active platform prominently in the serve startup banner, not just buried in /health.
- **Verifier note:** One nuance the finder understates: the fetch path's `ct` (STM/ME/NS — companion/src/main.rs:147, companion/CLAUDE.md WFM-quirks) is DE's platform code, which is NOT the same vocabulary as WFM's `Platform` header (pc/ps4/xbox/switch). So login can't simply "reuse the detected ct" verbatim — a mapping is required (the finder's suggested_fix acknowledges this with STM/ME→pc, NS→switch, so the fix is sound, but the body's framing that login "ignores the solved problem" overstates how directly reusable ct is). Also worth noting the blast radius is bounded to console/Switch players on the order-management (serve) half only; inventory display via fetch is unaffected because it uses the scanned ct independently, and PC dominates WFM trading. Severity major is correct: it silently authenticates/lists a real user subset against the wrong market with zero signal at login time.

#### [🟡 minor] Cloudflare 1015 / bot-block during login is only partially diagnosed; signin-time 1015 prints a raw HTTP body
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 3 — `wfm-fetch-inventory login`
- **Evidence:** The bootstrap GET has a Cloudflare-aware context ('bootstrap GET failed (Cloudflare may have blocked us)', main.rs:393) and a status check (main.rs:394-398). But the signin POST failure path just dumps 'Signin failed: HTTP {status}\nResponse body:\n{first 400 chars}' (main.rs:440-443) — a 1015 or JS-challenge HTML page renders as a wall of markup. The catalog fetch in serve similarly bails '/v2/items returned HTTP {}' (main.rs:1327) with no 1015 hint.
- **Why it's friction:** WFM's Cloudflare 1015 from a residential IP is a real, known failure (scripts/CLAUDE.md, wfm_demand.py:371-374). When it hits at signin or catalog load, the user gets raw HTML or a bare status with no 'you're rate-limited, wait and retry' framing, even though the codebase clearly understands this failure mode elsewhere.
- **Suggested fix:** Detect status 429/403 and 'error code: 1015' / cloudflare markers in the body and emit 'warframe.market is rate-limiting this IP (Cloudflare 1015) — wait a few minutes and retry' at both the signin and /v2/items call sites.
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is all accurate (main.rs:393-398 bootstrap has Cloudflare context; main.rs:438-444 signin dumps raw body with no 1015 framing; main.rs:1326-1327 catalog bails with bare HTTP status). But the finder overstates real impact in two ways. (1) The same client that does the signin POST and the catalog fetch sends BROWSER_UA (main.rs:30, 384), and the comment at main.rs:28-29 states the browser UA is precisely what avoids 1015. So a 1015 at signin/catalog requires the residential IP itself to be flagged DESPITE a valid browser UA — a low-probability one-time-login edge, not a routine failure. (2) The login flow's FIRST network call is the bootstrap GET, which already carries the Cloudflare-aware message (main.rs:393, 396) — that is the most likely spot a fresh user hits 1015. The signin POST and /v2/items run second/third on the same client and cookie jar; if bootstrap succeeded they are much less likely to 1015. So the diagnosis gap is real but narrow: it is a cosmetic error-message-quality inconsistency on lower-probability paths, the worst case being a readable-but-unframed Cloudflare HTML body (which still contains 'error code: 1015' text) at signin and a bare 'HTTP 429' at catalog. Severity 'minor' is correct.

#### [🟡 minor] The login --platform flag (the only way a console player can list correctly) appears in zero first-run surfaces; the post-connect platform label even defaults its display to 'pc', hiding the mismatch
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** step 3 (login) and the in-app Companion-connect panel
- **Evidence:** Console-search across prototype/public/install.sh, install.ps1, InstallWidget.svelte, and companion/README.md returns no mention of ps4/xbox/switch/console or the --platform flag (the only hits are UA-detection code and the Run section which shows bare `wfm-fetch-inventory`). The flag is defined only in companion/src/main.rs:83-85. The single post-hoc signal, App.svelte:1448 `· {companionPlatform ?? 'pc'} ·`, falls back to displaying 'pc' when null, so even a genuinely-wrong or unknown platform reads as a plausible 'pc'.
- **Why it's friction:** A console player has no way to discover that login took an optional --platform argument, and the one place the chosen platform is shown defaults to 'pc' — the exact value that would be wrong for them — so the mismatch is invisible at every step. They only find out something is broken when orders silently target the wrong market.
- **Suggested fix:** Document --platform in companion/README.md's Run section and in the installers' Next-steps when login is introduced; render the connected platform without the silent 'pc' fallback (show 'unknown' / an explicit warning when companionPlatform is null) so a Switch player can see at a glance that they're connected as the wrong platform.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate and verified: --platform is defined only at main.rs:83-85 with default_value="pc"; no console/platform mentions in install.sh, install.ps1, InstallWidget.svelte (only UA-detection), or companion/README.md (which never documents `login` at all); App.svelte:1448 does `{companionPlatform ?? 'pc'}`, and companionPlatform comes from /health's state.platform (711, 935), which is the value baked at login. The header is load-bearing — sent on catalog/me/order calls (1086,1114,1221,1256,1321,1591).

But the finder over-rates severity at major and overstates scope. (1) Title conflation: there are two distinct flags — `--platform-tag` on fetch (the inventory ct= tag, auto-detected) and `--platform` on login (the WFM header); the claim is really only about login's --platform. (2) Population is small: the whole tool is "PC-only by nature" (root CLAUDE.md) because inventory comes from a memory scan a console player cannot run; the affected user is a console player using only login+serve for order management — a narrow side path, not the main first-run journey. (3) WFM calls send Crossplay: true (companion/CLAUDE.md), which on modern WFM largely unifies the market across platforms, plausibly reducing or eliminating the "wrong market" harm; the finder asserts silent wrong-market targeting without verifying server behavior under a mismatched Platform header with crossplay on. Net: real, but minor edge polish (drop the silent 'pc' fallback; mention --platform if login is ever documented), not a major first-run blocker.

#### [🟡 minor] Two unrelated commands both say 'past the login screen' / 'login', overloading 'login' so a user can't tell the game-client login from the `login` subcommand
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Reading stepper step 02 and the FAQ while trying to set up listing
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:917 'With Warframe past the login screen, run:'; companion/README.md:12 'past the login screen'; App.svelte:1505 'obtained at login'. None of these refer to the `login` subcommand (main.rs:52-53) which is the WFM-account signin that listing requires. The actual `login` subcommand is named nowhere the user can see.
- **Why it's friction:** 'Login' in every visible string means 'the Warframe game's title-screen login', which is a prerequisite for fetch and needs no command. The actual `wfm-fetch-inventory login` subcommand (WFM-account signin, the gate for serve/listing) is invisible. A user reasonably concludes there is no account step at all, then is blindsided when serve demands an encrypted JWT they never created. The collision of the word makes the missing step harder to even suspect.
- **Suggested fix:** Reserve 'login' in user-facing copy for the WFM `login` subcommand; reword the game prerequisite to 'past the title screen' and add the `login` subcommand to the listing onboarding.
- **Verifier note:** The three cited strings are accurate and the `login` subcommand really is absent from all user-facing onboarding copy (install.sh "Next steps" lines 101-115, App.svelte stepper steps 01-03, and the "Not connected" listing strip at App.svelte:1442-1479 which only says "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" with no mention of running login first). The substantive friction the finder identified — a new user trying to list has no instruction to run `wfm-fetch-inventory login` to create the encrypted JWT that `serve` later demands a passphrase for — is real and correctly minor. However the finder's headline framing ("overloading 'login' so a user can't tell the two apart") overstates the word-collision angle: the `login` subcommand name appears nowhere a user can see it adjacent to the game-login copy, so there is no actual side-by-side collision to confuse — the real defect is simply the missing step, not an ambiguous shared word. The subcommand IS named in CLI --help (main.rs:52 "Log in to warframe.market...") and in the developer-facing CLAUDE.md files, just not in any onboarding surface. Net: claim is true and impact is real, but the title's "overloading" emphasis is the weaker thread; the missing-login-step is the load-bearing problem.

#### [⚪ polish] Two unrelated secrets both called 'passphrase' (the export passphrase vs the companion login/JWT passphrase) are never disambiguated, colliding in the user's mental model
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 3 (login) vs the in-app Export/sync flow — the user meets the word 'passphrase' in two places that mean different things
- **Evidence:** Companion login passphrase guards the WFM JWT at rest: main.rs:468-477 ('Encryption passphrase … used to decrypt the JWT later', min 12 chars). The in-app Export/import passphrase guards a device-sync snapshot of inventory: App.svelte:1550 ('passphrase only you hold (AES-256-GCM, PBKDF2 600k)'), App.svelte:803 min 4 chars, crypto.ts:65-66. FAQ 'Can I sync between desktop and laptop?' (App.svelte:1546-1555) introduces 'a passphrase only you hold' with no note that this is NOT the companion login passphrase.
- **Why it's friction:** Both flows use AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2 600k and the identical word 'passphrase', and the FAQ even says the on-disk shape 'mirrors' the companion format. A user who set up a login passphrase will reasonably assume the Export dialog wants the same one (or that reusing it is required/safe). They are different secrets with different length rules (12 vs 4) guarding different data. The overlap quietly invites password reuse and confusion about which secret unlocks what.
- **Suggested fix:** Name them distinctly in user-facing copy: 'WFM login passphrase' (companion) vs 'export/backup passphrase' (sync). In the Export dialog and the sync FAQ, add one line: 'unrelated to the companion login passphrase — pick anything.'
- **Verifier note:** The core facts hold: the login passphrase (main.rs:468-477, min 12, "used to decrypt the JWT later") and the export passphrase (App.svelte:802-803 min 4, crypto.ts:65-66) are two different secrets both called "passphrase", both AES-256-GCM + PBKDF2 600k, and the sync FAQ (App.svelte:1546-1555) never says they're unrelated. But the finder overstated impact in two ways. (1) Misattributed citation: the claim "the FAQ even says the on-disk shape 'mirrors' the companion format" is false — no user-facing FAQ text says "mirrors". The only "mirror" mentions are App.svelte:449 (Baro schedule, unrelated) and a developer-only line in prototype/CLAUDE.md ("Same parameters mirror the companion's wfminv-jwt-v1"). A new user never reads that. (2) Severity is polish, not minor: the two prompts never appear in the same context (one is CLI-only, one is web-only), the export feature is an optional second-device sync that is NOT on the first-run path (Steps 1-6 never touch it), and every web surface self-scopes the word — Export dialog says "Decrypt on another device with the same passphrase" (App.svelte:1658) and Import says "Enter the passphrase you used when exporting it" (App.svelte:1698-1699), anchoring "passphrase" to the export action rather than login. The "invites password reuse" concern is also empty: reusing the same passphrase across two independent strong-KDF local secrets degrades nothing.

### `companion-serve` (46)

#### [🔴 major] login and serve subcommands are undocumented everywhere a newcomer can see — the WFM-listing payoff is undiscoverable
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 3/5 — user wants to actually list items on WFM (the core differentiator over browse.wf/warframe.me)
- **Evidence:** grep across companion/README.md, InstallWidget.svelte, DropZone.svelte, install.sh, install.ps1, and the landing stepper (App.svelte:888-952) finds ZERO mention of `login` or `serve`. README.md documents only the bare fetch invocation. The only occurrence of `serve` in the whole UI is App.svelte:1464 'paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' — which presumes you already know the command exists and how to run it.
- **Why it's friction:** The pitch (title/og description, App.svelte:891-896) is 'better at what to sell right now' AND the Companion view advertises 'List N on WFM'. But a cold-start user following only README + landing + InstallWidget has no path to discover the login → serve sequence that unlocks listing. They hit a 'Not connected · paste the URL' dead-end with no idea what produces that URL.
- **Suggested fix:** Document the full sequence (login → serve, with the passphrase prompt) in companion/README.md and add a short 'To list on WFM' block in the in-app Companion view; ideally show the literal `wfm-fetch-inventory serve` command there.

#### [🔴 major] Companion-connect view gives no help for the two known live failure modes (serve needs a TTY; port ≠ 5173)
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5/6 — user runs serve and tries to connect the web app
- **Evidence:** The Companion view (App.svelte:1434-1481) is a one-line lede plus a bare connect strip placeholdered 'http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…'. No mention that serve must run in a real TTY. main.rs:741 reads the passphrase via rpassword::prompt_password (no TTY → 'reading passphrase / No such device or address (os error 6)'); a --passphrase-stdin escape hatch exists at main.rs:736-739/98-101 but is never surfaced. No copy distinguishes the random serve port (main.rs:770-781) from the website's 5173.
- **Why it's friction:** These are the exact two confusions observed live. The app assumes the user already holds a working URL and offers zero recovery when serve died on the TTY error or when they paste the wrong port. parseCompanionUrl (companion.ts:51-62) validates protocol/host/token but NOT 'you pasted the website port', so pasting http://127.0.0.1:5173?token=x sails past validation and fails later with a raw 'Health check failed: HTTP 404' (companion.ts:75-76) — no 'that looks like the website port' hint.
- **Suggested fix:** In the Companion view add: (1) the literal `serve` command, (2) a 'run this in a terminal window — it needs to prompt for your passphrase' note (or document --passphrase-stdin), (3) a hint that the port is random and is NOT 5173. Optionally special-case port 5173 in parseCompanionUrl with a tailored error.
- **Verifier note:** Minor framing nuance only — every line of cited evidence is accurate. The claim frames both failures as "the Companion view gives no help," but the two manifest in different places: the TTY error (main.rs:741) occurs in the terminal before the user ever opens the Companion web view, while the port-confusion error surfaces inside that view. The web view legitimately can't help with a serve that died on the TTY error (the user isn't looking at it yet) — the real gap there is that NO user-facing doc mentions serve at all (companion/README.md documents only fetch and never mentions login/serve; InstallWidget.svelte has 0 mentions of serve/login; install.sh/install.ps1 cover only install+fetch+setcap). So the fix should land partly in onboarding docs/InstallWidget, not solely in the Companion view. The port-confusion half is fully a Companion-view + parseCompanionUrl gap as described.

#### [🔴 major] serve cannot read its passphrase outside a real TTY and there is no detection, fallback hint, or doc
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** serve (start the loopback server before listing on WFM)
- **Evidence:** main.rs:736-743 — when args.passphrase_stdin is false it calls rpassword::prompt_password('Encryption passphrase: ') with no is_terminal() guard; rpassword opens /dev/tty and errors 'No such device or address (os error 6)' when there is no controlling TTY (observed live). The --passphrase-stdin flag exists (main.rs:98-101) but is documented in ZERO user-facing place: grep for passphrase_stdin/passphrase-stdin across *.md/*.sh/*.ps1/*.svelte returns nothing; companion/README.md never mentions serve or login at all.
- **Why it's friction:** The user has done everything right (login succeeded, JWT encrypted) and serve dies on a cryptic POSIX errno the moment they run it from anything that isn't an interactive shell (IDE run button, systemd, nohup, some terminal multiplexer setups, a wrapper script). The escape hatch (--passphrase-stdin) is invisible. The error message is the raw OS error with no 'run this in a terminal' translation.
- **Suggested fix:** Detect std::io::stdin().is_terminal() before prompting; if not a TTY and --passphrase-stdin was not given, bail with an actionable message ('serve needs a real terminal to read your passphrase, or pass --passphrase-stdin and pipe it'). Map the os-error-6 case to that same guidance. Document login -> serve -> --passphrase-stdin in companion/README.md (which currently documents only fetch).
- **Verifier note:** Severity over-rated as blocker; it is major. The DEFAULT and only-documented way to run serve is an interactive terminal, and login (main.rs:468-472) also prompts on a TTY — so any user who finished login already has a working terminal and will naturally run serve in it, where the prompt works fine. The os-error-6 failure only fires on non-default invocations the docs never suggest (IDE run button, systemd, nohup, some multiplexer setups). That is a real, cryptic, undocumented sharp edge with an invisible escape hatch — but it does not block the documented happy path, so it is major, not blocker. Everything else in the finding is correct: code (main.rs:736-743 no is_terminal guard; flag at 98-101), the only error context is .context("reading passphrase") with no terminal-translation, and passphrase-stdin appears in zero user-facing files. companion/README.md is even worse than stated — it documents only fetch and never mentions login OR serve at all.

#### [🔴 major] 'serve' is never documented for Windows — the only place it appears is a 'paste the URL' placeholder, with no command, no TTY/double-click warning, no port-vs-5173 disambiguation
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5: starting serve to connect the companion to the web app
- **Evidence:** grep for 'serve' / 'passphrase_stdin' across all .md/.svelte/.ps1/.sh user-facing files returns no usage instruction — only App.svelte:1463-1471 ('paste the URL the serve subcommand printed', placeholder http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…). companion/README.md documents only fetch, never serve. On Windows rpassword 7.5.3 reads the passphrase from the console handle (CONIN$), so a user who double-clicks wfm-fetch-inventory.exe (no attached console) or launches serve from a non-console context hits the same 'reading passphrase' failure observed on Linux without a TTY (main.rs:741).
- **Why it's friction:** The app's order-listing feature (its 'better than browse.wf' differentiator) is gated behind `serve`, but a new user is never told the command exists, never told to run it in a real terminal window, and never told the printed port is random and different from the website's 5173. They land on the Companion tab seeing 'Not connected · paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' with no idea how to produce that URL. This is the in-app dead-end version of the known live serve pain, and it bites Windows users too because the double-click-the-exe instinct produces no console for the passphrase prompt.
- **Suggested fix:** Add explicit serve instructions to the Companion tab and FAQ: the exact command (`wfm-fetch-inventory serve`), 'run it in an open PowerShell/terminal window — do not double-click the .exe, it needs a console to read your passphrase', and 'copy the WHOLE http://127.0.0.1:<random-port>?token=… line it prints — that port is not 5173'. Document serve in companion/README.md alongside fetch.
- **Verifier note:** The core claim is fully verified: `serve` appears in user-facing files only as App.svelte:1464's "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" placeholder (with http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=… at line 1471), companion/README.md documents only fetch+build (never serve), install.ps1's "Next steps" (lines 84-96) and install.sh end at the fetch step, InstallWidget.svelte and the FAQ (App.svelte:1496-1578) never mention serve, and SECURITY.md mentions it only as threat-model prose. The in-app dead-end and the missing command/port-vs-5173/TTY guidance are all real. One overstatement to correct: the Windows double-click failure is less certain than the finder implies. The companion is a console-subsystem Rust binary, so double-clicking wfm-fetch-inventory.exe spawns its own console window where rpassword CAN read from CONIN$; the genuine Windows failure mode is launching serve from a non-console host (a launcher/script with no inherited console), not the ordinary double-click. The Linux TTY failure (no stdin fallback at main.rs:741 unless --passphrase_stdin) is the concrete confirmed case. This is a secondary point; the primary friction — serve being entirely undocumented as a command plus the bare-placeholder Companion tab — holds without it.

#### [🔴 major] `serve` dies on "reading passphrase / os error 6" with zero in-app or in-binary guidance to use a TTY (or --passphrase-stdin)
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5 — run `wfm-fetch-inventory serve` to enable listing on WFM
- **Evidence:** companion/src/main.rs:741 calls `rpassword::prompt_password("Encryption passphrase: ")` with no isatty check and no fallback; the only non-TTY path is the undocumented `--passphrase_stdin` flag (main.rs:99-101). The error surfaces via `.context("reading passphrase")` (main.rs:742) and bubbles as raw anyhow text. No string anywhere in companion/ or prototype/ mentions 'tty', 'terminal', or 'No such device'. The in-app companion connect copy (App.svelte:1459-1478) gives no hint serve must run in a real TTY.
- **Why it's friction:** This is the single confirmed live blocker. A user who launches serve from anything that isn't an interactive terminal (IDE run button, nohup, a pipe, certain terminal emulators/systemd) gets `Error: reading passphrase / No such device or address (os error 6)` — a cryptic libc error with no next step. They never get the URL the web app demands, so the entire 'list on WFM' half of the product is unreachable. The fix flag exists but is invisible.
- **Suggested fix:** In run_serve, detect non-TTY (libc::isatty / std::io::stdin().is_terminal()) before calling rpassword and print an actionable message: 'serve needs an interactive terminal to read the passphrase. Run it directly in a terminal, or pipe the passphrase: echo "…" | wfm-fetch-inventory serve --passphrase-stdin'. Also surface --passphrase-stdin in install.sh/ps1 next-steps and the in-app companion tab.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate and verified: main.rs:741 prompt_password with .context("reading passphrase") at :742, no is_terminal guard; --passphrase_stdin (main.rs:98-101) is the only non-TTY path and is documented only in clap help ("for automation / systemd units"); no 'tty'/'terminal'/'No such device' string anywhere in companion/ or prototype/; App.svelte:1459-1478 connect copy gives no TTY hint; and neither install.sh nor install.ps1 mentions the serve subcommand at all (their Next-steps cover only login/fetch). However the finder over-rated severity as blocker. rpassword 7's prompt_password on Unix reads from /dev/tty (the controlling terminal), not stdin, so a simple pipe (echo x | serve) does NOT throw os error 6 — it still reads from the TTY. The 'No such device or address (os error 6)' fires only when there is NO controlling terminal at all (IDE run button, nohup, systemd, detached spawn). That is a real, confirmed-in-session population, but the documented happy path (run serve in a normal terminal) works fine. It blocks a subset of launch methods, not the default flow, so this is major, not a blocker.

#### [🔴 major] No single 'getting started in 60 seconds' path; the login → serve prerequisite chain is never spelled out anywhere a user looks
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Steps 3 & 5 — user wants to list on WFM and must run login then serve
- **Evidence:** grep across prototype/src: the user-facing string 'wfm-fetch-inventory login' appears nowhere (App.svelte:917/1505 'login' = game title screen / WFM auth narrative, not the subcommand). 'serve' appears once (App.svelte:1464) with no run instructions. InstallWidget.svelte covers only the curl one-liner + setcap; no login/serve. companion/README.md documents only fetch (lines 10-36), never login or serve. Companion tab header App.svelte:1437-1440 explains what the loopback CLI is but gives zero commands.
- **Why it's friction:** The three subcommands have a hard ordering — login (writes encrypted JWT) must run before serve (decrypts it; main.rs:728-733 bails 'Run login first' if absent). A new user who clicks 'List on WFM' is told to 'paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' (1464) but is never told serve exists as a command, that login is a prerequisite, or where to run them. There is no end-to-end runbook in any README, the install widget, the FAQ, or the Companion tab. The fetch path is documented; the entire listing path is folklore.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a top-level README.md (none exists at repo root) and an in-app 'To list on WFM' block in the Companion tab giving the literal three lines: `wfm-fetch-inventory login` (once), then `wfm-fetch-inventory serve`, then paste the printed URL. A FAQ entry 'How do I list items on warframe.market?' covering login→serve→paste would catch the user where they actually ask.
- **Verifier note:** Two small precision points, neither defeats the claim. (1) The finder says serve "appears once (App.svelte:1464) with no run instructions" — accurate, but that line does name it as "the serve subcommand," so serve's existence is hinted (not invented); login as a prerequisite, however, is genuinely never mentioned in the UI. (2) The claim's framing that there's "no single 60-second path" slightly overstates: the CORE value path (fetch -> drop inventory.json -> read what-to-sell) IS spelled out as numbered steps 01/02/03 at App.svelte:905-940. What is undocumented is specifically the LISTING path (login -> serve -> paste URL), an advanced action reached only after the companion already works. So the friction is real and correctly scoped to the listing flow, but it does not block first value, which keeps it at major rather than blocker.

#### [🔴 major] Companion-connect panel re-exposes the live serve TTY failure and the two-port confusion with zero in-app help
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5 — user runs serve and/or tries to paste the URL
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1459-1478 — 'Not connected · paste the URL the serve subcommand printed', placeholder 'http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…', no surrounding guidance. serve reads the passphrase via rpassword::prompt_password (main.rs:741) which requires a real TTY → the known 'reading passphrase / No such device or address (os error 6)'; the only escape hatch is --passphrase-stdin (main.rs:98-101) which is documented nowhere user-facing. The serve port is random (ServeArgs port default 0, main.rs:95-96; bind 127.0.0.1:0) and printed at main.rs:778-781 — distinct from the website's 5173.
- **Why it's friction:** Both documented live pains land precisely here. (a) A user who runs serve inside a non-TTY context (some terminals-in-editors, piped invocations, certain DE launchers) gets os error 6 and the app offers no hint about TTY or --passphrase-stdin. (b) The placeholder shows :XXXXX but nothing warns that this is NOT 5173, so a user who has the website open at 127.0.0.1:5173 may paste that. The panel assumes a working URL is already in hand and gives no recovery path when it isn't.
- **Suggested fix:** Add one line of help text under the input: 'This is the random port serve printed (e.g. 49xxx) — not the website's 5173. Run serve in a real terminal; if you see "reading passphrase / os error 6", that terminal has no TTY.' Link to a FAQ entry. Optionally have the connect handler detect a pasted :5173 and warn 'that looks like the website port, not the companion port.'
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is all accurate (App.svelte:1459-1478 panel with bare placeholder and no guidance; main.rs:741 rpassword::prompt_password; main.rs:98-101 --passphrase-stdin doc'd only in the Rust #[arg] help; main.rs:95-96 + 770 random port). I confirmed there is NO in-app/doc help anywhere for either pain: the FAQ (App.svelte:1500-1577) has 6 entries, none about serve/TTY/ports; InstallWidget (components/InstallWidget.svelte) and both install scripts stop at the fetch step (install.ps1:84-93 lists steps 1-4, no serve/login/passphrase); no root README exists; grep for 5173/TTY/os error 6/passphrase-stdin across prototype/src and install scripts returns nothing. The TTY half is the stronger, fully-unmitigated friction. One nuance the finder overstated: the 5173-confusion is PARTIALLY caught — parseCompanionUrl (companion.ts:61-62) rejects a pasted bare website URL with 'URL is missing ?token=… — re-paste the full line', so it is not literally 'zero help' on the paste path, though it never names the port mistake and the finder's specific :5173 detection does not exist. This nuance does not change severity; the TTY/passphrase failure alone (cryptic os error 6, no recovery hint anywhere in app or docs) justifies major because it fully blocks Step 5 order-management onboarding for users in non-TTY contexts.

#### [🔴 major] Stale market data has no qualitative label and the only warning (the dot) is aria-hidden
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — user reads 'what to sell' and trusts the prices
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1061-1067 renders 'Market data' + marketStaleness (a neutral relative time like '29 min ago', ago() at :594) with the freshness signal carried solely by <span class="dot {marketFreshness}" aria-hidden="true"> (1063). marketFreshness buckets are fresh/aging/stale (App.svelte:605-611, red after 24h). No text ever says 'fresh'/'stale'/'outdated'; no banner. FAQ App.svelte:1540-1541 explains the dot colors but only if the user opens that FAQ.
- **Why it's friction:** The product's entire pitch is current sell decisions, yet the only thing distinguishing a 29-minute snapshot from a 3-week-old one is a small colored dot that is explicitly hidden from screen readers and easy for sighted users to miss next to a neutral timestamp. A user acting on weeks-stale prices gets no worded warning — directly the 'silently weeks stale' risk.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a visible word to the staleness pill ('29 min ago · fresh' / '23 days ago · stale') driven by marketFreshness, and remove aria-hidden (or add an aria-label) so the state is announced. When marketFreshness === 'stale', show an inline 'Prices may be outdated' note near the Sell view header, not buried in the FAQ.
- **Verifier note:** Minor overstatement: for sighted users the staleness signal is not literally "silent" — the dot turns red (.dot.stale -> var(--bad), App.svelte:2077) after 24h, a real if easy-to-miss color cue. The "silently weeks stale / no warning" framing is fully accurate only for screen-reader users (the dot is aria-hidden at :1063 with no aria-label, so the state is never announced) and for the absence of any *worded* warning. Everything else in the finding is verbatim correct: marketFreshness (:605-611, fresh/aging/stale, red after 24h) is consumed in exactly one place (:1063) as a CSS class only and never rendered as text; the only adjacent label is the neutral ago() relative time (:588-597, :1066); the FAQ (:1536-1543) documents the dot colors but is a collapsed <details> the user must open.

#### [🔴 major] Companion-connect step offers zero recovery for the two known live serve failures (TTY passphrase crash, random-vs-5173 port confusion)
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 5 — run serve, then 6 — paste the URL into the Companion tab to list on WFM
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1459-1478: the disconnected state shows only "Not connected · paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" and a field placeholdered http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=… . No mention that serve must run in a real TTY or it dies with "reading passphrase / No such device or address (os error 6)", and no note that the serve port is random and different from the website's 5173. The companion/CLAUDE.md confirms serve binds 127.0.0.1:0 (random port) and prompts for the JWT passphrase.
- **Why it's friction:** This is the gate between "see what to sell" and the differentiator's full payoff (actually listing on WFM in-app). The two confusions called out as observed live pain — the TTY passphrase crash and mistaking 5173 for the serve port — both land exactly here, and the UI assumes the user already holds a working URL. When they don't, the field just sits there with a generic error span (companionError, line 1465) and no diagnostic. A first-timer has no path forward without leaving the app to debug the CLI.
- **Suggested fix:** Add inline help under the Not-connected field: a one-liner that the URL is the random http://127.0.0.1:<port>?token=… printed by serve (NOT the website's 5173), plus a note/expander that serve must be run in a real terminal (TTY) and what the os error 6 / passphrase failure means and how to fix it.
- **Verifier note:** Two precision points, neither overturns the finding. (1) The port-vs-5173 confusion is partially mitigated OUTSIDE the app: serve prints the exact connect URL — companion/src/main.rs:778-781 emits "In the web app, set the companion URL to: http://{actual}?token={session_token}". A user who reaches a successful serve is handed the correct full URL, so the port confusion mainly bites those who never get that far (i.e., the TTY crash) or who guess without reading stdout. The app UI itself still gives zero guidance, as claimed. (2) The TTY default is confirmed structurally by the opt-in --passphrase-stdin flag (main.rs:98-101, 736-742) and the rpassword::prompt_password call whose error context is literally "reading passphrase" (main.rs:742) — matching the observed "Error: reading passphrase / No such device or address (os error 6)". Severity major is correct, not blocker: this gates the secondary differentiator (in-app WFM listing), while the PRIMARY value prop (drop inventory.json -> read "what to sell", steps 4/6) is fully reachable without ever running serve.

#### [🔴 major] --passphrase-stdin (the shipped fix for the os-error-6 serve TTY failure) is documented nowhere a user can see
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** serve (Linux, running serve from a non-TTY context: IDE terminal, pipe, systemd, `serve &`)
- **Evidence:** The flag exists only at companion/src/main.rs:100-101 and is consumed at main.rs:736; a repo-wide grep finds zero occurrences of `passphrase-stdin`/`passphrase_stdin` in any .svelte, .md, .sh, .ps1, or .html (only the two main.rs lines). The known live failure is `serve` dying with 'reading passphrase / No such device or address (os error 6)' when no TTY is present.
- **Why it's friction:** The single known live blocker on the order-management half of the product already HAS a built-in workaround — `serve --passphrase-stdin` reading one line from stdin — but a stuck user has no way to discover it short of reading Rust source or running `--help`. The fix exists and is invisible at exactly the moment the user is blocked. The doc-comment even names the use cases (automation / systemd) that produce the os-error-6.
- **Suggested fix:** Surface `--passphrase-stdin` in the companion-connect panel's failure help and in whatever serve docs get written: 'No such device or address (os error 6) means serve has no terminal to read the passphrase — run it in a real terminal, or pipe the passphrase: `printf %s "$PASS" | wfm-fetch-inventory serve --passphrase-stdin`'.
- **Verifier note:** The finder's grep set listed .svelte/.md/.sh/.ps1/.html but not .rs; in fact a repo-wide grep including .rs returns exactly the two main.rs lines (98 and 101/736-739) and nothing else — so the "documented nowhere a user can see" claim is even stronger than stated: there is no README in the repo at all, install.sh (lines 101-115) and install.ps1 document only fetch+setcap and never mention `serve` whatsoever, and SECURITY.md (lines 21, 143-144) mentions the passphrase concept but neither the flag nor the TTY failure. The many `passphrase` hits in prototype/src/ are the unrelated browser WebCrypto export feature, not the companion. One nuance the finder understates is which users hit it: a normal desktop terminal reads the passphrase fine, so the os-error-6 only strikes the non-TTY subset (IDE terminal, pipe, systemd, `serve &`) — narrower than the whole new-user base, but exactly the automation/systemd cases the doc-comment at main.rs:98-99 calls out.

#### [🔴 major] The 01/02/03 onboarding stepper presents fetch as the whole journey and never mentions login/serve, so order-management is a dead prerequisite chain discovered only at the Companion tab
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** first-run stepper -> later: Companion connect
- **Evidence:** The empty-state stepper (App.svelte:901-937) is exactly three steps: get companion / run `wfm-fetch-inventory` / drop the file. A grep of App.svelte for a standalone `login` step returns nothing (only 'past the login screen' game-state references). The Companion tab (App.svelte:1459-1478) then asks the user to 'paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' with no upstream pointer that `login` (main.rs:352) must run first and that serve will refuse without ~/.config/wfminv/wfm-jwt.enc (main.rs:728-733: 'No JWT at ... Run login first').
- **Why it's friction:** A user who reaches the Companion tab to actually list items is two undocumented subcommands deep (login, then serve), each with its own passphrase prompt, but the onboarding flow taught them the product is a single command (`wfm-fetch-inventory`). The prerequisite chain (login writes the encrypted JWT -> serve decrypts it -> serve prints the URL) is invisible until the user hits the 'No JWT' bail at the CLI. This is the second-order shape of the logged 'login/serve undocumented' item: the stepper actively sets the expectation that there is nothing past fetch.
- **Suggested fix:** Either add a fourth optional stepper card ('Want to list on WFM? run `login` once, then `serve`'), or have the Companion 'Not connected' panel link to a short login->serve sequence. The panel currently assumes a working URL already exists in hand.
- **Verifier note:** Severity is under-rated. The finder called it "minor"; it's "major". The login->serve chain gates the product's headline differentiator (the "List N on WFM" button / order management, App.svelte:1090,1455), which is the entire reason TennoWorth claims to beat browse.wf and warframe.me at acting on "what to sell". Every new user who tries to list hits the Companion "Not connected" panel (App.svelte:1459-1478) asking for a URL they were never told how to produce, and only discovers login+serve (each with its own passphrase prompt) by hitting the CLI bail at main.rs:728-733. That is a dead-end on the primary monetizing action, not a cosmetic stepper omission. It stops short of "blocker" only because the read-only "what to sell" table works without serve. Also worth noting: the InstallWidget reinforces the wrong expectation even harder than the finder said — InstallWidget.svelte:65 literally states "One command — paste and go," and InstallWidget has zero mentions of login/serve/passphrase.

#### [🔴 major] Companion tab says "Required to list on WFM" but offers no path to learn what `serve` is, that `login` comes first, or that the port differs from 5173
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5 — user opens the Companion tab to try listing on WFM
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1437-1440 lede: "The loopback CLI that reads your inventory and relays listing actions to WFM. Required to list on WFM." The connect strip (App.svelte:1459-1478) shows only "Not connected · paste the URL the `serve` subcommand printed" and a field placeholdered `http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…`. `serve` is referenced as a known noun but defined nowhere in the app; the install widget (InstallWidget.svelte:59-120) documents only fetch; the FAQ summaries (App.svelte:1501/1520/1536/1546/1558/1569) contain no login/serve/connect entry. parseCompanionUrl rejecting an https or non-loopback paste (companion.ts:53-58) hints at the two-port confusion but only *after* a wrong paste, never proactively.
- **Why it's friction:** The tab makes a promise ("required to list") and then assumes the user already possesses a working serve URL — i.e. that they've independently discovered serve exists, learned login must run first, run both in a TTY, and not confused the random port with 5173. Every one of those is undocumented at this surface. The result is a dead-ended mental model: the user is told they need a thing, shown a box for it, and given no thread to pull to obtain it. This is the discoverability-specific complement to the logged "connect view gives no recovery for the two live serve failures" — that item is about error recovery; this is about there being no on-ramp at all.
- **Suggested fix:** In the not-connected strip, add an inline 2-step "How to get this URL": (1) `wfm-fetch-inventory login` (once), (2) `wfm-fetch-inventory serve` in a real terminal — copy the printed `http://127.0.0.1:<random>?token=…` line. Note explicitly that the port is random and is NOT 5173 (the website). Link to a single getting-started block so login→serve sequencing lives somewhere a user can find it.
- **Verifier note:** None of the cited evidence is wrong — every reference verified. The claim slightly overstates by lumping the two-port (5173 vs random) confusion into a discoverability gap; that part is the weakest leg since parseCompanionUrl (companion.ts:51-59) DOES catch a wrong-line https paste with a pointed message, so it's partially handled reactively. But the core finding holds independently: the Companion tab promises "Required to list on WFM" (App.svelte:1439) and provides zero on-ramp to obtain a serve URL. Confirmed serve is referenced as an undefined noun exactly once (App.svelte:1464); InstallWidget documents only install+setcap (components/InstallWidget.svelte:91-120), the onboarding steps 01-03 document only the bare `wfm-fetch-inventory` fetch (App.svelte:900-938), and the six FAQ entries cover safety/data/prices/sync/Overwolf/Rivens — none mention login or serve. login IS a genuine prerequisite: serve decrypts a JWT that only `run_login` creates (companion/src/main.rs:352-468), and the app never says login must run first. Severity is correctly major, not blocker: this gates only the order-management/list-on-WFM feature (the differentiator), while the core read-only "what to sell" journey via DropZone is fully documented and reachable without ever touching serve.

#### [🔴 major] Companion connect shows a false-green "Connected" for any wrong/stale token, because the health probe is unauthenticated
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 5-6 — serve prints a fresh URL; user pastes it into the in-app Companion connect box
- **Evidence:** companion.ts:74-78 pingCompanion does `fetch(${cfg.baseUrl}/health)` with NO X-Session-Token (the only headered call is callCompanion at companion.ts:168). The /health route is auth-free by design (main.rs:931-937). verifyCompanion (App.svelte:705-723) only calls pingCompanion, so on success it sets companionStatus='connected' and renders the green 'Connected' dot (App.svelte:1443-1448) without ever checking the token. The token is first exercised on a real action: submitPlan → callCompanion → 401 'missing or invalid X-Session-Token' (main.rs:948-954).
- **Why it's friction:** serve mints a NEW random token every run (main.rs:769). A returning user who restarts serve (e.g. after the live TTY/os-error-6 failure, or any reboot) very plausibly pastes the URL from previous scrollback. Connect reports green 'Connected', so they trust it, click 'List 50 on WFM', hand-tune an entire 50-item listing batch in the modal, hit Send — and only THEN see a raw 'missing or invalid X-Session-Token' as a bare red line (ListingReviewModal.svelte:115-117, 282-283). The connect step had the information to reject the token immediately and didn't. This is distinct from the logged truncated-token item (that's URL-parsing byte loss); here the full, syntactically valid token is simply stale, and the no-auth health probe structurally cannot catch it.
- **Suggested fix:** Make verifyCompanion confirm the TOKEN, not just liveness: after the /health ping, do one token-bearing GET (e.g. /plan/pending via getPendingPlan, which is already called at App.svelte:717) and treat a 401 as 'wrong token — re-copy the full URL from the serve output (the token changes every time you restart serve)'. Only show green once an authed call succeeds.
- **Verifier note:** Every cited line checks out (one path typo: ListingReviewModal lives at prototype/src/components/, not src/lib/ — error render is line 283 `{networkError}`, send path catch at 115-117). The finder UNDERSTATED the trigger, not overstated it. verifyCompanion DOES make a token-bearing call — getPendingPlan at App.svelte:717 — but it sets companionStatus='connected' FIRST (line 712), then wraps getPendingPlan in its own `try { ... } catch { pendingPlan = null }` (717-718) that swallows the 401 entirely. So the authed call already happens; its failure is just discarded, which is the precise bug. The finder's suggested fix (treat that 401 as a connect failure) maps exactly onto removing that swallow. Also: the false-green fires AUTOMATICALLY for returning users, not only on manual re-paste — onMount (App.svelte:212-213) restores the persisted config from localStorage (saved at connectCompanion:769) and auto-runs verifyCompanion, so a stale token from a prior serve run shows green on page load with zero user action. random_token(32) per serve run (main.rs:769) and the no-auth /health (main.rs:931-937) vs. token-gated everything-else (main.rs:943-954) are both confirmed.

#### [🔴 major] The in-app FAQ has zero entries on obtaining or connecting the serve URL, yet the connect box's only instruction is "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed"
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 5 — user reaches the Companion connect box with no working URL in hand
- **Evidence:** Companion connect box copy is only '· paste the URL the `serve` subcommand printed' (App.svelte:1463-1466). The FAQ (App.svelte:1500-1577) has six entries — ban-safety, where-data-goes, price-currency, sync, Overwolf, rivens — and none mention `serve`, `login`, the passphrase, or how to get the connect URL. grep confirms `serve` appears in App.svelte only at the connect placeholder (1464) and in the market 'serves that file' prose (1540); the only `login` references are the encrypted-export passphrase and the ban-safety paragraph.
- **Why it's friction:** A first-timer who has run fetch and dropped inventory.json successfully now wants to list, sees 'paste the URL serve printed', has never run serve, and opens the FAQ to learn how — and finds nothing. The natural in-app help surface is silent on the entire second half of the product (login → serve → connect). This compounds the logged 'serve/login undocumented on WFM' and 'companion tab says required but never explains' items by confirming the one place a stuck user looks for answers offers none, even though five lower-priority topics get FAQ space.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an FAQ entry 'How do I connect the companion to list items?' walking login → serve (in a real terminal, not piped) → copy the printed http://127.0.0.1:PORT?token=… line → paste here, with the note that the port and token change every serve run and that serve must run in a TTY (the os-error-6 caveat).

#### [🔴 major] Every companion escape-hatch flag (--port, --pid, --passphrase-stdin, --platform-tag, --jwt-path) exists only in --help; the fixes for the known live failures are invisible to users
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** fetch/serve recovery, when the happy path fails
- **Evidence:** A grep for '--port|--pid|--passphrase-stdin|--platform-tag|--jwt-path|--email' across prototype/, companion/README.md, SECURITY.md, and all *.md returns zero user-facing hits (only CLAUDE.md's unrelated --out for the scraper). All flags are defined in main.rs (FetchArgs 60-71, LoginArgs 76-85, ServeArgs 91-101) but documented nowhere a newcomer reads. The flags map directly onto known live pain: --port fixes 'serve port already in use', --pid fixes the multi-instance/arbitrary-process pick (find_wf_pid returns the first HashMap match, main.rs:218-223), --passphrase-stdin is the documented-only-in-code workaround for the os-error-6 TTY passphrase failure (main.rs:98-101,736-743), --platform-tag overrides a mis-detected ct.
- **Why it's friction:** When the user hits exactly the failures the brief calls out as observed-live (random-port collision, passphrase TTY death, wrong process picked), the binary HAS the escape hatch but the user has no way to discover it short of running --help, which nothing tells them to do. The product ships the fix and then hides it.
- **Suggested fix:** Reference the relevant flag in each failure's error text (e.g. the bind-failed error should mention '--port', the passphrase prompt failure should mention '--passphrase-stdin'), and add a short flags table to companion/README.md.
- **Verifier note:** Minor over-reach in the evidence list, not enough to flip the claim: (1) the flags are not "invisible" in the absolute sense — clap auto-generates `--help`, so a user who knows to run it sees them; the real gap is that no error message or doc tells the user `--help`/the flag exists at the moment of failure. (2) `--email` is weak filler in the title: login email is prompted interactively when omitted (LoginArgs:75-77), so its absence from docs has near-zero impact. The load-bearing flags are `--port`, `--passphrase-stdin`, and `--pid`, which map exactly onto the three observed-live failures. (3) companion/README.md does document the happy path (sudo/setcap/run) thoroughly — the gap is specifically recovery/escape-hatch docs, not all docs.

#### [🔴 major] No surface anywhere states the install → login → serve → connect ORDER; each subcommand is described in isolation so the dependency chain is invisible
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** The whole listing half — from finishing fetch to a working connect
- **Evidence:** The connect panel (App.svelte:1459-1466) says only 'paste the URL the `serve` subcommand printed' — no mention that serve first requires a stored JWT, which requires running `login` (main.rs:728-733 serve bails 'No JWT … Run `wfm-fetch-inventory login` first.' — but only after the user already tried serve). README documents neither login nor serve (grep: 0 hits). install.sh/install.ps1 next-steps stop at fetch+dropzone (install.sh:101-115, install.ps1:84-94). login's own success message (main.rs:493) says 'You can now run other companion subcommands' without naming serve.
- **Why it's friction:** There is no single place — README, installer next-steps, app FAQ, or connect panel — that lays out the four ordered steps needed to list on WFM. The user discovers the ordering only by hitting failures in sequence: run serve → bail 'run login first' → run login → run serve again → paste URL. Every step's docs assume the previous step already happened. The 'getting started in 60 seconds' path for the listing half does not exist as a sequence anywhere; it must be reverse-engineered from error messages.
- **Suggested fix:** Add one ordered checklist (install → `login` once → `serve` (leave running) → paste the printed URL here) to the Companion connect panel's not-connected state, and mirror it in the installer next-steps and the FAQ. Make login's success message name the next command explicitly: 'Next: run `wfm-fetch-inventory serve` and paste the URL it prints into the app.'
- **Verifier note:** Minor line-number drift: the connect-panel string is at App.svelte:1464, not 1459-1466 (it falls within that block, so the cite is acceptable). main.rs:493 is paraphrased — the actual text is "You can now run other companion subcommands that need WFM auth." (does not name serve, as claimed — accurate). Everything else verified verbatim: serve bail at main.rs:729-732, install.sh:101-115 and install.ps1:84-94 next-steps stop at fetch+dropzone, companion/README.md documents ONLY fetch (login and serve subcommands are entirely absent, not just under-documented). One nuance the finder undersold AND oversold: the app DOES have a numbered 01/02/03 onboarding (App.svelte:913-937) but it covers only install -> fetch -> drop-in (the read-only half) and never sequences the listing half — which strengthens the claim that the listing sequence exists nowhere. Severity counter-point: the serve bail at main.rs:730 explicitly names the missing prerequisite command ("Run `wfm-fetch-inventory login` first"), so the chain self-corrects in one fail-retry round-trip rather than leaving the user stuck — this caps it below blocker, but major holds because it gates TennoWorth's core differentiator (pushing listings to WFM) behind reverse-engineering from errors.

- **Platform:** both · **Step:** After step 03 'Drop it below' / after install.sh next-step 4

The single most valuable second action — push these listings to WFM — has zero discoverability from any of the three onboarding surfaces.
