The "List N on WFM" button (App.svelte:1084-1091, 1451-1455) only renders when companionStatus==='connected', so a new user never sees it. The finder slightly overstates "zero discoverability from any surface": the post-load sidebar DOES carry a persistent "Companion" nav-item (App.svelte:1005) whose Not-connected panel says "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" (line 1464). So a curious user who clicks the Companion tab finds a serve breadcrumb — but it assumes they already know to run serve, and nothing anywhere tells them to run `login` first (which is mandatory — serve prompts for the JWT passphrase set at login). #### [🔴 major] The word 'serve' appears in exactly one in-app string and 'login' never appears as a subcommand — a user told to 'paste the URL serve printed' has no in-app path to learn how to produce it
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** User clicks the Companion tab to try listing, sees 'paste the URL the serve subcommand printed'
- **Evidence:** grep of App.svelte + InstallWidget.svelte: `serve` occurs only at App.svelte:1464; the subcommand `login` is never surfaced in the UI (1505/1540 'login' references are prose about the game login screen and the cron, not the CLI subcommand). The #companion anchor (App.svelte:907, DropZone.svelte:62) resolves to InstallWidget id='companion' (InstallWidget.svelte:59), which documents only the fetch command.
- **Why it's friction:** The connect step assumes the user already knows two undocumented commands (login, then serve) and has run them in the right order. There is no in-app link, FAQ entry, or tooltip explaining how to obtain the URL it demands. The one anchor that the word 'companion' points to teaches a different command entirely. This is the in-app dead-end behind the known serve onboarding gap, viewed from the discoverability angle: the app references a command it never teaches and provides no jump to learn it.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the 'serve' reference a link/popover that shows the login→serve sequence inline, and add an Install·FAQ entry titled 'How do I get the companion URL for listing?'
- **Verifier note:** Severity major holds, but the finder slightly overstates scope: this blocks only the WFM-listing path (the Companion tab's connect step), not the primary "what to sell" journey, which needs only `wfm-fetch-inventory` (fetch) + dropping inventory.json — both of which ARE taught (App.svelte:907,918; InstallWidget.svelte:59-96). So it's a dead-end for the listing/order-management feature specifically, not the whole onboarding. Minor evidence nit: the finder cites "1505/1540 'login' references" — line 1540 is about market.json freshness ("the site serves that file"), not login; the actual game-login prose is at 917 ("past the login screen") and 1505 ("obtained at login"). The substance is correct either way.

#### [🟡 minor] Pasting the website port (5173) into the companion box fails with a raw JSON-parse error, not 'that's the wrong port'
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5→6 — connect the web app to the running serve
- **Evidence:** pingCompanion (companion.ts:74-78) does `fetch(${baseUrl}/health)` then `r.json()`. If the user pastes http://127.0.0.1:5173?token=… (the Vite dev/site port), the dev server answers 200 with SPA HTML, so `r.ok` is true and `r.json()` throws 'Unexpected token <'. That bubbles to verifyCompanion's catch (App.svelte:719-721) and renders verbatim as companionError in the Not-connected strip (App.svelte:1465). parseCompanionUrl (companion.ts:44-67) only validates protocol/host/token — it cannot distinguish 5173 from the random serve port.
- **Why it's friction:** This is exactly the observed '5173 vs random port' confusion. The placeholder literally shows http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX (App.svelte:1471), inviting the user to fill in a port, and 5173 is the one port number they've already typed into their browser. The resulting error ('Unexpected token <' / 'Health check failed') reads like a bug in the app, not 'you pasted the page's own URL.' No copy anywhere explains the port is random and printed by serve.
- **Suggested fix:** In pingCompanion, validate the /health response shape ({ok:true}) and on HTML/parse failure return a tailored error: 'Got a web page, not the companion, at that URL — you may have pasted the site address (port 5173). Use the http://127.0.0.1:<random>?token=… line that serve prints.' Optionally reject the app's own location.port in parseCompanionUrl.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code is accurate (companion.ts:74-78 ok-only check + r.json(); App.svelte:719-722 catch; :1465 verbatim render; :1471 port-inviting placeholder; parseCompanionUrl can't distinguish ports), and there is no mitigation anywhere (no location.port guard, no FAQ/doc/error copy about the random port; serve at main.rs:780-781 prints the full correct line but nothing warns about 5173). Two corrections to the finder: (1) the trigger is narrower than 'paste the page URL you already have' — a bare paste of http://127.0.0.1:5173 with NO token hits the clean 'URL is missing ?token=…' guard (companion.ts:62) FIRST and gives a clear error; the Unexpected-token-'<' JSON-parse failure only fires when a ?token= is ALSO present, i.e. the user copies serve's full line and edits only the port to 5173. (2) In production (static host) /health on 5173 would 404 → 'Health check failed: HTTP 404' (clearer); the raw 'Unexpected token <' is specific to the Vite dev SPA fallback. Severity is Major-overstated: serve prints a directly copy-pasteable correct line, the bare-URL mistake self-explains, and the broken path requires a specific port substitution into a token-bearing URL — opaque-error UX on a real-but-narrower trigger is minor, not a hard blocker.

#### [🟡 minor] Wrong/empty passphrase on serve aborts the whole process instead of re-prompting
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5 — serve prompts for the JWT passphrase
- **Evidence:** decrypt_jwt returns `anyhow!("Wrong passphrase, or the JWT file was modified.")` (main.rs:547) and run_serve calls `decrypt_jwt(&blob, &passphrase)?` (main.rs:744) with no retry loop — a single typo exits the binary. login enforces ≥12-char passphrases (main.rs:476-478) but serve accepts any input and just fails the AEAD.
- **Why it's friction:** The message is clear and actionable, but a single mistyped passphrase means the user must re-run the whole serve command (and, given finding #1, possibly fight the TTY issue again). A mild but repeated annoyance during the most fragile step.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the passphrase prompt + decrypt in a small retry loop (e.g. 3 attempts) before bailing, when running interactively.

#### [🟡 minor] Expired JWT only fails later, at first listing/orders action, with a raw 'WFM HTTP 401' relayed to the browser
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5→listing — serve starts fine but the stored JWT has expired
- **Evidence:** serve only decrypts the JWT at startup; the first real auth check is fetch_wfm_me (main.rs:1083-1104) which bails '/v2/me returned {status}: {body}' if expired, aborting run_serve before it prints a URL. If /me passes but the token later expires, per-order errors come back as 'WFM HTTP {status}: {msg}' (main.rs:1613) or list_user_orders bails 'WFM HTTP {status}: {body}' (main.rs:1125) → surfaced in the browser as raw text via callCompanion (companion.ts:177-181).
- **Why it's friction:** login's success message says 'Re-run login whenever the JWT expires (months from now)' (main.rs:494), but nothing maps a later 401 back to 'your token expired, run login again.' The user sees a bare HTTP 401 in the orders panel or a startup bail, with no pointer to the fix.
- **Suggested fix:** Special-case 401/403 from /v2/me and order routes into 'Your WFM session expired — run `wfm-fetch-inventory login` again.' both at serve startup and in relayed per-order errors.
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is all accurate and verified: fetch_wfm_me is called at main.rs:765 during run_serve startup BEFORE the URL/token print (main.rs:778-781), so an expired JWT bails at main.rs:1097 before serve becomes usable; list_user_orders bails 'WFM HTTP {status}: {body}' at main.rs:1125; order create returns 'WFM HTTP {status}: {msg}' at main.rs:1613; callCompanion relays the raw error to the browser at companion.ts:177-181; and login.rs success text (main.rs:494) is the only expiry pointer, with zero 401-to-login mapping anywhere in companion/src, prototype/src, or companion/README.md. What the finder slightly overstates is the onboarding relevance: this audit targets the FIRST-RUN journey, and the JWT is freshly minted at step 3 (login) immediately before step 5 (serve), with a documented multi-month lifetime (main.rs:494, companion/CLAUDE.md). Token expiry therefore cannot occur during a genuine first-run session — it is strictly a returning-user problem weeks/months later, not new-user onboarding friction. So the diagnosis is correct but the 'first-run' framing is off; impact is low-frequency. Severity minor is right (arguably polish). Note also the startup-bail message '/v2/me returned 401: {body}' does at least surface the word/status that a savvy user could tie to auth, so it is not a totally opaque failure.

#### [🟡 minor] The whole second half of the product (list/manage WFM orders via login + serve) is invisible to a newcomer — absent from the empty-state stepper and the entire FAQ
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 1 (Discover) / Step 3-5 (the login+serve half) — never surfaced until after inventory is loaded and the user clicks into the Companion tab
- **Evidence:** The empty-state landing's 01/02/03 stepper (App.svelte:901-938) and the dropzone are purely fetch -> drop -> read; grepping the empty-state region (888-957) finds no 'serve', 'login', 'list', or 'push' beyond 'login screen'. The 6-entry FAQ (App.svelte:1500-1577) likewise never mentions that the app can create/edit/delete listings on WFM. The 'List N on WFM' button and the connect panel only exist after phase==='done' inside the sidebar (App.svelte:1442-1481). A user evaluating the tool from the landing has zero signal that order-pushing — a real differentiator over the read-only browse.wf/warframe.me — exists at all.
- **Why it's friction:** Two compounding harms for the newcomer: (a) they cannot tell from the landing that this does more than the read-only competitors, so the strongest reason to adopt is hidden; (b) when they later hit the Companion tab cold, login+serve are prerequisites they were never told to set up, so 'paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' is the first time they learn serve and login are even things. The product's two halves are never introduced as a whole.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a fourth, clearly-optional step or a one-line teaser to the empty state ('Want to push prices straight to warframe.market? After fetch, run `login` then `serve` — see the Companion tab.') and a short FAQ entry covering login -> serve -> connect so the capability is discoverable before the user is blocked on it.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate and verified: the empty-state stepper (App.svelte:900-938), the landing InstallWidget (components/InstallWidget.svelte, install+fetch only), and the 6-entry FAQ (App.svelte:1501-1577) never surface login/serve/order-management; "login" in the empty state refers to the game's login screen (App.svelte:917) and "warframe.market" appears only as the price-data source. The List-on-WFM button and connect panel exist only after phase==='done' (App.svelte:1090, 1442-1481), and the Companion tab assumes prior knowledge of serve ("paste the URL the serve subcommand printed", 1464). There is no README, so no other user-facing surface introduces it. The finder over-rated severity to major. The framing "the whole second half is invisible" overstates the blocking impact: this does NOT block the product's primary journey ("what to sell right now," which CLAUDE.md names as the core value); it is a discoverability/positioning miss for a secondary capability plus a cold-prerequisite annoyance when the user later reaches the Companion tab. The capability IS reachable once inventory is loaded. That is a minor, not a major — it annoys and undersells, but does not block any task the newcomer set out to do.

#### [🟡 minor] The `--passphrase-stdin` escape hatch for the known serve TTY failure is documented only as a Rust doc-comment for 'automation'
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5 (serve) — when serve dies with 'reading passphrase / No such device or address (os error 6)' outside a real TTY
- **Evidence:** ServeArgs exposes `--passphrase-stdin` (companion/src/main.rs:98-101) and run_serve reads the passphrase from stdin when it's set (main.rs:736-739) — this is exactly the fix for the os-error-6 TTY failure called out as observed live pain. But its only description is the `#[arg]` doc-comment 'Read the encryption passphrase from stdin … Useful for automation / systemd units', which frames it as an ops feature, not a recovery path. It appears in no README (companion/README.md documents only fetch), no FAQ entry, the install.sh/install.ps1 'Next steps' (which never mention serve at all), and not in the in-app companion connect panel (App.svelte:1459-1478).
- **Why it's friction:** A newcomer who hits the os-error-6 failure has a working remedy shipping in the same binary but no way to discover it: --help frames it for systemd, and nothing else mentions it. The already-logged finding is that the failure has no detection/help; this is the distinct, sharper point that the cure already exists and is just hidden behind ops-flavored phrasing.
- **Suggested fix:** When serve's interactive passphrase read fails with an ENXIO/os-error-6-class error, print a one-line hint pointing at `echo 'passphrase' | wfm-fetch-inventory serve --passphrase-stdin` (or run inside a real terminal), and reword the flag's help and a FAQ entry to name the no-TTY case explicitly rather than only 'automation / systemd'.
- **Verifier note:** The claim slightly understates the doc gap: companion/README.md does not merely "document only fetch" — it never mentions the serve OR login subcommands at all (README.md:1-100 covers only fetch), so the absence of --passphrase-stdin there is part of a total absence of serve documentation. Otherwise every cited line is accurate.

#### [🟡 minor] Expired saved login surfaces as a raw 'WFM HTTP 401' on the Orders tab with no 'log in again' pointer
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 / returning user — opening Orders or listing after the months-old JWT expires
- **Evidence:** MyOrdersPanel.svelte:67-69 auto-loads /orders on connect; the catch at :58-61 + render at :174 shows 'Couldn't load orders: {error}' where error is the raw companion relay 'WFM HTTP 401: ...' (main.rs:1124-1126 bails with 'WFM HTTP {status}: {body}', companion.ts:177-181 rethrows it verbatim). The companion's own login success print says 'Re-run login whenever the JWT expires (months from now)' (main.rs:494) but that string lives only in the CLI; the browser FAQ (App.svelte:1501-1569) has no JWT-expiry entry.
- **Why it's friction:** This is the FIRST failure a returning user hits, and it is silent until then: serve decrypts the stale JWT fine and prints 'Connected', so the user believes everything is wired up. The error they finally see ('WFM HTTP 401') names no cause and no fix. The one piece of copy that explains expiry (re-run login) is in a terminal they closed weeks ago. Second-order to the already-logged 'expired JWT fails at first listing action' — the orders-tab AUTO-load makes it bite earlier and on a different screen, and the missing-recovery-text is the actual blocker.
- **Suggested fix:** When the companion relay returns 401/403 from any WFM call, have the companion tag it ('jwt_expired') and the browser map that to an actionable banner: 'Your saved warframe.market login expired. In the companion terminal run: wfm-fetch-inventory login, then restart serve.' Add a matching FAQ entry.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence chain verified end-to-end and accurate, with trivial line-number drift: the FAQ snippet is at App.svelte:1496-1579 (finder cited 1501-1569) and confirmed to contain NO JWT-expiry entry; MyOrdersPanel.svelte auto-load $effect is at 67-69, catch at 58-61, render at 174; companion.ts:177-181 rethrows the companion's error string verbatim; main.rs list_user_orders bails 'WFM HTTP {status}: {body}' at 1124-1126 and the /orders route (1017-1021) wraps it as HTTP 502 {error: ...}; main.rs:494 is the login-success 'Re-run login whenever the JWT expires (months from now)' line, confirmed CLI-only. I also confirmed serve never validates the JWT against WFM at startup (it only decrypts it, main.rs:746), so a stale-but-decryptable JWT does present as connected and the 401 first bites on the auto-loaded orders fetch — the 'silent until then' premise holds.\n\nWhat the finder over-rated: severity. This is a RETURNING-user, time-delayed failure ('months from now' per the login copy) — a brand-new user doing first-run onboarding will NOT hit it during the journey being audited. The error is also surfaced visibly in the orders panel and names its source ('WFM HTTP 401'), so it is not a silent or fully opaque failure at the moment it occurs — it just lacks an actionable recovery pointer. For an onboarding/first-run friction audit that argues for minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] Pasting the website URL with a token appended passes URL validation, then dies on a raw JSON SyntaxError
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5→6 — connecting the companion
- **Evidence:** parseCompanionUrl (companion.ts:44-67) only rejects non-http / non-loopback / missing-?token=; 'http://127.0.0.1:5173?token=x' passes all three. pingCompanion (companion.ts:74-78) checks only r.ok, then r.json(). The Vite dev server (and any same-host static site) returns index.html with HTTP 200 for /health, so r.json() throws a 'Unexpected token <' SyntaxError, surfaced raw in the connect box via verifyCompanion catch (App.svelte:719-722, rendered at :1465).
- **Why it's friction:** The already-logged 5173 item is about parse rejection (missing token). This is the harder-to-diagnose sibling: a user who DOES append ?token= to the website URL clears validation and gets a cryptic JS parser error with no mention of ports or serve. Distinct failure path, distinct (worse) message.
- **Suggested fix:** In pingCompanion, check the response content-type / catch the JSON parse and emit a targeted message: 'That URL answered with a web page, not the companion. Make sure you pasted the random http://127.0.0.1:PORT line that `serve` printed — not the website address.'
- **Verifier note:** Nothing material wrong. Evidence verified: parseCompanionUrl (lib/companion.ts:44-67) accepts http://127.0.0.1:5173?token=x (only checks http protocol, loopback host, presence of ?token=); pingCompanion (lib/companion.ts:74-78) checks only r.ok then r.json() with no content-type guard; throw caught in verifyCompanion (App.svelte:719-722) into companionError, rendered raw at App.svelte:1465. Vite SPA fallback returns index.html HTTP 200 for /health so r.json() throws Unexpected token. The placeholder at App.svelte:1471 literally shows ?token= which slightly raises plausibility, but this is a narrower trigger than the already-logged bare-website-URL case (caught by the missing-token check). Severity minor is correct.

#### [🟡 minor] Connect shows green 'Connected' with a wrong/truncated session token because /health is unauthenticated
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5→6 — connecting the companion
- **Evidence:** /health requires no token (main.rs:930-937 returns 200 before the X-Session-Token gate at :943-954). pingCompanion (companion.ts:74-78) only hits /health, so verifyCompanion sets companionStatus='connected' (App.svelte:710-712) and shows the 'fresh' dot + 'Connected' (App.svelte:1443-1448) regardless of token correctness. A wrong token only fails later as 401 on the first real action.
- **Why it's friction:** The connect step's success signal is decoupled from the credential it is supposed to validate. A user who mis-copies the token (easy: it's a 43-char base64 string on a separate line from the URL) is told everything is fine, then hits an unexplained 401 on their first listing or orders load — and won't think to re-check the token because connect was green.
- **Suggested fix:** Have the connect/verify step make one authenticated probe (e.g. GET /orders or a tiny token-gated /whoami) so a bad token fails at connect time with 'Token rejected — re-paste the full line incl. the ?token=… part', not later on an unrelated action.
- **Verifier note:** The finder's mechanism is correct but it missed one nuance that actually strengthens the claim: verifyCompanion does NOT rely on /health alone — at App.svelte:717 it also calls getPendingPlan(), which hits the AUTHED route GET /plan/pending via callCompanion (companion.ts:142-150, 168-181). With a wrong token the companion returns 401 {"error":"missing or invalid X-Session-Token"} (main.rs:948-954); getPendingPlan re-throws it (the /no pending plan|HTTP 404/ test at companion.ts:147 does not match a 401); but verifyCompanion deliberately swallows that throw in its inner best-effort catch (App.svelte:716-718, "a network blip here shouldn't break the connect flow"), so companionStatus stays 'connected'. So a token-validating signal IS produced at connect time and then discarded — not merely "never probed." Also: the URL line the companion prints (main.rs:781) already contains the full ?token=…, and parseCompanionUrl rejects a URL with no token at all (companion.ts:62), so the happy path (copy the whole URL line) is safe; the bug requires the narrower mis-copy of a truncated/wrong token onto an otherwise-valid URL+host. Everything else in the evidence (line refs, fresh dot + 'Connected' at App.svelte:1443-1448, deferred 401 on first action) is accurate.

#### [🟡 minor] Landing stepper teaches a one-shot mental model ('Run it once') that silently contradicts the persistent `serve` process listing-on-WFM requires
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 2 reading the stepper vs Step 5 discovering serve later
- **Evidence:** Step 02's title is literally 'Run it once' (App.svelte:916) and the three-step arc is get -> run once -> drop. But the Companion tab states 'Required to list on WFM' (App.svelte:1439) and requires a long-running `serve` process bound to a random port (main.rs:778-782). Nothing in the stepper, header sub-copy (App.svelte:892-897), or FAQ foreshadows that the headline 'list on WFM' capability needs a separate, persistent background command per session.
- **Why it's friction:** The onboarding sets the expectation that the companion is a one-shot extractor you run and forget. A user who then wants to actually push listings (the feature that differentiates this from a read-only dashboard) discovers a whole second mode — a persistent server, a passphrase prompt, a random port — with no prior mental scaffolding. The 'run once' framing actively mis-sets the model.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a fourth, optional step or a one-line aside in the stepper / header: 'Want to push listings to WFM from the app? You'll also run `serve` (a small local server) — see the Companion tab.' Reframe step 02 so the one-shot fetch and the persistent serve are presented as two distinct modes up front.
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence all checks out: Step 02 title is "Run it once" (App.svelte:916), the 3-step stepper is get->run once->drop with no 4th step (App.svelte:901-938), the header sub-copy (892-897) only mentions dropping inventory.json and ranking sells, the Companion tab says "Required to list on WFM" (App.svelte:1439), serve binds a random port and prints a persistent URL + session token (main.rs:768-782), and the landing FAQ (App.svelte:1496-1578, six entries) never mentions serve or a persistent background process. So the claim is accurate. The finder OVER-rated severity at "major." The one-shot fetch path (steps 1-3) is a fully functional onboarding for the CORE "what to sell" journey — a user reaches the ranked sell table without ever touching serve. The serve/list-on-WFM flow is a secondary, optional capability, and when the user does pursue it the Companion tab (1434-1479) explains serve and shows exactly what to paste. So this is a late-surfacing mental-model/expectation gap that annoys users on the push-to-WFM path, not something that blocks the primary flow. That is minor, not major. (Note: the known live blockers — serve's TTY passphrase failure, website-port vs serve-port confusion, silent ~/Downloads landing — are the genuinely major onboarding pains; this stepper-framing gap is a notch below them.)

#### [🟡 minor] The two listing-related tabs (Companion, My orders) only exist after an inventory is loaded — there is no entry point to set up serve first, and the landing page never hints the WFM-listing capability exists
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5 — trying to connect serve before/without loading inventory
- **Evidence:** The Companion and My-orders nav buttons live inside the `phase === 'done'` shell (App.svelte:1005-1008, 999-1004), which only renders after a successful inventory load (the `{:else}` branch beginning App.svelte:958). The landing state (App.svelte:888-957) shows only steps + dropzone + InstallWidget + FAQ — no mention of listing-to-WFM or the Companion connection panel.
- **Why it's friction:** A user who has just run `serve` and has a URL in hand, but hasn't yet dropped an inventory, has nowhere to paste it — the Companion tab is unreachable. More subtly, a brand-new user on the landing page gets no signal that 'push listings straight to warframe.market' is even a feature, so the product reads as a read-only dashboard until they happen to load a file and notice the tabs. The biggest differentiator over browse.wf/warframe.me is hidden behind a gate.
- **Suggested fix:** Surface the listing capability on the landing page (a line in the header sub-copy or a fourth step), and/or allow the Companion connection panel to be reached pre-load so serve can be wired up independently of inventory.
- **Verifier note:** Cited line ranges are accurate and the behavior holds. One refinement worth noting (does not change the verdict): companionConfig is loaded AND auto-verified on mount independent of inventory (App.svelte:211-213), so a previously-connected user's session is restored in state regardless of inventory — but it still cannot be displayed or acted on, because the entire done-shell (nav buttons 999-1008 plus the Companion connect form at 1436+) renders only under phase==='done', and phase reaches 'done' exclusively via inventory paths (snapshot restore L225, fresh load L295, encrypted import L878). So a first-time user with serve running and no inventory truly has no place to paste the URL. The finder slightly undersells the second prong: beyond the unreachable tab, the landing FAQ (1496-1578) frames the companion purely as the inventory fetcher ('Where does my inventory data go') and never mentions relaying listings to WFM — the core differentiator is invisible until a file is loaded. That is a genuine discovery gap, but it under-sells rather than hard-blocks the flow, so minor is the correct severity.

#### [🟡 minor] Companion-connect input only accepts the full ?token= URL — a user who copies just the host:port (or pastes the two printed lines separately) gets a dead-end validation error
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Connecting the web app to a running serve process
- **Evidence:** main.rs:778-781 prints the address and the token on SEPARATE lines, then a combined 'http://{actual}?token={token}' line. companion.ts:44-67 parseCompanionUrl REQUIRES a parseable URL with a `token` query param: a bare 'http://127.0.0.1:45891' throws 'URL is missing ?token=… — re-paste the full line'; pasting just '127.0.0.1:45891' (no scheme) throws 'Not a valid URL.'; pasting the bare 64-char token alone throws 'Not a valid URL.'. The connect box placeholder (App.svelte:1471) is 'http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…' but the panel copy (App.svelte:1464) says 'paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' without clarifying it must be the THIRD combined line, not the 'Companion listening on…' line a user instinctively grabs first.
- **Why it's friction:** serve prints three address-ish lines; the most prominent ('Companion listening on http://127.0.0.1:PORT') is exactly the one that does NOT carry the token, so the natural copy fails. The error messages are technically correct but the user has to notice there's a separate combined line further down. Each failed paste re-prompts for the JWT passphrase if they restart serve, compounding the known TTY pain.
- **Suggested fix:** Accept a bare host:port plus a separately-pasted token (two fields, or detect a token-only paste and prompt for the URL), or have serve print only ONE copy-this line and label it 'Paste THIS into the web app:'. Alternatively, make the 'URL is missing ?token=' error point at the right printed line ('grab the line that ends in ?token=…, not the "listening on" line').
- **Verifier note:** Cited evidence is all accurate (main.rs:778-781, companion.ts:44-67, App.svelte:1464/1471 verified verbatim), so the behavior claim holds. But the finder overstated impact and missed two in-place guardrails. (1) serve does NOT just print three address-ish lines blindly — main.rs:780 prints the label "In the web app, set the companion URL to:" immediately ABOVE the combined http://...?token=... line, so the correct line is explicitly signposted, not buried. (2) The connect-box placeholder (App.svelte:1471) shows the exact required shape "http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…", and the error for a token-less paste ("URL is missing ?token=… — re-paste the full line.") is a directly actionable correction that steers the user to the only line carrying a token. (3) The "compounding TTY passphrase pain" in why_friction is wrong: a rejected paste leaves serve running — the user just re-pastes; nothing forces a serve restart or a second passphrase prompt. Net: this is real but a recoverable, signposted, self-correcting error, sitting at the low end of minor / borderline polish.

#### [🟡 minor] Both installers' "Next steps" end at the dropzone and never reveal that listing-management (login → serve → connect) exists
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 2→6 transition — the hand-off from install to "now what can I do?"
- **Evidence:** install.sh:101-115 "Next steps" stops at "4. inventory.json lands in ~/Downloads — drop it into the web UI." install.ps1:86-93 has the identical truncation ("4. inventory.json lands in your Downloads folder — drop it into the web UI."). Neither mentions `login` or `serve`. In the app, the My-orders nav item only renders once `companionStatus === 'connected'` (App.svelte:1000-1003) and the Companion tab (App.svelte:1005-1008) is the only entry to connecting — its strip just says "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" (App.svelte:1464) with no definition of serve and no statement that login is a prerequisite.
- **Why it's friction:** The installer is the one moment the product has the user's full attention and a stdout it controls. It sells exactly one capability (drop file → see what to sell) and then goes silent. The second, differentiating half — actually pushing listings to WFM — is gated behind a chicken-and-egg: the My-orders tab is hidden until connected, connecting requires a serve URL, serve requires login, and none of login/serve/the-two-step-sequence is named anywhere the user has been. So a new user has no way to even *discover* that bulk-listing exists, let alone the order to run the subcommands. This is distinct from the logged "login/serve undocumented on WFM" — the gap here is the missing forward-pointer at the exact post-install moment, on both platforms identically.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an optional fifth "Next step" to both installers: "Want to push listings to warframe.market in bulk? Run `wfm-fetch-inventory login` once, then `wfm-fetch-inventory serve`, and paste the printed URL into the app's Companion tab." Mirror that as a one-line teaser in the landing stepper or FAQ so the capability is discoverable before the user has solved the puzzle.
- **Verifier note:** Severity over-rated as major; corrected to minor. All cited evidence is accurate and I confirmed the gap is broader than cited (the word `serve` appears nowhere else in the UI, and the entire in-app Install/FAQ view at App.svelte:1483-1571 plus InstallWidget.svelte contain zero forward-pointer to login/serve/listing — the "Where does my inventory data go?" FAQ even truncates at "~/Downloads" like the installers). But this does not block the product's stated reason-to-exist: the core "what should I sell right now" journey completes fully without ever touching login/serve. Listing-management is the secondary, differentiating capability, and the gap is a missing discoverability pointer (under-selling), not a broken or dead-end path. That is annoy-not-block = minor.

#### [🟡 minor] verifyCompanion runs on every page load against a saved companion URL, surfacing a stale connect error to users who only want to read their sell list
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 1/6 — returning user reopens the app to check what to sell
- **Evidence:** onMount (App.svelte:210-213) calls loadCompanionConfig() then unconditionally `if (companionConfig) verifyCompanion()`. verifyCompanion (705-723) pings the saved baseUrl; serve is almost never still running from a prior session (random ephemeral port, manual Ctrl-C), so the fetch fails and sets companionStatus='error' with the raw fetch failure as companionError (721). That error string then renders in the Companion strip (App.svelte:1465) the moment the user opens the Companion tab.
- **Why it's friction:** Listing via serve is an occasional action; reading the sell table is the everyday one. But the saved companion URL persists in localStorage (wfminv:companion-v1) indefinitely, so every subsequent visit eagerly probes a long-dead loopback port and stores a failure. A user who connected once weeks ago and now just wants the sell list is greeted, on the Companion tab, by a raw browser fetch error (e.g. 'Failed to fetch') attached to a port that legitimately no longer exists — framed as an error rather than the expected 'serve isn't running right now'. The probe also can't distinguish 'port dead' from 'wrong token' because of the no-auth health design above.
- **Suggested fix:** Treat a failed probe of a saved config as the neutral 'companion offline — start serve and reconnect' state, not an error: a dead loopback port on reload is the normal case, not a fault. Reserve companionStatus='error' (red) for genuinely surprising failures, and word it as 'serve isn't running' rather than echoing the raw fetch exception.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate and verified: onMount (App.svelte:213) unconditionally calls verifyCompanion() when a saved config exists; verifyCompanion (705-723) pings the saved baseUrl and on failure sets companionStatus='error' + stores the raw exception in companionError (720-721), which renders on the Companion strip (1465). pingCompanion (companion.ts:74-78) does `await fetch(baseUrl+'/health')`, so a dead loopback port rejects with the browser's raw 'Failed to fetch'/NetworkError as e.message — confirming 'raw fetch exception'. The finder slightly UNDER-stated reach: the error is not confined to the Companion tab. The nav Companion item renders a red 'stale' dot on EVERY view (App.svelte:1007: companionStatus==='error' ? 'stale'), so a returning user who only opens the Sell list still sees a persistent red indicator without navigating anywhere. Severity 'minor' is correct — the sell table and Orders fallback (line 701 routes Orders->Sell when not connected) work fine; this is a trust/cosmetic annoyance, not a functional block.

#### [🟡 minor] Onboarding step 01 anchors the whole companion mental model to 'fetch' — its link target (#companion) and 'Nothing else.' copy positively foreclose login/serve
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 1 (discover/install) — reading the cold-start 01/02/03 stepper
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:905-910 step 01 'Get the companion' body: '...to fetch your inventory from DE\'s own endpoint. Nothing else.' linking href="#companion". The #companion anchor (InstallWidget.svelte:59-66) header says 'Reads the running game\'s process memory to fetch inventory.json ... One command — paste and go.' Neither login nor serve appears anywhere the link leads.
- **Why it's friction:** The single navigational link the new user is invited to follow in step 01 lands them on a section that describes the companion as a one-command fetch tool, and the word 'Nothing else.' is an explicit claim that no further functionality exists. This is more corrosive than 'login/serve are undocumented': the copy actively builds a mental model in which listing-on-WFM cannot exist, so when the user later meets the Companion tab's 'paste the URL the serve subcommand printed' they have no schema to attach it to — they reasonably conclude they pasted the wrong thing or the app is broken.
- **Suggested fix:** Soften step 01 to 'Reads your inventory — and, optionally, lists items on WFM for you' and either point the link at a section that names all three subcommands or add a one-line 'fetch to read, login + serve to list' map. Drop the absolute 'Nothing else.'
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is factually accurate (App.svelte:905-910 has "Nothing else." + href="#companion"; InstallWidget.svelte:59-66 / id="companion" describes only the one-command fetch; neither login nor serve appears there). But the finder overstates impact and mis-rates severity. (1) The 01/02/03 stepper is explicitly the cold-start "get your inventory in" path (App.svelte:900-944), and the whole onboarding's stated goal (header, App.svelte:893-896) is "drop inventory.json -> rank what to sell." Listing-on-WFM is a deliberately separate advanced feature, not a first-run step, so step 01 omitting it is by design, not a defect. (2) "Nothing else." most naturally reads as a TRUST/scope statement about the binary ("reads memory to fetch inventory and does nothing else") — reinforced by the safety FAQ at App.svelte:1501-1517 — not as a claim that the product cannot list items. The finder's "positively forecloses login/serve / user has no schema to attach it to" is a psychological inference, not a behavioral block. (3) The serve flow has its own self-describing entry point: the dashboard companion-strip (App.svelte:1442-1481) literally says "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" with placeholder "http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=..." and companion.ts:42-62 returns explicit paste-correction errors. A user who reaches it is told exactly what to do, undercutting the "concludes app is broken" claim. The genuine onboarding blockers (per the known-pain list: serve TTY passphrase failure os error 6, 5173-vs-random-port confusion, silent ~/Downloads drop) are the real majors here; this copy gap is a discoverability nit. Severity should be minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] Saved companion URL+token is persisted across sessions but the token is regenerated every serve restart, with no copy warning it's single-use-per-process
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5/6 — returning user reconnecting after restarting serve
- **Evidence:** companion.ts:6/17-19 persists {baseUrl, token} in localStorage 'wfminv:companion-v1'; App.svelte:212-213 reloads + verifyCompanion() on every mount; main.rs:769 session_token = random_token(32) is freshly generated each run_serve, and main.rs:781 prints a new http://{actual}?token={token} every time (port is also random per main.rs:770/95-96). On a stale token /health passes auth-free (main.rs:931) but every real route 401s; verifyCompanion only pings /health (companion.ts:75) so it can show 'connected' with a token that fails on the first orders/plan call.
- **Why it's friction:** The connect box says 'paste it once' (companion.ts:2) and the value sticks across refreshes, training the user that connection is durable. But the moment they Ctrl-C and restart serve (after a reboot, a rebuild, or closing the terminal), both the port and the token change, and the saved value is silently dead. Worse, because verifyCompanion only checks the no-auth /health route, the app can show green 'Connected' against an old port/token, then fail opaquely on the first listing action. Nothing in the UI or serve stdout says 'this URL is good only until you stop serve — re-paste after every restart.'
- **Suggested fix:** In serve stdout add 'This URL changes every restart — re-paste it in the app after restarting.' In the app, have verifyCompanion hit an authed route (or note that /health is unauthenticated) so a stale token surfaces as 'reconnect needed' immediately, and label the saved connection 'valid until you restart serve.'
- **Verifier note:** All file:line evidence is accurate (companion.ts:2,6,17-19,75; App.svelte:212-213,705-723; main.rs:769,770,781,931; port default 0 at main.rs:95-96). But the finder over-weights the 'shows green Connected then 401s opaquely' path. That path only occurs when the user passes a fixed --port so the port survives a restart while only the token rotates. On the DEFAULT random-ephemeral port, a restart changes the port too, so the saved baseUrl points at a now-closed port; pingCompanion's /health fetch throws a connection error (companion.ts:76), verifyCompanion sets companionStatus='error' (App.svelte:719-721), and the error is shown in the connect box (App.svelte:1465). So in the common default case the dead connection surfaces visibly on reconnect, not silently-green. The genuine, unmitigated defect is the messaging gap: 'paste it once' (companion.ts:2) plus durable localStorage persistence trains the user that the connection is permanent, while serve stdout (main.rs:778-782) and the UI never say the URL/token is per-process and must be re-pasted after any restart — and restarts are routine because setcap is wiped on every cargo build (companion/CLAUDE.md). That trains durability and wastes a returning user's time, but it is a re-paste annoyance, not silent failure on the default path, so it is minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] Cold-start page hides the entire 'Manage / Companion' nav, so a user who installed specifically to manage WFM listings sees no path to it until they happen to drop an inventory file
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 1/5 — first visit, before any inventory is dropped
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:900-957 the idle/loading branch renders only the stepper, DropZone, InstallWidget, and FAQ. The sidebar containing the 'Companion' nav and 'Manage' group (App.svelte:997-1009) lives in the {:else} branch (App.svelte:958+) that only renders once phase leaves idle (i.e. after an inventory is loaded). The connect panel is therefore gated behind a successful inventory drop.
- **Why it's friction:** Connecting the companion (login+serve) is logically independent of having an inventory loaded — a user could install, log in, and start serve to test the connection before ever running fetch. But the app makes the connect surface conditional on first dropping inventory.json, coupling two unrelated steps. A user whose primary goal is order management has to satisfy the read flow first just to find the connect box, and nothing on the cold-start page hints that managing listings is even possible.
- **Suggested fix:** Expose a lightweight 'Connect companion' entry (or a line in the stepper) on the cold-start page so the listing flow is discoverable without first loading an inventory; or explicitly state on the landing page that connecting requires loading inventory first and why.
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is accurate: phase only becomes 'done' after a successful inventory load (App.svelte:225, 295, 878), and the entire sidebar — Manage group + Companion nav (App.svelte:997-1009) and the connect panel (App.svelte:1434-1481) — lives in the {:else}/phase==='done' branch, so the connect surface is unreachable on cold start. The cold-start stepper (App.svelte:900-944) only describes the fetch flow (`wfm-fetch-inventory`), and neither the FAQ (App.svelte:1496-1580) nor the InstallWidget mentions login/serve/order-management. So the discoverability gap is real.\n\nBut the finder over-states impact in two ways. (1) Its premise that 'connecting is logically independent of having an inventory loaded' is mostly false for the primary payoff: the connect panel's main action, 'List N on WFM', is disabled={results.length === 0} (App.svelte:1456) — listing literally requires loaded inventory. So connect+serve is NOT cleanly decoupled from the inventory step; the dominant order-management action needs inventory anyway. (2) The genuinely inventory-independent feature (viewing existing WFM listings via 'My orders') is doubly gated: it only renders when companionStatus==='connected' (App.svelte:999), which requires the connect panel, which requires phase==='done'. A user whose ONLY goal is to view/edit existing orders with no inventory has no path — but that is a narrow edge case, not the documented inventory-first onboarding journey (the whole product thesis and the 6-step flow are 'drop inventory → what to sell'). There is no dead-end or error: a normal user proceeds through the natural fetch→drop flow and the nav simply appears. This is a polish/minor-boundary discoverability nit on a secondary feature, correctly rated minor (not higher).

#### [🟡 minor] connectCompanion wipes the input before verify runs, so the common serve failure leaves an empty box and a disabled Connect button — no one-click retry
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 5-6 — connect the web app to the serve URL
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:764-776: parseCompanionUrl runs first, then `companionInput = ''` (line 770) clears the box, THEN `await verifyCompanion()` (line 771). When verify fails (serve not running / wrong TTY / port confusion — the documented live pains), companionStatus becomes 'error' but the input is already empty. The Connect button is `disabled={!companionInput.trim()}` (App.svelte:1475), and the only 'Retry' button in the file (line 1615) belongs to pending-plan resume, not to re-running verifyCompanion against the still-saved companionConfig.
- **Why it's friction:** The most likely outcome of a first connect attempt (serve died, wrong port, TTY error) dead-ends: the error shows, the box is blank, the button is disabled, and there is no path to retry the saved URL. The user must re-paste the entire `http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…` line every single time they want to retry — exactly when they're already fighting the serve startup.
- **Suggested fix:** Only clear companionInput AFTER verifyCompanion succeeds (move line 770 into the success branch of verifyCompanion or after the await resolves without error). Add a 'Retry' button in the error state that calls verifyCompanion() against the saved companionConfig without requiring a re-paste.
- **Verifier note:** Cited lines are all accurate (input cleared at 770 before verify at 771; verifyCompanion 705-723 doesn't restore input on failure; Connect disabled at 1475; the only Retry at 1615 calls doResume for plan-resume, not verifyCompanion). The in-panel dead-end is real. BUT the finder overstates "no path to retry the saved URL" and over-rates severity. connectCompanion calls saveCompanionConfig(cfg) at line 769 BEFORE clearing the box, and companionConfig stays set (768); App.svelte:212-213 auto-runs verifyCompanion() against the loaded config on every page mount. So a full page reload retries the saved URL with zero re-paste — the user does NOT have to re-paste "every single time." It's just undiscoverable (the error UI at 1459-1480 doesn't mention it) and a reload drops other app state. Also: the worst documented serve pain (TTY 'os error 6' passphrase failure) happens at serve STARTUP — serve never prints a URL in that case, so it never reaches connectCompanion; the failures that actually hit this flow are serve-died-after-printing / wrong-port / token-mismatch. Downgraded major→minor: a working (if hidden) escape hatch exists and retrying means re-copying a URL still sitting in terminal scrollback, not re-entering data — annoying, not blocking.

#### [🟡 minor] verifyCompanion auto-runs on every page load and surfaces a raw 'Failed to fetch' for returning users whose serve isn't running
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** returning visit after a first session
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:213 (onMount) calls verifyCompanion() whenever a companionConfig is persisted. pingCompanion (companion.ts:74-78) does a bare `fetch(${cfg.baseUrl}/health)` with no AbortController/timeout (grep for AbortController/timeout in lib/companion.ts and App.svelte returns nothing). A dead loopback port yields a connection-refused `TypeError: Failed to fetch`, assigned verbatim to companionError (App.svelte:721) and rendered raw at App.svelte:1465.
- **Why it's friction:** serve binds a RANDOM ephemeral port per run and the user almost never leaves it running between visits, yet the saved config persists. So on a normal second visit the user is greeted with a red error dot and a cryptic 'Failed to fetch' in the companion strip for something they didn't touch — and (per the finding above) no clean retry. It reads like the app is broken rather than 'your serve isn't running / the port changed'.
- **Suggested fix:** Catch the connection-refused case in verifyCompanion and show an actionable message ('Companion not reachable at <port> — the serve port changes every run; paste the new URL `serve` printed'). Treat a clean refusal as 'unchecked/not running' rather than a loud error, and add a short fetch timeout so a wrong-but-bound port doesn't hang.
- **Verifier note:** Cited evidence is all verified: App.svelte:213 auto-runs verifyCompanion() on mount when a config is persisted; companion.ts:74-78 pingCompanion is a bare fetch(/health) with no AbortController/timeout; App.svelte:721 assigns e.message ('Failed to fetch') verbatim to companionError; App.svelte:1465 renders it raw. A dead loopback port does produce TypeError: Failed to fetch. However the finder overstates WHERE the raw string appears. The companion-strip containing line 1465 is inside `{:else if effectiveView === 'companion'}` (line 1434), so the raw 'Failed to fetch' text is ONLY shown on the Companion view. A returning user lands on their last-saved view, defaulting to 'sell' (line 88) — the common case — where they see only a small red dot on the Companion nav item (line 1007: .dot.stale = var(--bad), line 2077), NOT the cryptic string 'in the companion strip'. The raw text surfaces only after the user clicks into Companion (or if their last view happened to be companion/orders). So 'greeted with a cryptic Failed to fetch' is too strong for a normal return visit; 'greeted with a red error dot' is accurate, the raw string is one click away. Severity minor is correct: it never touches the core 'what to sell' view and the user can re-paste the new serve URL in the same Connect box, so nothing is blocked — it's a trust/polish wart, not an impediment.

#### [🟡 minor] Wrong passphrase, expired JWT, and Cloudflare 1015 all surface only at serve startup or first orders call, with errors that don't name the remedy
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 5 — wfm-fetch-inventory serve
- **Evidence:** decrypt_jwt (main.rs:547) returns 'Wrong passphrase, or the JWT file was modified.' which aborts run_serve with no 're-run serve and try again' hint — a single typo kills the whole process. fetch_wfm_me at startup (main.rs:1083-1104) and list_user_orders (main.rs:1106-1129) bail with raw 'WFM HTTP {status}: {body}' on an expired JWT; the browser MyOrdersPanel renders that verbatim as 'Couldn't load orders: WFM HTTP 401 …' (MyOrdersPanel.svelte:58-61,173-174) with no 'your saved login expired — run login again' translation. fetch_wfm_catalog (main.rs:1316-1328) bails '/v2/items returned HTTP {status}' with no mention that a 1015/CF block needs a retry/different network.
- **Why it's friction:** The three credential-class failures a real user hits (typo, months-later expiry, Cloudflare bot block) all produce terse status-code strings that don't tell the user the one concrete next step (re-run serve for a typo; re-run login for expiry; wait/retry for 1015). The expired-JWT case is doubly bad because it only shows up later on the Orders tab as a raw 401, indistinguishable from a transient server error.
- **Suggested fix:** Map known statuses to next steps: on decrypt failure print 'wrong passphrase — re-run `serve` and re-enter it'; on a 401/403 from /v2/me or /v2/orders, bail/relay 'your saved WFM login has expired — run `wfm-fetch-inventory login` again'; on 1015/429 add 'warframe.market is rate-limiting this IP (Cloudflare 1015) — wait a few minutes and retry'. Surface the translated text in MyOrdersPanel instead of the raw HTTP line.
- **Verifier note:** Two citation/framing inaccuracies, but the core claim holds. (1) The exact /v2/me failure string is "/v2/me returned {status}: {body}" (main.rs:1097), not "WFM HTTP {status}" — that literal is only in list_user_orders (main.rs:1125). (2) The why_friction overstates the expired-JWT-as-later-401 angle: fetch_wfm_me runs at serve STARTUP (main.rs:765, before the server binds), so a stale JWT aborts serve immediately with "/v2/me returned 401" and never reaches the browser. The raw-401-in-MyOrdersPanel path (verified: error=e.message line 59, rendered "Couldn't load orders: {error}" line 174) only fires if the JWT expires mid-session after a clean startup — a narrower window than "months-later expiry shows up on the Orders tab." Everything else is accurate: decrypt_jwt msg (547) propagates through run_serve (744) aborting the process with no re-run hint; fetch_wfm_catalog bails "/v2/items returned HTTP {status}" (1327) with no 1015 remedy (1015 is mentioned only in a dev-facing code comment at lines 28-29, never surfaced at runtime).

#### [🟡 minor] README + onboarding stepper teach a 'one-shot, run it again' mental model that is the OPPOSITE of serve's long-lived-daemon lifecycle, with nothing to un-teach it
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5 (serve) — but the damage is done at Step 2/4 when the user forms the wrong mental model
- **Evidence:** companion/README.md:85-86 'It doesn't keep running in the background. One-shot — run it again when your inventory changes.'; App.svelte:916 step header literally reads 'Run it once'; install.sh:108 / install.ps1:90 next-steps run a bare one-shot command. But main.rs:782 'Ctrl-C to stop.' — serve is a blocking foreground daemon that must stay open the entire time the user lists/edits orders. No doc reconciles the two.
- **Why it's friction:** A new user is explicitly told the companion is a fire-and-forget one-shot. When they later reach the Companion-connect panel and must keep a terminal running serve open, that contradicts the only lifecycle model they were ever given. They will close the terminal (job done, it's one-shot, right?), the loopback server dies, and verifyCompanion() flips to error with no clue that closing the window is what broke it. The friction is not 'serve is undocumented' (already logged) — it's that the docs actively plant a FALSE model the user must discover is wrong.
- **Suggested fix:** Distinguish the two lifecycles explicitly: fetch = one-shot (run, exits, drop the file); serve = a server you leave running in a terminal while you list. In the companion README 'What it doesn't do' line, scope 'one-shot' to fetch only and add a sibling note that serve runs until Ctrl-C. In the connect panel, add 'keep that terminal open while you list.'
- **Verifier note:** Evidence all verifies verbatim (README.md:85-86, App.svelte:916 "Run it once", install.sh:108/install.ps1:90 bare one-shot, main.rs:782 "Ctrl-C to stop", and the connect panel at App.svelte:1463-1464 says only "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" with no keep-open hint; verifyCompanion at App.svelte:719-721 surfaces only the raw fetch error). Two framing overstatements: (1) "docs actively plant a FALSE model" is too strong — fetch genuinely IS one-shot, so the README/stepper are CORRECT about fetch; the real defect is that fetch's lifecycle is the ONLY one any doc teaches and serve's daemon lifecycle is documented nowhere except one terminal line. The companion README never mentions serve at all (it is entirely a fetch document), so it does not assert anything false about serve — it is silent. (2) Severity is over-rated as major. This bites only the optional order-LISTING path (Step 5/6), which the advanced user opts into; the PRIMARY "what should I sell right now" journey needs only fetch + drop-file and is unaffected. It degrades a secondary flow, so minor. Also closely overlaps the already-logged "serve is undocumented" punch-list item — the mental-model sharpening is a legitimate distinct nuance but not a new blocker.

#### [🟡 minor] The Companion nav item's only persistent state signal is an unlabeled gray dot that is aria-hidden and has no title — a logged-in user gets no cue that Companion is an unconfigured prerequisite
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Post-load — user is on Sell, scanning the sidebar for what to do next to actually list
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1005-1008 — the Companion nav button renders `<span class="dot {companionStatus === 'connected' ? 'fresh' : companionStatus === 'error' ? 'stale' : ''}" aria-hidden="true"></span>`. In the default `unchecked` state (App.svelte:688) the class string is empty, so it falls to the base `.dot { background: var(--muted) }` (App.svelte:2072) — a neutral gray dot, aria-hidden, no `title`. Compare the 'My orders' nav item which is hidden entirely until connected (App.svelte:999).
- **Why it's friction:** The whole second half of the product (listing/managing WFM orders) hangs off the Companion item, but its un-set-up state is communicated by a single gray dot indistinguishable from a decorative bullet, invisible to screen readers, and with no hover text. There is no 'set up' badge, no '!' affordance, nothing saying this is an incomplete step. A user who loaded inventory has zero pull toward configuring serve; the one entry point looks finished.
- **Suggested fix:** Give the unchecked Companion nav dot a meaningful state: a 'setup' / 'not connected' badge text (like the My-orders count badge) and a `title` such as 'Not connected — run login then serve to list on WFM'. Drop aria-hidden on a dot that is the sole status signal, or pair it with sr-only text.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is fully accurate (verified App.svelte:688 unchecked default, 1005-1007 empty dot class + aria-hidden + no title, 2072 base .dot uses var(--muted) gray, 999 'My orders' hidden until connected; no Sell-view banner/CTA pulls an un-connected user since both list-cta:1084-1091 and pendingBanner require connection). But the finder over-rated this at major and overstates the impact. The Companion nav item is NOT a bare dot — it is a persistently visible, clickable nav button explicitly LABELED 'Companion' in a 'Manage' group (App.svelte:1005-1006). Clicking it immediately surfaces the header 'Companion' with the lede 'Required to list on WFM.' (App.svelte:1437-1439) plus a Connect form. This is a discoverability/polish gap, not a major onboarding blocker. Correct severity: minor.

#### [🟡 minor] serve does two blocking WFM network calls AFTER the passphrase prompt but BEFORE printing any URL — offline / expired-JWT / Cloudflare death wastes the passphrase entry
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 5 (serve → connect)
- **Evidence:** companion/src/main.rs:744 decrypts (prompts passphrase) → :755 fetch_wfm_catalog (?-propagates) → :765 fetch_wfm_me (?-propagates) → only :771 binds the port and :778-781 prints the URL. fetch_wfm_catalog bails raw at :1326-1328; fetch_wfm_me bails raw at :1097 ('/v2/me returned {status}: {body}').
- **Why it's friction:** The whole reason a new user runs serve is to obtain the http://127.0.0.1:PORT?token=... line. But serve front-loads two unguarded network round-trips after the interactive passphrase prompt. If the saved JWT has expired (months later, exactly when a returning user comes back), or WFM is offline, or Cloudflare 1015-blocks the BROWSER_UA, the process dies with a raw 'parsing /v2/me' / '/v2/items returned HTTP 403' error AFTER the user already typed their passphrase and watched 'Loading WFM item catalog…'. No URL is ever printed, so the user can't tell whether they did serve wrong, typed the wrong passphrase, or hit a transient outage. The already-logged items place these failures at the orders tab or describe them generically; in reality expired-JWT and Cloudflare fail at serve STARTUP, pre-bind, which is a different and earlier dead end with a different recovery (re-run login vs. retry).
- **Suggested fix:** Bind the port and print the URL FIRST, then lazily warm the catalog / resolve the username on the first authed request (or in a background thread), so a transient network failure doesn't nuke the whole session before it starts. At minimum, special-case a 401 from /v2/me into 'Your saved login has expired — re-run `wfm-fetch-inventory login`' and a 1015/403 from /v2/items into 'WFM is rate-limiting or unreachable; retry in a minute', instead of dumping the raw status+body.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is exact and verified: passphrase prompt at main.rs:741, decrypt :744, fetch_wfm_catalog at :755 (?-propagates, bails raw at :1326-1328), fetch_wfm_me at :765 (?-propagates, bails raw at :1097), bind :771, URL printed :778-781 — both network round-trips do happen after the passphrase prompt and before any URL, with no 401/1015 special-casing. The :951 `401` the codebase contains is an unrelated incoming-request token check, not startup. Where the finder overreaches is the onboarding framing and severity: a brand-new first-run user has just completed `login`, so their JWT is fresh — the expired-JWT death (the finder's headline 'returning user months later') does NOT hit a first-run user at all; it hits returning users, outside this audit's first-run scope. The offline / Cloudflare-1015 variants are transient retry conditions, not first-run blockers, and the passphrase isn't destructively 'wasted' (re-running serve costs one more passphrase entry, nothing is lost). Real ordering and raw-error-message wart, but minor for onboarding, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] A 409 'plan already running' from a double-submit dead-ends the modal with no wait-and-retry path
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — submitting a listing batch (two tabs, or impatient re-click)
- **Evidence:** Companion returns 409 `a plan is already running; retry after it finishes` (main.rs:1011, 983). callCompanion throws that string (companion.ts:177-181); ListingReviewModal.send() catches it into networkError and sets phase='error' (ListingReviewModal.svelte:115-118). The error screen offers only 'Cancel' and 'Back to review' (lines 286-289). 'Back to review' → re-send will just 409 again until the other plan drains.
- **Why it's friction:** The 409 is a transient, self-healing condition (the other plan finishes in seconds), but the modal treats it like a terminal error. A user with two tabs open, or who clicks Send twice on a slow connection, lands on a red error with no 'this is temporary, wait a moment' framing and no retry-after affordance — re-sending immediately just reproduces it. The pending-plan recovery banner exists for the crash case but not for this concurrency case.
- **Suggested fix:** Special-case the 409 message in the modal: show 'A listing batch is already in progress — wait a few seconds and retry' with a Retry button (not a generic error), and disable the Send button while a submit is in flight to prevent the double-click that causes it.
- **Verifier note:** Two small precisions, neither of which overturns the finding. (1) The finder's worst-case trigger "clicks Send twice on a slow connection" in a single tab is largely guarded: send() sets phase='sending' synchronously (ListingReviewModal.svelte:98) before the await, and the Send button only renders while phase==='review' (line 230 inside the {#if phase === 'review'} block at 163), so Svelte removes the button on the first click — canSubmit (lines 81-85) plays no in-flight role, but the phase-gated render already prevents the same-tab double-submit. The realistic trigger is therefore the TWO-TABS / two-clients case, which the finder also lists and which is genuinely unguarded. (2) Worth noting the 409 path is wider than implied: it fires on both POST /plan (main.rs:1011) AND POST /plan/resume (main.rs:983), so the same dead-end hits the pending-plan-recovery flow too, not just a fresh submit. All cited evidence (main.rs:983/1011, companion.ts:177-181, modal:115-118 and 282-290) is accurate; severity 'minor' is correct — it needs an atypical concurrent-submit setup and the error text is honest ("retry after it finishes"), it just lacks a one-click Retry affordance.

#### [🟡 minor] makeAllVisible failure wipes the results table that recorded which listings were created
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — after a successful batch create, clicking 'Make N visible'
- **Evidence:** ListingReviewModal.svelte:143-146 — on a bulkVisibility throw, the catch sets `phase = 'error'`, which replaces the whole 'results' view (the per-item ✓/✗ table at lines 241-281) with the bare error screen (lines 282-291) showing only networkError.
- **Why it's friction:** By the time the user clicks 'Make N visible', the listings have already been created on WFM (invisible). If the visibility call then fails (network blip, expired JWT, WFM 5xx), the success record of WHAT was created is destroyed by the phase flip — the user is left with a generic error and no list of the order IDs/slugs they just created, so they can't tell which listings exist or retry visibility selectively. The created listings silently persist as invisible on WFM with no in-app trace.
- **Suggested fix:** Surface visibility failures inline within the 'results' phase (a banner + a Retry button) instead of switching to phase='error', so the created-listings table stays on screen and the user retains the record and can retry the visibility toggle.
- **Verifier note:** The code-level evidence is correct (ListingReviewModal.svelte:143-146 sets phase='error' on a bulkVisibility throw, swapping the results table at 241-281 for the bare error screen at 282-291; serverResults survives in state but is no longer rendered, and neither error-screen button — Cancel/Back to review, line 287-288 — re-shows it). But the impact is overstated. The why_friction claim that the created listings "silently persist as invisible on WFM with no in-app trace" and the user "can't tell which listings exist or retry visibility selectively" is wrong: MyOrdersPanel (always rendered, App.svelte:1432) calls GET /orders and lists every listing the user has, with a per-order visible/invisible toggle (MyOrdersPanel.svelte:211-215, title "Click to make visible"). So the recovery path the finder says is missing exists in a sibling panel — the user can see exactly which listings were created and flip each one visible. What is actually lost is the modal's in-context success table at the moment the visibility call fails (an annoyance), not the ability to find or fix the listings. Also note all listings are created invisible by design (visible:false, line 108), so they reach WFM regardless of this bug.

#### [🟡 minor] serve prints 'set the companion URL to: http://127.0.0.1:<random>?token=…' but never warns this port is NOT the website's — and the website is the only place that URL is used
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** User reads serve's stdout, then switches to the browser to connect
- **Evidence:** main.rs:778-782 prints 'Companion listening on http://127.0.0.1:<actual>' and 'set the companion URL to: http://{actual}?token={token}'. The browser app runs on a different port (dev 5173, prod 443). The known live pain is users confusing the two. Neither serve's stdout nor the connect placeholder 'http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…' (App.svelte:1471) says which port belongs to which thing.
- **Why it's friction:** serve's own output is the one moment to disambiguate, and it doesn't. It says 'set the companion URL' without ever clarifying that this loopback URL goes into a field in a DIFFERENT app on a DIFFERENT port — the precise confusion observed live. From the mental-model lens, the user holds two 127.0.0.1 URLs and nothing in either the CLI or the app distinguishes 'the page you're looking at' from 'the thing you paste'.
- **Suggested fix:** In serve's stdout add 'Paste the full line below into the Companion tab of the TennoWorth web app (a different page/port — not this one).' and label the connect field 'paste the companion URL (random port, NOT this site's address)'.
- **Verifier note:** The finder overstated two things. (1) It claims serve's output never indicates the URL belongs to a different app — but main.rs:780 literally prints "In the web app, set the companion URL to:" immediately above the URL line (781). The finder's evidence even omitted the "In the web app" prefix, quoting only "set the companion URL to:". So serve DOES tell the user where the URL goes; what it lacks is only the explicit "different port than this page / not the site you're on" caveat. (2) The browser side also already hints direction: App.svelte:1464 says "paste the URL the serve subcommand printed" and the placeholder at 1471 is "http://127.0.0.1:XXXXX?token=…". So both ends establish CLI-URL → web-app-field. Severity is over-rated: this is not a major blocker. The serve URL is pasted as one opaque blob into a labeled field — the user is not asked to reconcile two ports by hand. The real "5173 vs random port" confusion is about which page to open / connect status, not about this paste step. Downgrade to minor (a wording polish that would reduce a documented but non-blocking confusion).

#### [⚪ polish] The word 'companion' overloads three distinct concepts (the binary, the install section anchor, the connect tab) with no signposting of which is which
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Steps 1, 5, 6 — navigating between install, fetch, and connect
- **Evidence:** InstallWidget.svelte:59 section id="companion" titled 'Install the companion' (about fetch only); App.svelte:1005-1008 sidebar nav item 'Companion' → effectiveView 'companion'; App.svelte:907 step 01 links 'CLI binary' to #companion; DropZone.svelte:62 links 'companion CLI' to #companion. The stepper/dropzone 'companion' links resolve to the install widget, while the sidebar 'Companion' tab is the serve-connect panel — same word, opposite halves of the product.
- **Why it's friction:** A user told 'open the Companion' has no way to know whether that means the install card, the binary on disk, or the connect tab. Clicking an in-stepper 'companion' link jumps to the install widget (fetch docs), while the sidebar 'Companion' tab is the serve-connect panel. A lost user looking for 'where do I connect' is as likely to land on the install card and conclude there's nothing to connect.
- **Suggested fix:** Rename one of the surfaces — e.g. sidebar tab 'Connect / List on WFM' and install section 'Install the CLI' — so each name maps to one job. Keep 'companion' for the binary only.
- **Verifier note:** All cited line numbers are accurate (paths corrected: the components live at prototype/src/components/, not prototype/src/lib/components/). The word "companion" genuinely overloads three concepts: the binary, the install section anchor (InstallWidget.svelte:59 id="companion", titled "Install the companion" at :61), and the sidebar "Companion" tab (App.svelte:1005-1008 → effectiveView 'companion' → the serve/connect panel at :1434-1481). However, the finder overstates the navigation hazard. The two clickable "companion" surfaces are mutually exclusive by render phase and NEVER co-occur on screen: the #companion anchor links (App.svelte:907 stepper, DropZone.svelte:62) only exist on the landing page (phase !== 'done', App.svelte:888-957), where InstallWidget IS rendered on the SAME page at App.svelte:950 — so those anchors are working in-page jumps to the install card, exactly where "get the CLI binary" should point. The sidebar "Companion" tab only exists in the post-load app shell (phase === 'done', App.svelte:958+), which contains no #companion anchor links at all. A user is therefore never presented with a "companion" link and a "Companion" tab that resolve to opposite halves at the same time; each link/tab lands coherently within its own phase. This is a real terminology-hygiene inconsistency, not a navigation trap that strands a new user, so severity is polish, not minor.

#### [⚪ polish] serve's /v2/me failure dumps the entire raw WFM JSON response body to stderr — noisy and at odds with the 'companion never prints' posture
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 5 (serve startup)
- **Evidence:** companion/src/main.rs:1097 `bail!("/v2/me returned {status}: {body}")` and :1103 `anyhow!("/v2/me response shape unexpected: {body}")` both interpolate the full deserialized response Value; list_user_orders does the same at :1126 ('WFM HTTP {status}: {body}').
- **Why it's friction:** companion/CLAUDE.md's 'Companion never prints secrets' invariant is scoped to accountId/nonce/JWT, and the /v2/me body is account metadata rather than the bearer token, so this is not a secret leak. But for a brand-new user the first thing they see when their saved login has gone stale is a wall of raw JSON (ingameName, ids, reputation fields, etc.) printed to the terminal with no plain-language 'your login expired, re-run login' framing. It reads like a crash, not an actionable recovery, and it's the very first serve interaction a returning user has after months away.
- **Suggested fix:** On a non-2xx /v2/me, map 401/403 to a one-line 'Saved login expired or rejected — run `wfm-fetch-inventory login` again' and only print the raw body behind a --verbose/RUST_LOG gate. Apply the same to list_user_orders.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code is accurate: companion/src/main.rs:1097 (`bail!("/v2/me returned {status}: {body}")`), :1103 (`anyhow!("/v2/me response shape unexpected: {body}")`), and :1126 (`bail!("WFM HTTP {status}: {body}")`) all interpolate the full deserialized response Value, and because fetch_wfm_me is called with `?` at startup (:765) inside `main() -> Result<()>` (:113), a stale-login failure surfaces as a single `Error: ...` line on stderr. So the literal claim holds. But the finder's impact rationale describes the WRONG body for its own headline scenario. The "wall of raw JSON (ingameName, ids, reputation fields, etc.)" it warns about is the /v2/me SUCCESS (200) body. On the stale/rejected-login path the finder centers on, /v2/me returns 401/403, and WFM's error response is a small `{...}` error payload, not the account-metadata dump — that prints via :1097, not :1103. The verbose account-metadata leak only happens on the :1103 path, which fires when status IS 2xx but the shape drifted (rare API-drift case), not the everyday stale-login case. So the "first thing a returning user sees is a wall of account metadata" framing is inaccurate. The real residual issue is narrower: a stale login prints a terse `Error: /v2/me returned 401 Unauthorized: {small json}` with no "re-run login" guidance — an actionability/polish gap, not a noisy-dump or secret-posture problem. The finder itself concedes it is not a secret leak, and companion/CLAUDE.md scopes the "never prints secrets" invariant to accountId/nonce/JWT only, so the invariant-conflict framing is rhetorical. Severity should be polish, not minor.

#### [⚪ polish] Companion 'slug mismatch — refusing' rejection surfaces raw in the results Detail column with no explanation
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 5/6 — first bulk-list attempt via the List on WFM modal
- **Evidence:** main.rs:1559-1563 returns `ref low_sell {low}p is more than {3}× our {p}p; likely a slug mismatch — refusing` as a per-item ItemResult.message. ListingReviewModal.svelte:258 renders `{r.message ?? r.order_id ?? ''}` verbatim in the Detail column under a ✗. Nothing defines 'slug mismatch' for the user or tells them what to do.
- **Why it's friction:** This guard fires precisely on a confusing case — the price the app pre-filled (low_sell-based) is wildly below the reference, which usually means the item resolved to the wrong WFM slug. A first-time lister sees a ✗ next to an item with a cryptic 'slug mismatch' phrase and no next step. They can't tell if it's their fault, a bug, or safe to ignore. Because it's the safety net catching exactly the dangerous-resolution case, the worst outcome is the user manually re-lists at the under-price the guard just protected them from.
- **Suggested fix:** In the modal, detect the 'slug mismatch' / 'refusing' message class and render a plain-language line: 'We refused this one — the price looks far below market, which usually means this item matched the wrong listing. Skip it or check the item name.' Don't show the raw multiplier math.
- **Verifier note:** accurate

### `docs` (17)

#### [🔴 major] Still no single 'getting started in 60 seconds' path that names all three subcommands in order — the journey is reconstructable only by cross-referencing four surfaces
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Whole journey (steps 1-6)
- **Evidence:** fetch lives in the cold-start stepper (App.svelte:916-924) and InstallWidget; login appears ONLY in companion stdout (main.rs:493-494); serve appears only as a placeholder string in the Companion tab (App.svelte:1464,1471) which is unreachable until inventory is loaded (sidebar nav renders only in the non-idle {:else} branch, App.svelte:958+). No file enumerates fetch→login→serve as an ordered list. Installers' 'Next steps' (install.sh:101-114, install.ps1:84-94) stop at fetch + drop-in.
- **Why it's friction:** Every other logged item is a local symptom; this is the structural cause. The full mental model — 'fetch to read, log in once, then serve whenever you want to list' — exists in no single place. A user must already understand the architecture to assemble it from CLI stderr, an install widget, a placeholder, and a tab they can't reach yet. There is no canonical 60-second quickstart, so the entire listing half of the product is effectively undiscoverable to anyone who didn't read the source.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a top-level quickstart (README and/or an always-visible app panel) with three numbered lines: 1) fetch → inventory.json, 2) login (once) → encrypted token, 3) serve → paste the printed URL to list. Make the Companion/Connect tab reachable from the cold-start page.
