#### [🟡 minor] companion README's setcap line uses bare ./wfm-fetch-inventory while the binary it just built lives two dirs down in target/release/ (and the installed one in ~/.local/bin)
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** 2 (build → setcap)
- **Evidence:** companion/README.md:24 'sudo setcap cap_sys_ptrace=eip ./wfm-fetch-inventory' and :25 './wfm-fetch-inventory' appear under the 'Run' heading with NO cd/cwd context above them; the Build section at :43-45 places the actual binary at 'target/release/wfm-fetch-inventory'; the installer (install.sh:14,88) places it at $HOME/.local/bin/wfm-fetch-inventory.
- **Why it's friction:** companion/README.md is the canonical Linux run doc for the only path that exists pre-release (build from source). A user who runs `cargo build --release` (cwd = companion/) and then copy-pastes the README's `sudo setcap cap_sys_ptrace=eip ./wfm-fetch-inventory` gets 'setcap: ./wfm-fetch-inventory: No such file or directory' because the binary is at ./target/release/. If they instead run it from the repo root, same failure. The very next line `./wfm-fetch-inventory` also fails to launch. Unlike install.sh (which correctly uses target/release/$BIN_NAME in its fallback message and $DEST/$BIN_NAME in next-steps), the README's relative path matches no real location, so the one-time setcap silently targets nothing and the next fetch still hits Permission denied — sending the user back to square one.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the README's setcap/run paths absolute or match the build output: `sudo setcap cap_sys_ptrace=eip target/release/wfm-fetch-inventory` then `target/release/wfm-fetch-inventory` (matching the Build section), or reference ~/.local/bin to match the installer. Pick one canonical path and use it consistently across README, install.sh, and the in-app snippet.
- **Verifier note:** The cited lines are real (companion/README.md:24-25 use bare ./wfm-fetch-inventory; Build section at :45 places the binary at target/release/), so the path inconsistency exists and the finding is not fabricated. But the finder over-rates it as major and overstates the impact. (1) The README's `## Run` section (lines 10-36) is generic post-install usage written in bare-PATH style — line 18 is `sudo wfm-fetch-inventory` with no `./` at all — not a `cd companion && cargo build` continuation with cwd=companion/. The finder's premise that this README is "the canonical Linux run doc for the only path that exists pre-release" is its own assertion, not how the doc is structured. (2) A botched setcap is a LOUD error (`setcap: ./wfm-fetch-inventory: No such file or directory`), not the "silently targets nothing" the finder claims. (3) The "sends the user back to square one" outcome does not hold because the failure self-corrects on the next run (see existing_mitigation). It is a real doc-polish inconsistency but does not strand a real user, so it is minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] install.sh mv over $DEST/$BIN_NAME silently succeeds while a serve process is still running the old inode — upgrade looks clean but the live serve keeps the old token
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** 2 (upgrade/reinstall) into 5 (serve)
- **Evidence:** prototype/public/install.sh:88 `mv "$TMPDIR/$ASSET" "$DEST/$BIN_NAME"` renames over the destination inode; a running process holds the old inode open, so the rename succeeds with no 'text file busy' error. install.sh:113-114 only warns that the upgrade clears the capability, not that a running serve is now divorced from the on-disk binary.
- **Why it's friction:** A user who keeps `serve` running in one terminal and pipe-reinstalls (or rebuilds) in another gets a clean-looking upgrade. They re-run the documented setcap on the NEW binary and assume everything is current, but the browser is still connected to the OLD serve process holding the OLD random session token and OLD in-memory JWT/catalog. Any 'why didn't my fix take effect' debugging is invisible because nothing signals the split. This is the install-time sibling of the already-logged cargo-build/setcap-wipe-while-serve-running items, reached through a different command (the installer) with no warning in install.sh's next-steps.
- **Suggested fix:** In install.sh's next-steps, add a line: 'If `serve` is currently running, stop and restart it — the upgrade does not affect an already-running server (and its session token changes on restart).' Same note belongs in install.ps1 and the rebuild-companion skill output.
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is accurate and the POSIX mechanism is real: install.sh:88 `mv "$TMPDIR/$ASSET" "$DEST/$BIN_NAME"` replaces the directory entry, a running serve keeps its open text-mapped inode, and no "text file busy" fires (that error is only raised by open(O_WRONLY)/truncate on a running executable, never by rename). install.sh:113-114 indeed warns only about the cleared capability, not about a divorced running serve. The project already treats the sibling case as real and documents the fix elsewhere — .claude/commands/rebuild-companion.md:7-19 detects a running wfm-fetch-inventory and tells the user to restart it after `cargo build` — so the installer is genuinely the one upgrade path missing this note.

What the finder over-weights: real-user impact is thinner than "minor" friction implies. (1) The installer currently cannot upgrade anything — REPO is still the placeholder `OWNER/REPO`, so install.sh:34-42 hard-exits before reaching the mv; the scenario only exists post-publication. (2) It requires a user to keep `serve` persistently running in one terminal AND pipe-reinstall in another AND not restart serve. (3) Most important, it is self-healing: restarting serve is ALREADY mandatory for any upgrade to take effect, so the moment a user wants the new binary's behavior they restart, which dissolves the split. The "invisible debugging" harm is bounded by the fact that the obvious next step (restart serve) is the fix. This is closer to polish than minor.

#### [🟡 minor] Stepper step 02 teaches a bare binary name the installer itself admits may not be on PATH in the same session
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** User copies the `wfm-fetch-inventory` snippet from stepper step 02 right after installing
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:918 snippet is bare `wfm-fetch-inventory`; InstallWidget.svelte:93 installs to ~/.local/bin (Linux) / :99 %LOCALAPPDATA%\wfminv (Windows); install.sh:94-97 explicitly warns '$DEST is not on your PATH' may occur and tells the user to edit their shell rc. The stepper command assumes the happy PATH case the installer admits may not hold.
- **Why it's friction:** The onboarding teaches one invocation ('run wfm-fetch-inventory') across the stepper, the README, and the FAQ, but the install location is not guaranteed on PATH in the same session (Windows PATH change applies only to future shells; Linux needs an rc edit). A new user pastes the taught command, gets 'command not found', and has no in-stepper recovery — the PATH caveat lives only in installer stderr they may have scrolled past.
- **Suggested fix:** Have the stepper/README show the path-qualified form (~/.local/bin/wfm-fetch-inventory) or add a one-line 'command not found? it's at <path>, or open a fresh terminal' note adjacent to the snippet.
- **Verifier note:** The finder slightly overstates "no in-stepper recovery." App.svelte:922 — one sentence below the bare snippet, inside the SAME step 02 — already shows the path-qualified form `~/.local/bin/wfm-fetch-inventory` (in the setcap example), so an attentive Linux user sees the full install path adjacent to the snippet. Also, the installer mitigations are stronger than implied: install.sh:96-97 prints not just a warning but the exact `export PATH=...` fix, and install.ps1:89 explicitly instructs "In a fresh terminal, run: wfm-fetch-inventory" while :81 prints "restart your shell to pick it up" — so a Windows user who follows the installer's own Next Steps gets a working bare invocation (PATH is added permanently at :80). The residual gap is real but narrow: it only bites a user who (a) reads the web stepper instead of installer output, (b) is on a distro where ~/.local/bin isn't already on PATH or hasn't opened a fresh Windows shell, and (c) overlooks the path-qualified form shown one line down. Note ~/.local/bin is on PATH by default on most modern Linux distros (Fedora, Ubuntu 20.04+, systemd ~/.profile), shrinking the affected population further.

#### [⚪ polish] InstallWidget silently routes detected-macOS users to a Linux installer that hard-exits
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 1 — a Mac user copies the auto-selected install command
- **Evidence:** InstallWidget renders only Linux/Windows tabs (InstallWidget.svelte:70-82). On mac detection, detectedOs='mac' and activeOs='mac' (lines 22-25), and commands.mac maps to `curl -fsSL .../install.sh | sh` (lines 42-46). But install.sh:16-19 exits 1 on non-Linux uname with 'This installer is for Linux. For Windows, see the website.' — which never mentions Mac.
- **Why it's friction:** A detected-Mac user sees no Mac tab (so they land on whichever tab activeOs resolves to), copies a command that aborts with a message that doesn't even acknowledge macOS, and gets no pointer to the 'rebuild from source' path the code comment (InstallWidget.svelte:38-41) assumes they'll take.
- **Suggested fix:** Either show an explicit 'macOS — build from source' tab/note in the widget, or have install.sh print a Mac-specific 'no prebuilt binary yet; build from source: cd companion && cargo build --release' message instead of the Linux/Windows-only text.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code evidence is all accurate and I confirmed it (InstallWidget.svelte:22-25, 42-46, 70-82, 85; install.sh:16-19). I even found an extra wrinkle the finder missed: for a mac user the {#if activeOs === 'linux'} guard (lines 91-103) is false, so the {:else} branch renders the Windows/PowerShell helper text underneath the curl command — a second inconsistency. Where the finder is wrong is severity/impact. It rated this 'minor' as if it blocks a real onboarding. It does not: Warframe has no native macOS client (DE ended Mac support; the game runs Windows + Linux/Proton), and the companion works ONLY by memory-scanning the running game process. A 'detected-Mac user' has no game to scan and cannot use the product at all — the broken installer path is a dead-end appended to an already-unusable scenario. So this is confusing-but-harmless UI for a non-viable user: polish, not minor. The bug is real; its impact on a real new user is near-zero.

#### [⚪ polish] No README at repo root — the install widget's 'inspect before piping' / manual-download path points at OWNER/REPO placeholders
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 1 — discover / decide to trust the installer
- **Evidence:** No README* exists at the repo root (ls of root shows none). InstallWidget's manual-download details link to https://github.com/OWNER/REPO/releases/latest (InstallWidget.svelte:109) and install.sh:11 / install.ps1:10 still carry REPO='OWNER/REPO', with both installers correctly bailing 'No public release exists yet' (install.sh:34-42, install.ps1:24-31).
- **Why it's friction:** A security-conscious new user who wants to read a README or grab the binary manually before piping curl|sh finds no README and a dead OWNER/REPO link. The installers fail honestly, but the discovery step offers no canonical landing doc. This is gated on the still-manual repo registration (per memory) so it's expected, but it's a real first-run gap.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a root README covering the install→login→fetch→serve→upload journey and the TTY/port gotchas; replace OWNER/REPO once the repo is registered (guard already tracked in CLAUDE.md open items).
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate at every cited line (no root README; InstallWidget.svelte:109 -> OWNER/REPO; install.sh:11 and install.ps1:10 carry REPO=OWNER/REPO; honest bails at install.sh:34-42 and install.ps1:24-31). One overstatement: the claim says the discovery step "offers no canonical landing doc," but the InstallWidget's manual-download <details> panel (lines 116-118) already tells inspect-minded users the installers are "short, plain-text, and live in this repo at prototype/public/install.sh / install.ps1. Inspect before piping" — so the inspect-before-piping path is partially served; only the manual-binary-download sublink (the OWNER/REPO releases URL) is truly dead. Polish is the correct severity: no public release exists yet so a new user cannot install at all today, making the missing README moot until launch, and the OWNER/REPO swap is already a tracked release gate (CLAUDE.md open items + branding-tennoworth memory).

#### [⚪ polish] Step 02 buries the Linux ptrace setcap requirement as a parenthetical, and never says it must be re-run after every upgrade
- **Platform:** linux · **Step:** Step 2 — first fetch on Linux
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:917-924: the runnable snippet is just `wfm-fetch-inventory` (918); setcap appears mid-sentence in muted text (921-923). The 'setcap is wiped on rebuild/reinstall' fact is documented in install.sh:113-114, ptrace_open_error (main.rs:1803) and companion/CLAUDE.md, but NOT in the web app's step 02 or the InstallWidget (InstallWidget.svelte:91-96 also omits the re-run-after-upgrade caveat).
- **Why it's friction:** A Linux first-timer who runs the bare snippet from step 02 without first running setcap hits Permission denied. The companion's CLI error (main.rs:1796-1804) recovers well, but the web onboarding presents the happy-path command first and the prerequisite as an aside, so the user only learns the ordering by failing. The 'wiped on upgrade' gap means a returning user who re-ran the installer silently loses the capability with no in-app reminder.
- **Suggested fix:** In step 02, show the Linux path as an explicit two-line ordered snippet (setcap line, then run line) the way install.sh:106-108 does, and add the one-line 're-run setcap after any upgrade/reinstall' note that install.sh:113-114 already carries.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate, but the finder over-states impact. setcap is NOT a hidden "aside" — it sits two lines below the command in the same step-02 paragraph (App.svelte:921-923: "Linux: grant ptrace once (sudo setcap cap_sys_ptrace=eip ...)"), so a Linux user reading the step sees it; the claim that the user "only learns the ordering by failing" is too strong. More importantly the failure is fully self-recovering: on PermissionDenied, ptrace_open_error (main.rs:1796-1804) prints the exact setcap line, the run line, AND the upgrade caveat ("re-installing or rebuilding the binary clears the capability — re-run setcap after an upgrade") — plus a ptrace_scope=3 hint. So the user cannot get stuck. This is a documentation-polish nicety (formatting the snippet as an ordered two-liner + adding the upgrade note to the web UI), not a real onboarding blocker. Downgrade minor -> polish.

#### [⚪ polish] Landing step-02 'Run it once' is not OS-aware, so a detected-Windows visitor still reads a bare command plus Linux setcap noise
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Step 2 — landing-page onboarding stepper (separate from the InstallWidget)
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:902-926 hard-codes the 01/02/03 steps as static HTML: step 02 shows `<code>wfm-fetch-inventory</code>` bare and the muted line mixes both platforms ('Windows: no admin needed. Linux: grant ptrace once (sudo setcap ...)'). Unlike InstallWidget.svelte:19-34/91-103, which detects the OS and swaps the Linux/Windows blurb, the stepper has no `detectedOs`/`activeOs` wiring at all (grep for those identifiers in App.svelte returns nothing).
- **Why it's friction:** The two onboarding surfaces on the same page disagree in sophistication: the install widget greets a Windows user with 'Windows · detected' and Windows-only prose, but the numbered hero stepper right above it shows them a Linux `sudo setcap` command they must mentally filter out. For the equal-first-class Windows target this reads as Linux-default with Windows bolted on, and the irrelevant setcap line is exactly the kind of noise that makes a non-technical Windows user think they've missed a required step.
- **Suggested fix:** Make step 02 OS-aware like InstallWidget (reuse the same detection), or at minimum split the muted line so the Windows branch shows only 'No admin needed — run as the same user that's running Warframe.' and hides the setcap clause.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate: the hero stepper (App.svelte:901-938) is static HTML, step 02 (918-924) shows bare `wfm-fetch-inventory` plus a both-platforms muted line including `sudo setcap cap_sys_ptrace=eip` (922), and App.svelte has zero visitor-OS detection (the line-711 `platform` is the companion health platform, unrelated), while InstallWidget.svelte:15-34/91-103 does detect and swap. So the surfaces genuinely differ. But the finder overstates the impact: the setcap clause is NOT unlabeled noise — line 921 explicitly prefixes the two platforms ('Windows: no admin needed. Linux: grant ptrace once...'), so a Windows visitor reads a clearly Windows-tagged sentence first and a clearly Linux-tagged conditional second. That labeling already does most of the disambiguation the suggested_fix asks for, making the 'non-technical Windows user thinks they missed a step' scenario weak. This is presentation/consistency polish, not minor friction; severity dropped minor -> polish. It also ranks far below the real onboarding blockers (serve TTY passphrase failure, 5173-vs-random-port confusion, silent Downloads landing, stale market.json with no timestamp).

#### [⚪ polish] InstallWidget renders no active/detected tab for a macOS visitor — both Linux and Windows tabs appear un-highlighted while a command shows below
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 1 — discover/install via InstallWidget
- **Evidence:** InstallWidget.svelte:23 can set detectedOs='mac' and line 25 sets activeOs=detectedOs. The tablist (lines 70-82) only renders Linux and Windows buttons, with class:active={activeOs === 'linux'} / {activeOs === 'windows'}. When activeOs==='mac', neither button receives .active and neither shows the '· detected' suffix, yet commands[activeOs] (line 45, mac→install.sh) still renders a command in the box below.
- **Why it's friction:** Beyond the already-logged 'Mac users get the Linux installer' issue, the tab UI itself looks broken to a Mac visitor: a command appears under a tab strip where no tab is selected/highlighted, with no 'detected' marker anywhere. It reads like a rendering bug and undermines first-impression trust, separate from the installer-mismatch problem.
- **Suggested fix:** When detectedOs==='mac', clamp activeOs to 'linux' (so the rendered command and the highlighted tab agree) and surface a small 'macOS: build from source / use the Linux path' note, rather than leaving both tabs inactive.
- **Verifier note:** Code evidence is exact and verified (line 23 sets detectedOs='mac'; line 25 activeOs=detectedOs; lines 70-82 render only linux/windows buttons so neither gets .active or '· detected' when activeOs==='mac'; line 45/85 still render the install.sh command). So the finding is real. But the finder over-rated it as 'minor'. macOS is an explicitly unsupported platform (project is Windows + Linux only, memory-scan is PC-only, no Mac binary exists per the line 38-41 comment), the glitch is purely cosmetic (a copyable command still renders, page isn't broken), and it only affects an unsupported visitor on the discovery page before any investment. That is polish-tier, not minor.

#### [⚪ polish] install.ps1 leaves a stray temp file behind on every download/checksum failure
- **Platform:** windows · **Step:** Install — install.ps1 on a flaky network or pre-release (no binary exists yet)
- **Evidence:** prototype/public/install.ps1:20 `$Tmp = New-TemporaryFile` with no try/finally or trap; the `throw` paths at lines 51, 60, 65, 69 all exit before the `Move-Item -Force $Tmp $Bin` at line 73 that would consume it
- **Why it's friction:** $ErrorActionPreference='Stop' means any failure (download 404, missing SHA256SUMS, checksum mismatch, even the pre-release placeholder throw at line 24-31 — wait, that one is before $Tmp) throws and aborts, leaving the New-TemporaryFile artifact in %TEMP% forever. The Linux installer is careful here (`trap 'rm -rf "$TMPDIR"' EXIT`, install.sh:56); the PowerShell port dropped that hygiene. A user who retries a few times during the pre-release window or a flaky download accumulates orphaned tmpXXXX.tmp files. Minor, but it is an asymmetry where the Windows path is sloppier than the Linux one for no reason.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the download+verify+move in `try { … } finally { if (Test-Path $Tmp) { Remove-Item -Force $Tmp } }`, mirroring install.sh's EXIT trap.
- **Verifier note:** The code facts are all correct: $Tmp = New-TemporaryFile at install.ps1:20, $ErrorActionPreference='Stop' at :7, throw paths at :51/:60/:65/:69 all precede the only consumer Move-Item at :73, and there is no try/finally or trap anywhere — versus install.sh:55-56 which does clean up via mktemp -d + `trap 'rm -rf' EXIT`. The asymmetry is genuine. Two corrections: (1) The finder's parenthetical that the pre-release placeholder throw is "before $Tmp" is BACKWARDS — $Tmp is created at line 20, the OWNER/REPO throw is at lines 24-31, i.e. AFTER. So the single most common pre-release failure ALSO leaks the temp file; the finder under-counted the leaking paths. (2) Severity is over-rated as minor and should be polish. The leaked artifact is a tiny New-TemporaryFile (empty on failures that throw before the line-49 download writes into it) sitting in %TEMP% — an OS-managed scratch dir routinely purged by Storage Sense/Disk Cleanup. It produces zero user-visible symptom, blocks no onboarding step, and a real new user will never notice it. It is a code-hygiene asymmetry, not user friction. Ranked by "how much it blocks/annoys a real new user" (the task's stated yardstick), impact is effectively nil.

### `inventory-load` (22)

#### [🔴 major] Returning user with no network is dumped to the cold-start landing page and loses their restored inventory
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Re-opening the app on a later visit (snapshot restore from localStorage)
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:210-230 onMount restore sets inventoryName + resolved.owned from loadSnapshot(), then calls `if (!market) market = await loadMarket()`; on failure the catch sets `phase = 'error'`. App.svelte:888 gates the whole shell behind `{#if phase !== 'done'} ... {:else}<shell>`, so phase='error' renders ONLY the landing page (steps + dropzone + error card at App.svelte:946-948), never the shell. The restored owned-items map is in state but unreachable. market.ts:14-22 only adds the dev hint on the `!r.ok` branch; a true no-network fetch REJECTS first, so the card reads literally 'Error: Failed to fetch'.
- **Why it's friction:** A user who successfully used the app yesterday opens it offline (or while market.json briefly 404s during a cron push) and sees the new-user onboarding wall with a cryptic 'Failed to fetch', as if they'd never used it. Their inventory snapshot is safe in localStorage but the UI hides it. The market snapshot is non-essential to show what they already loaded (owned counts + last prices could render degraded), yet a transient network blip blocks the entire app.
- **Suggested fix:** On the restore path, treat a market load failure as non-fatal: keep phase='done', render the shell from the restored snapshot, and show a dismissible 'couldn't refresh prices — showing last-known market data / offline' banner instead of throwing to phase='error'. At minimum, special-case the no-network TypeError into an actionable message ('No connection — the price snapshot couldn't load; your saved inventory is still here') rather than 'Failed to fetch'.
- **Verifier note:** Wording overstated but mechanics correct.

#### [🔴 major] A valid-JSON wrong file (not an inventory) silently resolves to 0 owned and dumps the user into the full app with no diagnosis
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — drop inventory.json into the web app
- **Evidence:** prototype/src/lib/inventory.ts:24-34 flattenInventory() only yields entries for the TRADEABLE_CATEGORIES keys and never throws on a structurally-wrong object; App.svelte:264-295 loops over zero entries, builds an empty owned Map, and sets phase='done' unconditionally. App.svelte:620 emptyReason returns null when !resolved.owned.size, so the friendly empty-state diagnosis explicitly bails for the zero-owned case.
- **Why it's friction:** A cold-start user can easily drop the wrong valid-JSON file — market.json, an AlecaFrame export in an unexpected shape, or any random JSON. Instead of 'this doesn't look like a Warframe inventory', the app jumps to the full Sell view showing 'owned 0' and a blank table that reads identically to 'you have nothing worth selling'. There is no signal that the file was wrong, so the user concludes the tool is broken or that they own nothing tradable.
- **Suggested fix:** After resolution, if owned.size === 0, treat it as a likely wrong-file case: keep phase on the landing and show a dropzone-adjacent message like 'No tradable items found in <name> — is this really an inventory.json from the companion? Expected keys like Suits/LongGuns/Recipes were missing.' Distinguish it from the genuine all-untradable case.

#### [🔴 major] Error phase hides the stepper AND the dropzone, leaving a dead-end error card with no retry affordance
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — drop inventory.json (any failure: bad file, market/catalog fetch error)
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:900 gates the stepper+DropZone behind {#if phase === 'idle' || phase === 'loading'} — which excludes 'error'. App.svelte:946-948 renders only <div class="card error">Error: {error}</div> for phase==='error'. handleInventory (App.svelte:296-300) and onHiddenPicked (App.svelte:663-665) both set phase='error' on any throw, including a first-load loadMarket()/loadCatalogs() network failure (App.svelte:254-258).
- **Why it's friction:** The very first action a newcomer takes can fail (offline, market.json 404, catalog fetch error, or a malformed file). When it does, the DropZone they were using vanishes and they are left with a bare 'Error: ...' card and no way to drop another file or retry — they must discover that a full page reload is the only recovery. For the make-or-break first interaction this is a hard dead end.
- **Suggested fix:** Render the DropZone (and ideally the stepper) in the error phase too, with the error shown above or inside it as a non-fatal banner, so the user can immediately re-drop. Or add a 'Try another file' button to the error card that re-opens the picker.
- **Verifier note:** The "bad file / malformed file" example is wrong: DropZone.svelte:12-23 catches JSON.parse failures internally, sets its own inline parseError, and only calls oninventory on a SUCCESSFUL parse — so a malformed file leaves the dropzone mounted and fully recoverable, never reaching App's phase='error'. The genuine triggers for the dead-end error card are: (a) loadMarket() (market.ts:15) or loadCatalogs() (resolver.ts:29,32) throwing on a fetch HTTP failure / bad shape — offline, market.json or wfstat-catalog.json 404 — propagating through handleInventory's try (App.svelte:254-258) into its catch (296-300); and (b) a structurally-valid-but-wrong-shape JSON that parses in DropZone but throws inside flattenInventory/resolvePath. The onHiddenPicked path (663-665) is NOT a new-user vector — that button is only reachable from phase==='done'. Net: the architectural claim (line 900 gate excludes 'error'; 946-948 bare card; no retry affordance; reload is the only recovery) is fully accurate; only the malformed-file rationale is incorrect. Severity sits at the low end of major: it requires a fetch failure or wrong-shape file rather than firing on every first drop, and a reload does recover — but it is a true zero-affordance dead end on the make-or-break first interaction.

#### [🔴 major] Dropping a valid-but-non-inventory JSON resolves to 0 owned and renders a totally blank Sell pane with no message
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — open the web app, drop inventory.json in
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:243-301 handleInventory accepts ANY parsed JSON object — there is no shape guard; flattenInventory (inventory.ts:25-35) simply yields nothing for a non-inventory shape, so resolved.owned stays empty and phase becomes 'done'. App.svelte:619-620 emptyReason returns null when `!resolved.owned.size`, and App.svelte:1164-1203 only renders the table (results>0) or emptyReason. With owned=0 there is no results table AND no emptyReason, so the Sell pane shows just the header + a stats strip reading 'Owned 0 / Sellable 0 / Potential 0p' and nothing else.
- **Why it's friction:** A first-timer who grabs the wrong file (the app's own market.json, an encrypted export the importer didn't recognize, a random JSON, or a brand-new/empty account) gets a silent success: green-path UI, zero rows, zero explanation. There is no 'this file doesn't look like a Warframe inventory' message, so they can't tell a wrong-file mistake from 'I genuinely own nothing sellable'. This is distinct from the logged no-match-name-filter case (that operates on a non-empty inventory).
- **Suggested fix:** In handleInventory, after the flatten/resolve loop, detect resolved.owned.size===0 with a non-trivial input and set a dedicated state (e.g. notAnInventory) that renders an empty-state card: 'This file didn't contain any tradeable items — is it really an inventory.json from the companion? (We read the Suits/LongGuns/Pistols/Melee/Recipes/... keys.)' Make emptyReason also fire (not bail) on owned.size===0.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate; only a citation-path nit: flattenInventory is at prototype/src/lib/inventory.ts:25-35 (finder wrote inventory.ts, dropping the lib/ segment). All four logical claims verified verbatim: handleInventory (App.svelte:243-301) has no shape guard and sets phase='done' with empty owned; flattenInventory yields nothing when no TRADEABLE_CATEGORIES key matches (inventory.ts:5-35); emptyReason returns null on !resolved.owned.size (App.svelte:620); render block (App.svelte:1164-1203) shows neither ResultsTable nor an empty card when owned=0, leaving only the always-rendered stats strip (App.svelte:1045-1068) reading 'Owned 0 / Sellable 0 / Potential 0p'. Also confirmed the 'unresolved' hint (App.svelte:1024-1028) does NOT fire here: a non-inventory shape produces zero flatten entries, so resolved.unresolved stays {} and unresolvedSummary is empty — there is genuinely zero diagnostic text. Scope nuance the finder under-stated in the other direction: DropZone.svelte:60-67 ACTIVELY invites dropping foreign exports (AlecaFrame, warframe-api-helper), which raises real-world odds of a shape mismatch resolving to 0 — strengthens the finding. Severity is at the major/minor boundary (a correctly-produced companion inventory.json resolves fine; this only bites on a wrong-file or empty-account input), but the silent green-path success with no diagnostic on a documented foreign-import path justifies major.

#### [🔴 major] Per-surface staleness (Baro / relics / vault / sets) is never surfaced — the single freshness dot keys only on updated_at
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — Baro view, Relic planner, and Vaulted preset
- **Evidence:** csv_to_market_json.py writes a `surface_fetched_at` map per surface and deliberately rides preserved-from-prior data during upstream outages (reconcile(), csv_to_market_json.py:481-512), even logging `WARNING: {name} has been stale for {age.days} days — upstream looks permanently broken` (lines 491-492). But `updated_at` is rewritten every run regardless (line 550). The prototype never reads `surface_fetched_at` (grep finds zero references in prototype/src). marketFreshness keys solely on `market.updated_at` (App.svelte:606-607).
- **Why it's friction:** warframestat 522s intermittently (documented at csv_to_market_json.py:468). When it does, the Baro schedule, relic drop tables, and vault badges silently freeze at last-good values for days-to-weeks while the freshness dot stays green because updated_at refreshed. A new user trusting the Baro countdown or a 'vaulting soon' sell signal can act on weeks-old data with no cue anywhere in the UI. The data to warn them (surface_fetched_at) is already shipped in market.json and ignored.
- **Suggested fix:** Read surface_fetched_at in the Baro card / relic planner / vault badge code and show a small 'schedule data N days old' note (or hide the surface) when the relevant surface's stamp lags updated_at by more than a threshold. The producer already computes and ships the data — the consumer just needs to honor it.
- **Verifier note:** Nothing material wrong — every cited line checks out: surface_fetched_at is written per-surface (csv_to_market_json.py:477-512, emitted at :581), updated_at is rewritten unconditionally every run (:550), the stale WARNING exists (:491-492), the prototype has zero references to surface_fetched_at, and marketFreshness/the single dot key only on market.updated_at (App.svelte:605-611, dot at :1063). One refinement to the finder's framing: the strongest case is Baro specifically, because baroState derives a live countdown from baked voidTrader.activation/expiry (App.svelte:483-484) — preserved-stale Baro data doesn't just go quiet, it renders an actively WRONG 'arrives/leaves in' countdown or a false 'here' badge under a green dot. Relics/vault are softer (a stale-but-plausible value). Severity is genuinely at the major/minor line: the core 'what to sell' surface (live plat in market.items) is CSV-driven and DOES move with updated_at, so this misleads only the secondary Baro/relics/vault views — but the Baro countdown showing wrong times with a green freshness dot is a real trust hit, so major stands.

#### [🟡 minor] Market staleness — the entire stale-data warning is a single aria-hidden color dot with no qualitative word
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — user reads the ranked sell list and trusts the prices
- **Evidence:** Stats strip renders '<dot> Market data' + a neutral relative time (App.svelte:1061-1067). Freshness bucket is computed (App.svelte:605-611: green ≤6h / amber ≤24h / red after) but the dot carrying it is aria-hidden="true" (App.svelte:1063). The text is just 'N d ago' (App.svelte:595-596) with no 'fresh'/'stale' label; there is no banner when red.
- **Why it's friction:** For a tool whose whole value proposition is CURRENT sell decisions, a weeks-stale snapshot is the failure that quietly destroys trust. The sole signal is a tiny color dot — invisible to screen readers and easy to miss for everyone — with no words. This is the in-app form of the known 'silently weeks stale' risk.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a qualitative label next to the time ('fresh' / 'aging' / 'stale (N d)'), drop aria-hidden on the freshness dot (give it an aria-label), and surface a visible 'prices may be outdated' banner when the bucket is 'stale'.
- **Verifier note:** Severity is overstated as 'major'. The claim's specific facts all verify (dot is aria-hidden at App.svelte:1063; freshness bucket fresh/aging/stale computed at 605-611; staleness text is bare relative time at 595-596/1066; no stale banner anywhere — confirmed by grep). BUT a *visible* relative timestamp ('5 d ago', App.svelte:1066) IS rendered next to 'Market data' and is readable by everyone including screen readers — so staleness information is NOT entirely color-only as the prose implies; a sighted user can read '14 d ago' and judge it without the dot. The genuinely missing pieces are narrower: (1) the dot's qualitative verdict is invisible to screen readers (aria-hidden, no aria-label / no fresh/aging/stale word), and (2) there is no attention-grabbing red-state banner. That is an a11y + emphasis polish gap layered on an already-present signal, not the absence of staleness info, and it does not block the core sell-decision flow — minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] market.json load failure surfaces as a generic 'Error: …' card whose only hint is a dev-only Python command
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — drop inventory.json in (first upload triggers market.json fetch)
- **Evidence:** loadMarket throws `Couldn't load market snapshot (HTTP ${r.status}). In dev, run \`python3 scripts/csv_to_market_json.py\` to bootstrap one.` (market.ts:14-19). handleInventory awaits loadMarket inside its try (App.svelte:254-258); any throw lands in catch → `error = e.message` → `phase='error'` → rendered as `<div class="card error">Error: {error}</div>` (App.svelte:946-948). A no-network user (offline, or production host down) gets a fetch TypeError ('Failed to fetch') as the whole message.
- **Why it's friction:** On the user's very first action, a missing/offline snapshot aborts the entire upload with either a raw 'Failed to fetch' or advice to run a Python scraper they don't have and shouldn't need. There is no retry button and no 'check your connection' framing. The inventory they just produced appears to do nothing.
- **Suggested fix:** Catch loadMarket failure distinctly from inventory-parse failure; show an end-user message ('Couldn't reach the price snapshot — check your connection and retry') with a Retry button, and drop the csv_to_market_json.py hint from any user-facing build (keep it console-only).
- **Verifier note:** Code behavior is described accurately (market.ts:14-19 throw with the dev Python hint; App.svelte:254-258 awaits loadMarket in handleInventory's try; catch at 296-299 sets error=e.message/phase='error'; rendered at 946-947 as a bare "Error: {error}" card with no retry). But the severity is over-rated. The finder frames this as a routine first-run failure ("first upload triggers market.json fetch" → "the inventory they just produced appears to do nothing"). It is not routine: market.json is COMMITTED to the repo (git ls-files prototype/public/market.json, 1.5 MB) and ships same-origin under prototype/public/, so on any working build fetch('/market.json') returns 200 and this path is never hit. The error only triggers on infrastructure failure — offline/host-down (which produces a TypeError 'Failed to fetch' BEFORE the !r.ok branch, so the Python hint never even shows — the user gets raw 'Error: Failed to fetch') or a 404/500 from a broken deploy (only then does the Python hint reach an end user). Both are genuine UX gaps (no retry, no offline framing, hint not DEV-guarded), but they are conditional on a degraded environment, not the default new-user path — that's minor polish, not a major onboarding blocker. The market.json staleness sub-concern (raised in the prompt's known-pain list) is a separate issue not actually in this claim.

#### [🟡 minor] Stale market.json has no qualitative warning — a red dot marked aria-hidden is the entire signal that prices are weeks old
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — reading 'what to sell' off possibly-old prices
- **Evidence:** The freshness UI is `<span class="dot {marketFreshness}" aria-hidden="true"></span> Market data` + neutral relative time (App.svelte:1062-1066). marketFreshness buckets green≤6h/amber≤24h/red after (App.svelte:605-611) but the bucket is conveyed only by dot color, which is aria-hidden. The text is just '29 min ago' / '3 d ago' with no 'stale'/'outdated' word and no banner. When updated_at is missing entirely, the dot is 'unknown' and the text is '—'.
- **Why it's friction:** The product's whole claim is 'what to sell RIGHT NOW' vs browse.wf/warframe.me. If the cron silently wedges (commit history shows snapshots can lag), a user makes real plat decisions on weeks-old prices with no louder cue than a small colored dot they may not notice and screen-reader users cannot perceive at all. This is the known 'silently weeks stale' risk, unmitigated.
- **Suggested fix:** Promote red/amber to a visible textual label or banner ('Prices last updated 18 d ago — may be outdated') above the Sell table, and remove aria-hidden from the dot (give it an aria-label) or add an sr-only freshness phrase.
- **Verifier note:** Severity overstated as "major"; it is minor. The staleness IS surfaced as visible plain text right beside the Sell stats — marketStaleness renders "3 d ago" / "18 d ago" via the {marketStaleness ?? '—'} span (App.svelte:1066), and the red dot does flip for >24h data (App.svelte:610, .dot.stale background var(--bad) at App.svelte:2077). So a sighted user is not fed silently-wrong data; the age is present, just neither loud nor labeled with a qualitative word. The genuine gaps are (a) no 'stale/outdated' qualifier or banner and (b) the dot is aria-hidden="true" (App.svelte:1063) so screen-reader users get no freshness cue at all — these are an emphasis/accessibility polish defect, not a major blocker. Minor nit: the claim says when updated_at is missing the dot is 'unknown' — true (App.svelte:606) but there is no matching .dot.unknown CSS rule (only fresh/aging/stale exist at App.svelte:2075-2077), so that dot renders with no distinct color, slightly weaker than the claim implies.

#### [🟡 minor] market.json load-failure recovery text is dev-only ('run csv_to_market_json.py'), a dead end for a hosted-site end user
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — first paint / any session where the snapshot fetch fails
- **Evidence:** market.ts:14-19 throws 'Couldn\'t load market snapshot (HTTP {status}). In dev, run `python3 scripts/csv_to_market_json.py` to bootstrap one.' This is the only recovery instruction, and it assumes a local repo checkout + Python. On the production target (tennoworth.app) the realistic causes are a transient CDN error, an offline client, or a half-deployed snapshot — none fixable by running a Python script.
- **Why it's friction:** market.json is load-bearing: without it the entire 'what to sell' product is blank. The single piece of guidance on its failure path addresses the maintainer, not the new user who just installed everything and is staring at an error card telling them to run a build script they have never heard of. No retry, no 'check your connection', no 'try again in a minute'.
- **Suggested fix:** Branch the message by environment: keep the csv_to_market_json hint behind import.meta.env.DEV; for production show an end-user message ('Market data couldn\'t load — check your connection and reload; if this persists the snapshot may be redeploying.') plus a Retry button that clears the module cache and re-fetches.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is fully accurate (market.ts:14-19 verbatim; the message reaches the end user unmodified via App.svelte:228 setting error=e.message and rendering it raw at App.svelte:947 `Error: {error}`; no import.meta.env branching exists anywhere in src/; no retry for this path — the Retry at App.svelte:1615 is for plan-resume, unrelated). But the finder over-rated severity as 'major'. A major onboarding blocker must impede the typical new user on the normal path. This does not: market.json is committed and co-deployed as a 1.5MB static same-origin asset (prototype/public/market.json), so on a healthy hosted site the fetch succeeds and the product is NOT blank. The error only appears on a transient/edge failure — CDN blip, half-deploy, or offline client (no service worker, confirmed, so offline reload does hit it). Consequence is a confusing-but-non-destructive error card on a reloadable page. The maintainer-oriented text and absence of a retry/connection hint are a real UX defect, but a minor/polish one given the low reachability — not major. Suggested fix (DEV-gate the script hint, add end-user copy + Retry) is sound.

#### [🟡 minor] FAQ "How current are the prices?" hard-asserts a 2-hour refresh, actively reassuring users when data is silently weeks stale
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — user questions whether the prices driving their sell list are current
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1536-1543 — the only FAQ entry on freshness states 'A GitHub Actions cron job scrapes warframe.market every 2 hours and commits a fresh market.json' as unconditional fact, and explains the dot (green<6h/amber<24h/red>24h). There is no FAQ entry for 'the dot is red' or 'prices look out of date', and no runtime check that the cron actually ran — marketFreshness (App.svelte:605-611) is derived purely from market.updated_at, which is whatever the last successful bake wrote.
- **Why it's friction:** The known failure mode is market.json going weeks stale with no loud warning. A user who notices odd prices and opens the FAQ — the natural help destination — is told prices refresh every 2 hours, which is exactly the wrong message when the pipeline is down. The FAQ converts a real staleness incident into false confidence. The whole product pitch is current sell decisions, so this is a trust-critical mismatch, not cosmetic. Distinct from the logged 'red-dot is aria-hidden' items, which are about the visual cue; this is the textual help actively contradicting the stale state.
- **Suggested fix:** Reframe the FAQ answer conditionally and add a 'What if the data looks old / the dot is red?' entry: explain the cron CAN stall, that the red dot means >24h with no refresh, and that the displayed 'Market data · X ago' is the source of truth — not the 2h cadence. Ideally surface a one-line banner when marketFreshness==='stale' rather than relying on a collapsed FAQ.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate: App.svelte:1535-1543 states the 2h cron as unconditional fact, marketFreshness (605-611) is derived purely from market.updated_at, and there's no FAQ entry or banner for a red/stale state. However, the finder overstates impact by calling it "major" and implying the staleness is silently reassured-away. The actual snapshot age IS rendered on-screen next to the dot — App.svelte:1066 shows `{marketStaleness ?? '—'}` ("3 d ago", "2 w ago", etc.) right beside "Market data". So the source-of-truth age is always visible in the stats strip; the FAQ is a secondary help page consulted only if a user is already confused. The mismatch is a real trust/copy bug (the FAQ should say the cron CAN stall and point to the displayed age), but it is not a blocker or major-severity item because the truthful signal is not hidden — it is shown, just without a loud warning. The dot being aria-hidden (a separately-logged issue) weakens the signal for screen-reader users, but the text age is not aria-hidden. Downgrade to minor (copy/trust polish).

#### [🟡 minor] Market freshness dot reflects only the cron run timestamp, not the age of the data behind any surface — preserved-on-outage data shows green
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — read 'what to sell' / market freshness signal
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:599 marketStaleness and App.svelte:605-611 marketFreshness are derived solely from market.updated_at. csv_to_market_json.py:550 rewrites updated_at on EVERY run, and its own comment at lines 578-581 says 'updated_at refreshes every run even when a surface is riding on preserved prior data — these stamps [surface_fetched_at] say when each surface was actually fetched successfully.' The reconcile() preserve-on-outage logic (lines 468-487, STALE_DAYS=7) can keep relic_rewards/vault_status/set_to_parts frozen for days. grep confirms the browser never reads surface_fetched_at anywhere in prototype/src.
- **Why it's friction:** The whole pitch is current sell decisions, and the only freshness cue the user has is a dot that can be green while the Relics/Sets/Vaulted surfaces (and, on a stalled scrape, even prices) are a week stale. The truthful per-surface staleness is computed and shipped in market.json but thrown away by the UI. This is a second-order layer beneath the already-logged 'staleness signalled only by an aria-hidden dot': even when you DO notice the dot, it can lie green.
- **Suggested fix:** Read surface_fetched_at in market.ts/App.svelte and compute freshness per surface; degrade the relevant view's badge (Relics/Sets/Vaulted) when its surface is older than ~24-48h, and add a tooltip on the Market-data dot listing the oldest surface age. At minimum, drive the dot off the OLDEST of {updated_at, min(surface_fetched_at)} so a frozen surface can't read green.
- **Verifier note:** The core mechanism is accurately evidenced and verified: App.svelte:599 (marketStaleness) and :605-611 (marketFreshness) derive solely from market.updated_at; the dot at App.svelte:1063 is driven only by marketFreshness; csv_to_market_json.py:550 rewrites updated_at every run; reconcile() (lines 481-512, STALE_DAYS=7) can freeze relic_rewards/vault_status/set_to_parts/path_to_info/baro on preserved prior data; surface_fetched_at is shipped (line 581) but absent from the Market type (types.ts:67-81) and grep-confirmed never read in prototype/src. So the dot can read green while vendor surfaces are days stale.

Two corrections to scope/severity: (1) The claim's parenthetical 'and, on a stalled scrape, even prices' overreaches. Prices come from wfm_results.csv into items{} (lines 514-547) and are NOT subject to this reconcile() preserve-on-outage path — only the five warframestat-sourced surfaces (path_to_info, set_to_parts, relic_rewards, vault_status, baro) are frozen by reconcile. A stalled price scrape is a different failure mode. (2) Severity major is too high. The trigger is bounded: it only fires during a warframestat upstream outage (the 522s noted at lines 468-475), the healthy 2h cron stays correctly green, and it degrades the secondary Relics/Sets/Vaulted/Baro surfaces, not the primary sell-table prices. The finder itself frames this as a second-order layer beneath an already-logged dot-visibility finding. Real and worth fixing, but minor — not a blocker to a new user reading the sell table.
