#### [⚪ polish] No explicit 'loaded inventory.json (N items)' confirmation after upload — the only echo that the right file was picked is the sidebar filename pin
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — confirming the file just picked from Downloads is the correct one
- **Evidence:** On a successful parse the app sets phase to done and jumps to the Sell view; the loaded file is reflected only as `inventoryName` in the sidebar `src-pin` (App.svelte:1019-1023). There is no toast, banner, or 'Loaded inventory.json — 2,175 items, 405 sellable as of <file mtime>' confirmation tying the upload action to the file. The Sell stats strip shows Owned/Sellable counts (App.svelte:1045-1053) but never labels them as 'just loaded from <filename>'.
- **Why it's friction:** A user hunting in ~/Downloads may have several inventory.json copies (re-fetched on different days, or a stale one from a prior session). The weak feedback loop means they can load the wrong/old file and never notice — the app jumps to a confident ranked sell list regardless, and the only disambiguator is a small filename in the sidebar with no timestamp of the inventory's own age relative to 'now'.
- **Suggested fix:** On load, show a brief confirmation (toast or banner) naming the file and its owned/sellable counts, and surface the inventory's saved/loaded time more prominently than the small `saved <ago>` pin. Consider warning if the picked file's mtime is days old.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate. On a successful drop, handleInventory (App.svelte:250-295) sets inventoryName = name, lastUpdated = Date.now(), phase = 'done', with no setView call so it lands on the default 'sell' view (App.svelte:88). The only file echo is the src-pin <strong>{inventoryName}</strong> (App.svelte:1020); the Owned/Sellable stats (App.svelte:1045-1053) are not tied to the filename, and grep confirms no toast/load-confirmation banner exists (the only .pending-banner is for order batches, App.svelte:1583/2464). So the finder is factually correct.

Two corrections to the finder's framing: (1) Severity is overstated at minor — every datum needed to confirm the load IS already on screen (filename pin + visible Owned count + a delta column that highlights count changes vs the prior snapshot, ResultsTable.svelte:142/380-382, surfaced via the Replace tooltip 'Counts that changed will be highlighted', App.svelte:1030). The failure is only that these aren't bundled into one explicit message — a polish-grade packaging gap, not a real onboarding blocker. The 'wrong file' scenario also requires the user to ignore both the visible owned count and the filename pin. (2) The finder under-credited that delta mitigation and overstated impossibility of the fix: the suggested 'warn if mtime is days old' is only partly applicable — inventory.json carries no fetch timestamp, and the existing 'saved {inventoryStaleness}' pin actually shows ago(lastUpdated) where lastUpdated = Date.now() at load (App.svelte:292,600), i.e. it always reads ~'0 m ago' right after a drop and reflects app-load time, not the inventory's true age — so today there is genuinely no inventory-age signal, which strengthens the finder's point but is a separate, sharper bug than the one titled.

#### [⚪ polish] "Market data 29 min ago" exposes no absolute snapshot timestamp anywhere, so a newcomer can't verify freshness or judge a borderline/stale snapshot
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 (read what-to-sell) — the freshness cue in the loaded-view stats strip
- **Evidence:** prototype/src/App.svelte:1061-1066 the "Market data" stat shows only the relative `marketStaleness` (e.g. "29 min ago") plus an aria-hidden color dot, and unlike its sibling stats it carries NO `title=` attribute (the Replace/Export/Clear buttons and many other elements do — see 1030-1032). The FAQ entry (App.svelte:1535-1543) explains what the dot colors MEAN but never surfaces the actual `market.updated_at` date. The only place an absolute date appears is `new Date(pendingPlan.started_at).toLocaleString()` at 1623, which is unrelated.
- **Why it's friction:** For a tool whose whole pitch is "prices right now," a newcomer has no way to confirm the relative claim or to reason about a red/amber state — "3 d ago" gives no date to cross-check against a known WFM crash or a Baro arrival, and there's no hover to reveal the real timestamp. This is the verification gap behind the already-logged "silently weeks stale" risk: even a user who notices the dot has nothing concrete to act on. Polish because the relative time is usually adequate when fresh.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a `title={new Date(market.updated_at).toLocaleString()}` to the Market data stat cell (and ideally to the inventory "saved" line at 1021-1022) so hovering reveals the absolute snapshot time, matching the title-on-hover convention already used across the loaded view.

#### [⚪ polish] FAQ 'How current are the prices?' documents the freshness DOT thresholds in collapsed-by-default copy, but the dot it describes is aria-hidden and the relative-time text carries no qualitative word — so the one explanation can't actually be reached from the cue
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Post-load — user glances at 'Market data · 29 min ago' and wants to know if it's trustworthy
- **Evidence:** The freshness dot (App.svelte:1063) is `aria-hidden` with no title; its meaning is explained only inside a `<details>` FAQ entry (App.svelte:1535-1543: 'green if under 6 h, amber under 24 h, red after'). The FAQ lives on the Install/FAQ view and the cold landing page — not adjacent to the Sell-view stats strip where the dot renders.
- **Why it's friction:** The only legend for the color code is one collapsed FAQ accordion on a different view. A user looking at a red dot on the Sell view has no in-context way to learn 'red = prices are stale', and the relative-time text ('29 min ago' / could equally be '3 weeks ago') gives no fresh/stale verdict on its own. The explanation exists but is unreachable from the place the cue appears — a discoverability gap distinct from the already-logged 'dot is aria-hidden' note, because here the issue is the legend's LOCATION.
- **Suggested fix:** Put the threshold legend where the dot is: a `title` on the dot ('green <6h, amber <24h, red older') and/or a qualitative word next to the time ('fresh' / 'stale'). Don't rely on a collapsed FAQ on another view to decode a status indicator.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is all verified and correct: the dot at App.svelte:1063 is aria-hidden with no title; .dot CSS (2068-2077) adds no tooltip; the time text at 1066 is a bare relative string from ago() (599); the threshold legend lives only in the collapsed <details> at 1535-1543, and faqContent() renders on the landing (952) and install (1489) views, never on the sell view (1039-1068). The finding is also genuinely distinct from the prior aria-hidden note (that one is about screen-reader access; this is about legend LOCATION for sighted users). What the finder over-states is the user impact. The dot is a redundant at-a-glance accent on top of an already-legible signal: the relative-time text itself. "29 min ago" vs "3 weeks ago" is the strongest possible freshness cue and needs no color legend to interpret — a real user judges trustworthiness directly from the time string. So the unreachable legend decodes a decorative redundancy, not the actual freshness information, which is always present in plain words at 1066 (and again in plain language in the empty state at 1174). That makes this polish, not minor — there is no real point where a user is blocked from judging freshness.

#### [⚪ polish] A market.json missing its updated_at renders a neutral dot + em-dash with zero 'freshness unknown' signal
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — reading 'what to sell' from the stats strip
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:606 `if (!market?.updated_at) return 'unknown'`; the dot is rendered `<span class="dot {marketFreshness}">` (App.svelte:1063) but CSS defines only `.dot`, `.dot.fresh`, `.dot.aging`, `.dot.stale` (App.svelte:2068-2077). There is NO `.dot.unknown` rule, so the 'unknown' bucket falls through to the bare `.dot` base style (a generic neutral dot). marketStaleness also returns null → renders `—` (App.svelte:1066).
- **Why it's friction:** A new user who loads a market.json built by an older/partial pipeline run (or a half-written file that lost updated_at) sees a neutral dot and a `—` where the timestamp should be. There is no word, color, or warning telling them freshness is UNKNOWN — it reads like a cosmetic blank, not a 'do not trust these prices' state. This is strictly worse than the already-logged stale-dot problem because the 'unknown' state has no distinct visual at all. The whole product pitch is current sell decisions; an unknowable-freshness snapshot looks identical to a healthy one minus a timestamp.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a `.dot.unknown` rule (e.g. hollow/grey with a question mark) and make marketStaleness render a literal 'freshness unknown' string instead of `—` when updated_at is absent. Better: refuse to show a confident ranked table when updated_at is missing, with a one-line 'this snapshot has no build timestamp — prices may be arbitrarily old' banner.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code is accurate (App.svelte:606 returns 'unknown'; :1063 renders the dot class; :2068-2077 define only .dot/.fresh/.aging/.stale with no .dot.unknown; :1066 renders marketStaleness ?? '—'). But the finder over-rated severity (major) and overstated two things. (1) No shipped pipeline ever produces a market.json without updated_at: both generators write it unconditionally (csv_to_market_json.py:550 and wfm_demand.py:294 use datetime.now()), and the committed prototype/public/market.json has it. A new user does not hand-build market.json — the app ships its own and refreshes via cron. The 'unknown' bucket is essentially dead code on the onboarding path, triggered only by a corrupt/truncated file. That makes the real-user impact near-zero, not major. (2) The claim that the unknown state 'looks identical to a healthy one minus a timestamp' is wrong: the bare .dot base style is grey (background: var(--muted), App.svelte:2072), which is visually distinct from the green glowing .dot.fresh — so there IS a color difference, just no word. The finding is a legitimate missing visual-polish case (no worded 'unknown' state, no .dot.unknown rule) but ranks as polish, not major, because the triggering input is not produced by any documented/new-user flow.

### `what-to-sell` (24)

#### [🔴 major] Score-explainer formula doesn't match the scores it explains (median-clamp divergence)
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — reading the ranked Sell table and trying to verify the score
- **Evidence:** Banner copy (App.svelte:1154-1155): Score = `min(owned, vol_48h / 2) × low_sell`. But scoreRow() uses clearingPrice(), not low_sell (sell-priority.ts:68-69), and clearingPrice clamps a too-cheap ask UP to the 90d median (sell-priority.ts:58-59). Observed live: Meso W5 Relic shows Score 70 with Own 37, Vol 14, Low sell 3 — the stated formula = min(37,7)×3 = 21, but the table shows 70 (median ~10 drove the clamp). Confirmed by DOM eval: only divergent row in page 1, off by 3.3×.
- **Why it's friction:** The differentiator is a trustworthy sell-score. A skeptical new user does the one arithmetic the banner invites — Low sell × a couple of sales — and on real top-ranked rows (relics, troll-undercut mods) the number doesn't reconcile. A score you can't reproduce from its own published formula reads as either a bug or hand-waving, undercutting the exact trust the tool is selling over browse.wf/warframe.me.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the banner formula honest about the clamp: say `min(owned, vol_48h/2) × clearing price`, where clearing price = lowest live ask, sanity-clamped to the 90-day median when the ask is a troll undercut or lone fantasy ask. Or add a one-line 'why this differs from Low sell × Vol' note on rows where clearingPrice != low_sell.
- **Verifier note:** Severity major is correct; the only correction is that the finder understated the spread of the wrong formula. It is published in TWO user-facing places, not one: the dismissable banner (App.svelte:1155, "min(owned, vol_48h / 2) × low_sell") AND the per-column "?" tooltip for the Score header (ResultsTable.svelte:132, same string "min(owned, vol_48h / 2) × low_sell"). A user who clicks "?" to double-check the banner gets the same wrong formula reconfirmed, so the "hand-waving" impression is reinforced rather than resolved. Quantitatively, the divergence is ~1% of priced rows (26 of 2621 in current market.json), but it concentrates exactly where it hurts: clamping a cheap troll-undercut ask UP to median inflates the score, floating those rows toward the top of the Score-sorted table — i.e. the rows a skeptic inspects first. The cited live example reproduces exactly from prototype/public/market.json: meso_w5_relic has low_sell 3, vol 14, median_now 10 → clearingPrice 10 → min(37,7)×10 = 70 (matches observed Score 70), while the banner formula gives min(37,7)×3 = 21 (3.3× off).

#### [🔴 major] Relics dominate the top of 'Sell' while the Relic planner says crack them — two unreconciled verbs for the same items
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — first read of the default Sell list vs. the Relics tab
- **Evidence:** Default Sell view ranks Neo M1 Relic #2 (score 203, own 29), Neo N8 #4 (152), Meso W5 (70) — relics get a full sell_score (computeResults includes them, App.svelte:303-409). The Relics view (App.svelte:1266-1311) ranks DIFFERENT relics by expected plat per crack: live it showed Meso G1 / Meso O2 / Meso P1 — none of the Sell-view top relics appear. ListingReviewModal accepts rows with a `subtype` (ListingReviewModal.svelte:49,108), so 'List N on WFM' would queue relics for sale.
- **Why it's friction:** A newcomer's single biggest 'sell' recommendation (29× Neo M1 Relic) is an item the app elsewhere tells them to crack, and the two surfaces don't even agree on which relics matter. Selling intact relics at ~7p each is almost always worse than cracking them, yet the Sell view presents it as the #2 best move with no cross-reference. Worse, the one-click 'List N on WFM' CTA can action it. This actively misleads on the highest-value rows — the opposite of 'measurably better at what to sell'.
- **Suggested fix:** On relic rows in the Sell view, show a 'relic — see planner' pill linking to the Relics tab, and/or compare sell_score against the relic's expected-plat-per-crack and suppress/flag the row when cracking wins. At minimum exclude relics from the 'List N on WFM' default selection.
- **Verifier note:** The code-level evidence is all accurate and verified. Minor caveats, none of which change the verdict: (1) The specific relic names/scores in the evidence (Neo M1 #2 score 203, Meso G1/O2/P1 in the planner) come from one live inventory I can't reproduce, but the producing mechanism is fully confirmed and market.json carries real relic avg prices (up to 50p, e.g. axi_p2_relic), so the numbers are plausible — treat them as illustrative, not as fixed repo facts. (2) The two surfaces ranking 'different relics' is inherent to the two formulas, not a bug per se: Sell sorts relics by sell_score = units_today x clearingPrice (sell-priority.ts:65-75, type-agnostic; default sortKey 'sell_score' ResultsTable.svelte:50), while the planner sorts intact-only relics by expected-plat-per-crack epp (relic-planner.ts:54,95). They legitimately measure different things — the real defect the finder nails is that neither surface tells the user the other verb exists for the same item. The 'List N on WFM' / ListingReviewModal path is confirmed: rows={results.slice(0,50)} (App.svelte:1648) includes relics, every row defaults include:true (ListingReviewModal.svelte:51), and subtype is shipped to the companion (line 108).

#### [🔴 major] Relic planner hard-caps at 3 cards out of 145 owned relic types, with no total count and no 'show more'
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — opening the Relics tab to decide what to crack
- **Evidence:** deriveRelicPlan defaults to limit=3 and App.svelte:525 calls it as deriveRelicPlan(resolved.owned, market, 3); relic-planner.ts:96 does candidates.slice(0, limit). The view lede (App.svelte:1269) renders 'Top {relicPlan.length} relics you own…' which prints 'Top 3 relics', and the nav badge (983) shows {relicPlan.length} = 3. There is no pagination, no 'show more', and no 'of N' count anywhere in the relics view (App.svelte:1266-1321). Observed live: the loaded inventory owns 145 distinct intact relic types, yet exactly 3 relic-card elements render and the badge reads '3'.
- **Why it's friction:** The Relics tab is one of the three differentiating 'what to crack/sell now' surfaces. Silently showing 3 of 145 — discarding ~98% of the decision surface with no indication that more were considered or how many — both undersells the tool's depth and erodes trust: a user with a big relic stash cannot answer 'which of MY relics is worth cracking' because the planner only reveals the top 3 and never says there are more. Unlike the Sell table (which paginates and shows 'N rows'), here the cap is invisible.
- **Suggested fix:** Raise the cap and paginate like the Sell table, or render all ranked relics with a collapsible 'show 142 more' control. At minimum, change the lede to 'Top 3 of 145 relics you own, ranked by expected plat per crack' so the truncation is honest, and add a 'show more' affordance.
- **Verifier note:** The "145 distinct relic types" figure is an observed-session number, not grounded in any code constant — only the hardcoded cap of 3 (App.svelte:525, relic-planner.ts:44/96) is verifiable in-repo. The structural claim holds regardless: any user owning more than 3 relic types hits an invisible cap. Minor nuance the finder understates: candidates are sorted descending by epp (relic-planner.ts:95) before the slice, so the single highest-value crack IS surfaced — the user can still act on the #1 pick. The harm is loss of depth and the inability to browse the full ranked stash plus the dishonest "Top 3" lede with no "of N", not a total inability to get a recommendation. Severity major is correct (silently discards the bulk of a core differentiating surface with no indicator and no expansion affordance, unlike the Sell view which shows results.length at App.svelte:1052/972).

#### [🔴 major] Set-completion recommendations tell the user to spend plat to flip a set with zero liquidity/volume check, unlike the relic planner which does warn
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — opening the Set picks tab and acting on a 'buy the missing part, sell as a set' recommendation
- **Evidence:** deriveSetRecos computes near-complete net_plat = setLowSell − missingCost purely from market low_sell with no volume reference (set-recos.ts:79,95,116-132); the SetReco shape carries no vol/moving field (set-recos.ts:32-44) and the Sets card markup renders none (App.svelte:1213-1264). By contrast deriveRelicPlan tracks moving_count via MOVING_THRESHOLD=5 (relic-planner.ts:19,66) and the relic card surfaces '{moving_count}/{total_rewards} rewards moving' with a bad-text warning (App.svelte:1289-1291). Observed live in Set picks: 6 cards, none mention vol/moving/liquid/trades/patience; top card reads 'Complete Okina Prime +38p … Buy Blade + Blueprint for 17p, sell as a set for 55p'.
- **Why it's friction:** This is the only recommendation in the whole app that asks the user to SPEND real plat, and it does so on the unverified assumption that the assembled set will clear at low_sell. Low-demand weapon sets (e.g. Okina Prime) can trade a few times a month, so the advertised +38p may be unrealizable for weeks — the new user buys parts and gets stuck holding a set nobody is buying. The relic surface explicitly guards against this exact 'gold expected value, dead market' trap; the set surface, where the downside is real plat spent, has no equivalent guardrail, which is both a trust hazard and an internal inconsistency.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a liquidity signal to deriveSetRecos mirroring the relic planner: pull the set entry's vol (and/or the missing parts' vol) from market.items and render a 'moving'/'thin'/'patience' badge on the set card, or suppress/deprioritize near-complete flips whose set vol is below a threshold. At minimum show the set's 48h volume next to the +Np net so the user can judge whether the flip will actually clear.
- **Verifier note:** The structural claim is fully accurate and verified line-by-line: deriveSetRecos uses only low_sell with no volume reference (set-recos.ts:79,95,116-132), SetReco carries no vol field (set-recos.ts:32-44), the Sets card renders no liquidity signal (App.svelte:1213-1264), and the relic planner does guard via MOVING_THRESHOLD=5 / moving_count with a bad-text badge (relic-planner.ts:19,64-66; App.svelte:1289-1291). The `vol` data is present and populated on set entries (types.ts:18; e.g. reaper_prime_set vol=25, akbronco_prime_set vol=32 confirm genuinely thin sets exist), so the omission is a real inconsistency, not a missing-data excuse. One correction: the finder's headline live example 'Okina Prime' is a POOR illustration of the dead-market trap — okina_prime_set actually has vol=515 (515 trades/48h), i.e. very liquid, so that specific card would clear fine. The trap is real only for the thin-vol subset of recommended sets, not the example cited. Also note recos are sorted by net_plat desc, which tends to float pricier/more-liquid sets toward the top, somewhat (not fully) limiting exposure. Severity major stands but sits at the lower end of major for these reasons.

#### [🔴 major] "List N on WFM" acts on the unfiltered results, not the rows the user filtered in the table (pill chips + name filter live only inside ResultsTable)
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6→act — clicking the List CTA after narrowing the table
- **Evidence:** The name filter (ResultsTable.svelte:52) and the peak/hold/patience/vaulted/aug pill filter (ResultsTable.svelte:67 activePills) are component-local $state that never propagate to App.svelte. The List CTA and review modal operate on App-level results: App.svelte:1090/1455 label "List {Math.min(results.length,50)}", and the modal is fed rows={results.slice(0,50)} (App.svelte:1648). So filtering the visible table to e.g. "peak 88" then clicking "List 50 on WFM" stages the top 50 of the full 405-row set — not the 88 peaks on screen.
- **Why it's friction:** This is the moment the tool turns insight into action — the payoff. A user curates "only peaks" or types a name to target a specific batch, hits List, and the review modal silently contains different items (the global top-50). They either catch it and lose trust, or miss it and post listings they never intended. The button count ("List 50") matches the global results length, not the filtered count they're looking at, so even the label gives no warning.
- **Suggested fix:** Lift the name + pill filters to App.svelte (or have ResultsTable emit its filtered/sorted row set upward) so the List CTA and ListingReviewModal stage exactly what the table shows. Failing that, label the button "List top 50 (all rows)" and disable/relabel it whenever a table-local filter is active.
- **Verifier note:** x

#### [🔴 major] Empty-state diagnosis ignores the preset/tag/vault filters that actually zeroed the table, so it blames the wrong thing and offers a fix that can't work
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — reading 'what to sell' after one-click switching to a non-default preset (Vaulted/Trending) or clicking a tag chip
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:619-640 emptyReason only walks price/owned/type/kept. But computeResults applies four more exclusions the diagnosis never accounts for: vaultOnly (App.svelte:323-326), preset minVol (330-331), preset minMedian (336-337) and activeTags (315-320). The Vaulted/Trending/Sets presets and every tag chip are one click away in the preset row (App.svelte:1072-1107).
- **Why it's friction:** A new user with no vaulted primes clicks the prominent 'Vaulted' preset and gets a blank table whose card says e.g. 'N sellable items are under 5p average — lower the price threshold' (or owned/type/kept). That is a flatly wrong explanation: the rows were dropped by vaultOnly, not price. The 'differentiator' view actively misleads about why it's empty at the exact moment the user is trying to trust the tool. Same for Trending (vol/median floors) and any tag chip selection.
- **Suggested fix:** Extend emptyReason to count the preset clauses (vaultOnly/minVol/minMedian) and activeTags the same way computeResults does, and add empty-state branches: 'You own no vaulted/vaulting-soon prime parts' (with a 'Back to Default' button), 'Nothing clears the Trending liquidity floor', 'No rows carry the X tag (clear chips)'. When the cause is a preset, the recovery action should reset the preset, not nudge a price slider that won't change anything.
- **Verifier note:** Confirmed accurate. emptyReason counts only price, owned, type, kept; computeResults also drops rows via vaultOnly, minVol, minMedian and activeTags. For the Vaulted preset all four counters are zero so the empty card shows a wrong 0p price message with a no-op button. The tag-chip path is partly mitigated by availableTags chip counts; the preset clauses are not.

#### [🟡 minor] Dropzone hint sends the new user to the wrong directory for inventory.json
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — open the web app, find and drop inventory.json
- **Evidence:** DropZone.svelte:63-64 says the companion "extracts inventory.json from your running game and saves it next to itself"; but companion/src/main.rs:6 writes to "the user's Downloads folder", and App.svelte:920 ("Writes inventory.json to your Downloads folder") and FAQ App.svelte:1523 ("to your ~/Downloads") both correctly say Downloads. "next to itself" implies ~/.local/bin (the install target).
- **Why it's friction:** This is the single piece of copy physically attached to the action the stuck user is performing — locating the file to drop. It actively misdirects them to the binary's directory instead of ~/Downloads, at the exact moment they are hunting. It is the in-app amplification of the known "lands in ~/Downloads with no pointer" pain: not just absent guidance, but wrong guidance that contradicts every other surface in the app.
- **Suggested fix:** Change DropZone.svelte:64 to say the file is written to the Downloads folder (Windows: %USERPROFILE%\Downloads, Linux: ~/Downloads), matching main.rs:6 / App.svelte:920 / FAQ:1523. Ideally name the exact path so the user can paste it into the file picker.
- **Verifier note:** Two corrections. (1) File path is wrong: DropZone.svelte lives at prototype/src/components/DropZone.svelte, not prototype/src/DropZone.svelte. The cited lines (63-64) and the verbatim text "saves it next to itself" are correct, and the contradicting references at main.rs:6, App.svelte:920, and App.svelte:1523 all check out. (2) Severity is over-rated as major. The finder ignored that the fetch subcommand prints the authoritative, exact, correct path on every successful run: main.rs:207-208 emits "Wrote <out_path.display()> (N bytes)" where out_path defaults to <Downloads>/inventory.json (resolved at main.rs:246-252). So the user who just ran the companion in a terminal already has the correct absolute path in their scrollback. The dropzone hint is genuinely wrong copy and should be fixed, but it is one of several pointers — the CLI's own success line (correct) and three other in-app surfaces (correct) all point to Downloads. It is misleading-but-redundant copy, not the sole and authoritative pointer, so minor rather than major.

#### [🟡 minor] Stale market data is signalled only by an aria-hidden color dot with no qualitative word or warning banner
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — reading the ranked sell list and trusting the prices
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1061-1067 renders the freshness as a neutral relative-time string (marketStaleness, e.g. "29 min ago") plus a single status dot. The dot is the ONLY fresh-vs-stale distinction and it is marked aria-hidden="true" (App.svelte:1063). The bucket logic (App.svelte:605-611) computes fresh/aging/stale but that label is never shown as text — only as the dot's CSS class. There is no banner, no "prices may be outdated" copy when the snapshot is weeks old.
- **Why it's friction:** The entire product promise is "what to sell RIGHT NOW" — sell decisions made against three-week-old prices are wrong and erode trust silently. A red dot is the whole warning, it's invisible to screen readers, and the neutral "X d ago" text carries no judgement a newcomer can read at a glance. This is the in-app face of the known "market.json silently weeks stale" risk: the warning exists but is far too quiet for a decision tool.
- **Suggested fix:** When marketFreshness === 'stale', surface a visible labelled warning (text like "Prices may be outdated — last refreshed N days ago") not just a dot color; remove aria-hidden from the indicator or add an aria-label conveying the freshness bucket; consider a dismissible banner at the top of the Sell view when stale.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate and verified: App.svelte:1063 marks the freshness dot aria-hidden="true", the marketFreshness bucket (605-611) is applied only as a CSS class with pure-color styling (2075-2077: var(--good/warn/bad)), and the only adjacent text is the neutral relative-time string (1066). No banner or "outdated" copy exists. However the finder slightly overstates two things. (1) The signal is not "the dot is the whole warning" with zero text — the relative-time string "X d ago" sits right beside it and does carry readable information; a stale snapshot literally says e.g. "21 d ago", which a careful sighted user can judge. (2) The finder missed an existing partial mitigation: a FAQ accordion at App.svelte:1535-1543 ("How current are the prices?") documents the exact color code (green <6h, amber <24h, red after). So for sighted users — the overwhelming majority — a red dot + relative-time text + documented legend is a workable signal, which drops this below "major". The legitimate, unmitigated defect is the accessibility gap (aria-hidden removes any screen-reader text alternative for the freshness bucket) plus the absence of a judgement word/banner at decision time in the Sell view. That is a real trust/a11y issue but minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] A no-match name filter dead-ends to a blank table body with no message and no clear-filter affordance
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — narrowing the sell list by typing an item name
- **Evidence:** The name filter is applied in ResultsTable.svelte:240 (results.filter(r => (r.name||r.slug).toLowerCase().includes(f))). The header still prints "{sorted.length} rows · sorted by …" (ResultsTable.svelte:305), and the body {#each paged as r} (ResultsTable.svelte:352) has NO {:else} branch — so zero matches render an empty <tbody> with no text. App.svelte's friendly emptyReason diagnosis (App.svelte:618-640) only accounts for price/owned/type/kept exclusions and bails when results.length>0 upstream — it never fires for the downstream name filter.
- **Why it's friction:** A user who fat-fingers a name or searches for something they don't own sees "0 rows · sorted by Score" over a blank table with no explanation and no button to clear the filter — a confusing dead end mid-task. Lower rank than the misdirection/staleness issues because it's recoverable (clear the box) and only hit on a typo, but it's a rough edge in the core flow.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an {:else} empty-row state to the ResultsTable tbody (ResultsTable.svelte:352) that says no items match the name filter and offers a clear-filter button; or surface the active name filter in the empty-state diagnosis.
- **Verifier note:** File path is slightly wrong: the component lives at prototype/src/components/ResultsTable.svelte, not prototype/src/.../ResultsTable.svelte as the bare filename implies — but all cited line numbers match exactly (filter at 240, header "0 rows" at 305, {#each paged} with no {:else} at 352, closing {/each} at 437). The App.svelte emptyReason claim is also correct and slightly understated: ResultsTable is only mounted when results.length > 0 (App.svelte:1164-1165), and emptyReason returns null whenever results.length > 0 (App.svelte:620), so the friendly diagnosis is a *sibling* of the table that structurally cannot fire while the table — and thus the name filter — is active. Two additional confirming details the finder missed: (1) the pager is gated on sorted.length > pageSize (line 441), so a no-match also shows no pager, leaving just "0 rows" over pure blank; (2) the filter <input> (lines 284-289) has no clear button — manual deletion is the only recovery. One mild over-statement: the header DOES update to "0 rows · sorted by …", which is a (weak) signal that the filter excluded everything, so it's not entirely message-less.

#### [🟡 minor] 'Potential' headline stat is the metric the tool itself labels 'not realistic'
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — the stats strip is the first big number above the ranked table
- **Evidence:** Stats strip shows 'Potential 12,289 p' as the prominent headline (App.svelte:1054-1060), summing potential_plat = rec.count × m.avg (App.svelte:402, totalPotential App.svelte:614-616). The column-level help for that very metric calls it 'Optimistic — selling N copies usually clears below the average … upper bound, not realistic' (ResultsTable.svelte:130).
- **Why it's friction:** The whole pitch is that naive owned×avg overstates and sell-score is the honest answer (sell-priority.ts:1-8). Yet the single large plat figure a new user reads first is owned×avg — the disclaimed number. There is no headline sum of sell_score (the trustworthy metric) anywhere. A newcomer anchors on '12,289p' as 'what my account is worth to sell', the exact misconception the product exists to correct.
- **Suggested fix:** Lead the stats strip with a realistic aggregate (sum of sell_score, framed as 'est. plat/day' or a clearing-priced total), and either drop 'Potential' from the headline or label it 'optimistic ceiling' inline so the big number matches the thesis.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is fully accurate and verified verbatim (App.svelte:402 potential_plat = count×avg; :614-616 totalPotential reduce; :1054-1060 bare "Potential N p" headline with no tooltip; ResultsTable.svelte:130 same metric labeled "upper bound, not realistic"; sell-priority.ts:1-8 states owned×avg overstates and sell_score is the honest answer). There is genuinely no headline sum of sell_score. But the finder over-rated severity at "major." Two facts soften it: (1) the view header lede at App.svelte:1042 already reads "ranked by sell score," and the table IS sorted by sell_score with it as a first-class column, so the trustworthy metric is the dominant on-screen surface, not absent; (2) the headline word is "Potential," a hedged term — not "Net worth" or "Account value" — which is a weaker anchor than the claim frames it as. This is a framing/anchoring inconsistency, not a broken or deceptive flow; the correct metric sits one column over. minor is the right rating.

#### [🟡 minor] The only inline sell-score formula is dismiss-once-forever; the differentiator's explanation can vanish permanently after one stray click
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — first read, then any later session
- **Evidence:** Score-explainer renders only when `!scoreExplainerDismissed` (App.svelte:1151), and dismissScoreExplainer writes localStorage SCORE_EXPLAINER_KEY='1' permanently (App.svelte:99-104). The × is right next to the table; once clicked it never returns. The sole remaining explanation is the per-header `?` popover (ResultsTable.svelte:324-341), which requires knowing to click the tiny circle.
- **Why it's friction:** The sell-score IS the product. A new user who clicks the × to clear the banner (a near-reflex with dismissible cards) permanently loses the one piece of copy that explains why this tool beats raw avg-price sites — with no menu/help entry to bring it back. The legibility advantage is one accidental click from gone for that browser, for good.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the dismissal session-scoped rather than permanent, or add a persistent 'How scoring works' affordance (a small link in the Sell header or a help icon next to the Score column header that reopens the banner) so the explanation is always recoverable.
- **Verifier note:** The factual mechanics are correct (App.svelte:99-104, 1151; the dismissal is permanent per-browser; grep confirms no reopen path exists). But the finder overstates "the sole remaining explanation is the per-header ? popover which requires knowing to click the tiny circle." It is not the sole remaining surface: the Score column header also carries a native hover tooltip via title={HELP[col.key]?.text} (ResultsTable.svelte:320), so hovering the header reveals the same explanation text without any click. And the popover content (HELP['score']) duplicates the banner's formula — no unique copy is lost, only the prominent first-run framing. So the explanation is recoverable two ways on the very same column, not "one accidental click from gone with no recourse." Severity minor is right (borderline polish), not higher.

#### [🟡 minor] Headline stats (Sellable / Potential) silently rescope to the active preset, with no label and physically detached from the control that changes them
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — reading 'what to sell' after inventory loads, while exploring the preset pills
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1045-1068 renders the stats strip (Owned/Sellable/Potential/Market data) ABOVE the presets row (App.svelte:1070-1092). `results` is the preset-FILTERED output of computeResults (App.svelte:308-337 apply minPrice/vaultOnly/minVol/minMedian per active preset), and the strip binds Sellable={results.length} (1052) and Potential={totalPotential} where totalPotential sums `results` (614-616). Observed live: Default → Sellable=405 / Potential=12,289p; click Vaulted → Sellable=17 / Potential=69p; click Trending → Sellable=217 / Potential=6,871p. The Sell nav badge {results.length} (972) swings identically. No stat has a tooltip (verified: all four .stat title attributes null) and the view header still reads 'Sell — Items in your inventory worth listing right now'.
- **Why it's friction:** A first-run user clicks a preset to explore (e.g. 'Vaulted' or 'Trending') and the single biggest headline number — Potential, the thing you'd screenshot or anchor on — collapses from 12,289p to 69p with no explanation. The labels 'Sellable' and 'Potential' read as inventory-wide totals, and the rescoped value sits above and apart from the preset button that caused it, so the cause→effect is invisible. The user is left thinking their whole inventory is worth 69p, deflating the exact value prop the tool exists to prove.
- **Suggested fix:** Either keep the headline stats inventory-wide (compute Sellable/Potential from the unfiltered owned×market join, independent of the active preset) and show the filtered count only inside the table toolbar ('217 rows' already lives there), OR add a scope label to the strip when a non-Default preset is active (e.g. 'Sellable (Vaulted): 17' / 'Potential in view: 69p') plus a tooltip on each stat. The cleanest is to decouple the headline (always whole-inventory) from the in-table count.
- **Verifier note:** Severity over-rated: this is minor, not major. The first-run/landing state uses the 'default' preset (App.svelte:131), which is inventory-wide, so the headline numbers are correct and impressive on arrival — the deflation only occurs AFTER the user actively clicks a narrowing preset (Vaulted/Trending), and is fully recoverable by clicking back to Default. The numbers are also technically accurate for the active scope, not wrong data. It is a real clarity/polish gap (no scope label, stat physically above the control that changes it, no tooltips — all verified), but it does not block reading 'what to sell' nor produce misleading actionable rows; the table content matches the stat scope. Also note the suggested_fix is partly wrong: it claims a '217 rows' count 'already lives there' in the table toolbar, but ResultsTable.svelte renders no total row count (grep for rows.length/filtered.length in the template returns nothing) — only per-pill chip counts (ResultsTable.svelte:87-94). Minor evidence nit: the view header reads 'worth listing right now, ranked by sell score' (App.svelte:1042), not exactly 'worth listing right now'.

#### [🟡 minor] Default preset — the view every new user lands on — renders 14–15 columns and buries the differentiator signals (Vol 48h, Δ90d, Demand, Trend) off-screen behind horizontal scroll
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — first look at the ranked table

The other four presets (ducats/trending/sets/vault) all narrow to 6–8 columns. In the live screenshot only ~6 columns fit (Item, Own, Score, Avg, Low sell, Top buy) with the table clipped mid-"Tr[end]" and a horizontal scrollbar; Vol 48h, Δ90d, Demand, Ducats, Raw value, Potential are all off-screen. Wrap uses overflow-x:auto (ResultsTable.svelte:486).
- **Why it's friction:** The pitch over browse.wf/warframe.me is liquidity- and timing-aware selling: volume, 90-day trend, buyers-vs-sellers. On the default landing preset those exact columns are invisible without discovering horizontal scroll, so a first-time user sees what looks like any other price table (name + avg + low sell). The unique value is one curated-preset click away, but nothing tells the newcomer that — the strongest evidence for the product's reason to exist is hidden by default.
- **Suggested fix:** Give the Default preset an explicit, curated `columns` list that keeps the signal columns (sell_score, low_sell, volume_48h, delta_90d_pct, ratio) on screen at common widths, matching the discipline the other four presets already follow. Move the long-tail columns (potential, raw_value, ducats, p/100d) into their dedicated presets or behind a column toggle.
- **Verifier note:** Two factual overstatements. (1) The finder says "the table clipped... Vol 48h, Δ90d, Demand are all off-screen" and frames the landing view as looking like "any other price table (name + avg + low sell)." But sell_score (the "Score" column, ResultsTable.svelte:143) IS rendered near the left AND is the default sort key (App.svelte:111 activePreset='default', :134 defaultSort sell_score dir -1). sell_score is itself the headline differentiator — a curated, liquidity-aware ranking — and it is on-screen and drives row order. So the unique value is NOT fully hidden; the ranking signal is the most prominent thing on the page. What's buried is the *supporting* evidence columns (volume_48h, delta_90d_pct, ratio). (2) The default view renders 14 columns, not 15: the `delta` column (Δ, line 142) is filtered out when no prior snapshot is loaded, which is always true on first run (ResultsTable.svelte:168, hasDeltas false). Everything else verified exactly: ALL_COLUMNS = 15 defs (139-155), default preset has no `columns` key (131-135) so visibleColumns is null (App.svelte:166) and the narrowing filter is skipped (ResultsTable.svelte:169), other 4 presets narrow to 6-8 cols, .wrap uses overflow-x:auto (486) with table min-width:max-content (492), workspace max-width 1720px (1742). Severity lowered major→minor: the primary differentiator (sell-score ranking) is visible and default-sorted, the curated presets that surface the buried columns are one prominent chip-click away, and horizontal scroll is a recoverable (not blocking) discovery cost. It's a real first-impression polish/UX gap, not something that blocks or seriously annoys the core 'what to sell' task — the ranked answer is already on screen.

#### [🟡 minor] Relic planner silently excludes all non-Intact relics and the empty state falsely says "No relics in your inventory"
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — Relics tab
- **Evidence:** relic-planner.ts:54 `if (rec.subtype !== 'intact') continue;` drops Exceptional/Flawless/Radiant relics entirely. The resolver does preserve all four refinements (resolver.ts:52 REFINEMENTS set, subtype = last.toLowerCase()). The sidebar Relics nav only renders when relicPlan.length>0 (App.svelte:980), and the empty state reads "No relics in your inventory. Once you pick up relics, this planner ranks them…" (App.svelte:1317-1318) — the lede admits "(Intact state)" (App.svelte:1269) but the empty copy contradicts it.
- **Why it's friction:** End-game players routinely refine relics to Radiant before cracking (better rare-drop odds). A user who holds 50 Radiant relics and zero Intact gets either no Relics tab at all, or — if they reach it via a persisted view — a message telling them they own no relics, which is plainly false. The planner's whole job ("which of MY relics should I crack tonight?") silently fails for the players most likely to care, with no signal that refined relics were filtered out.
- **Suggested fix:** Either rank refined relics too (use the matching refinement's drop table) or, at minimum, count refined relics and show an honest empty/info state: "You own N refined relics; the planner currently models Intact drops only." Don't claim "No relics in your inventory" when subtyped relic rows exist in `resolved.owned`.
- **Verifier note:** Core evidence is all accurate and verified: relic-planner.ts:54 drops every non-Intact relic; resolver.ts:67 sets subtype=last.toLowerCase() so Exceptional/Flawless/Radiant relics really do exist as distinct owned rows (corroborated by relic-planner.test.ts:55, a radiant fixture); App.svelte:980 gates the Relics nav on relicPlan.length>0; App.svelte:1317-1318 says "No relics in your inventory."; App.svelte:1269 lede admits "(Intact state)". I also confirmed the finder's "persisted view" caveat is real and stronger than stated: effectiveView (App.svelte:699-703) has explicit fallback guards for baro and orders but NONE for relics, so a localStorage-persisted view='relics' (VIEW_KEY 'wfminv:view-v1', set by setView at line 94) renders the false empty state whenever relicPlan is empty. The only mis-rating is severity. Finder said "major"; for the first-run onboarding lens this is a minor. (1) The relic planner is a secondary tab, not the core "what to sell right now" flow. (2) The most common refined-relic-holder path is silent feature absence (no Relics nav at all), which is annoying but not a false claim. (3) The actual false-message path additionally requires a prior session where the user visited Relics with Intact relics present, then later having zero Intact relics — a real but compound precondition, not a pure first-run state. Both halves of the claim hold; impact is confined and conditional, so minor, not major.

#### [🟡 minor] Set picks and Relics value parts at raw low_sell, bypassing the troll-ask clamp the Sell table relies on — the same part shows different worth across surfaces
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — Set picks / Relics tabs vs Sell table
- **Evidence:** Sell-score deliberately routes every price through clearingPrice() to neutralise a lone 1p troll undercut or a 2,999p fantasy ask (sell-priority.ts:42-63, with the documented akbolto/corpus_void_key bugs it fixed). But set-recos.ts:79/95/117 and relic-planner.ts:63-65 read me.low_sell directly with no clamp. So a part with one 1p troll ask reports its honest clamped value in the Sell table yet a near-zero value in Set picks' "sell as a set for Xp / net +Yp" math and in the relic EPP.
- **Why it's friction:** These secondary surfaces give concrete plat recommendations ("buy the missing part for Ap, sell the set for Bp, net +Cp"; "Crack: 12.4 p/crack"). A single troll listing on any constituent part skews those numbers in exactly the way the Sell table was hardened against — so the user gets an inconsistent worth for the same item depending on which tab they're on, and the set/relic recommendations can be quietly wrong (the documented failure mode the clamp exists to prevent).
- **Suggested fix:** Reuse clearingPrice(m) for component and reward valuation in set-recos.ts and relic-planner.ts so all three value surfaces agree and inherit the anti-manipulation clamp.
- **Verifier note:** The core technical claim holds and all citations verify: clearingPrice() (sell-priority.ts:52-63) is imported only by sell-priority.ts and App.svelte; set-recos.ts (lines 79/95/117) and relic-planner.ts (lines 63-65) read me?.low_sell directly with no clamp, so set "net +Cp" math and relic EPP inherit the troll/fantasy-ask distortion the clamp exists to neutralize (documented akbolto 1p / corpus_void_key 2,999p cases, sell-priority.ts:44-50, mirrored at App.svelte:346). But the finder over-states "the same part shows different worth across surfaces": the displayed low_sell COLUMN is also raw/unclamped in the Sell table itself (App.svelte:397) and is shown raw in set/relic cards (App.svelte:1305, 1243). The clamp is applied ONLY to DERIVED synthetic numbers — sell_score (sell-priority.ts:68), plat_per_100d (App.svelte:348-351), and the timing/band signal. So a user reading the literal low_sell value sees the SAME number on every surface; the real divergence is that the Sell table's RANKING/SCORE and deal badges are clamped while the set-flip and relic recommendation math are not. The bug is "recommendation math built from a manipulable input," not "displayed price differs per tab." Direction is also two-way: a 1p troll ask deflates set net / relic EPP, while a fantasy high ask on a dead reward inflates EPP. Severity minor is correct — bounded to parts carrying an outlier ask (lowSell*3 < median, or vol<2 & lowSell>median*3), affects only secondary surfaces, never blocks onboarding.

#### [🟡 minor] Headline stats (Sellable / Potential) ignore the table's name and pill filters, so the strip and the table disagree the moment a user filters
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — stats strip vs filtered table
- **Evidence:** Sellable = results.length and Potential = sum of results' potential_plat (App.svelte:1052, 614-615) — both derived from the App-level results array. The name filter and pill filter are local to ResultsTable (ResultsTable.svelte:52, 67) and the toolbar's own "{sorted.length} rows" reflects them (ResultsTable.svelte:305). So typing a name or selecting "peak 88" updates the table count and body but leaves "Sellable 405" and the Potential total unchanged.
- **Why it's friction:** A new user reads the big stats strip as the summary of what they're looking at. After filtering to peaks they see a 88-row table but "Sellable 405" and a Potential total covering all 405 — two numbers on the same screen that contradict each other with no explanation of which scope each reflects. It quietly undermines confidence in the dashboard's bookkeeping right where the user is trying to size a decision.
- **Suggested fix:** Either recompute the headline stats against the same filtered/sorted set the table shows (requires lifting the table filters to App, see the List-CTA finding), or label the strip explicitly ("across all sellable rows") so it's clearly a different scope than the filtered table count.

#### [🟡 minor] The first-session "About the Score column" banner stays put on presets that don't sort by Score, mis-teaching the differentiator
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Reading the ranked sell list after switching presets (Trending / Ducats)
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:1151 gates the score-explainer only on `results.length > 0 && !scoreExplainerDismissed` — never on `activePreset`. Observed live: clicking Trending (sort label becomes 'Δ 90d ↓', top row 'Pain Points' score 70) leaves the banner reading verbatim 'About the “Score” column. Expected plat per day… Higher = better' even though Score is not the sort key and the rows are ordered by Δ90d.
- **Why it's friction:** The score-explainer is the single most important piece of onboarding copy in the whole product — it teaches the liquidity-weighted metric that is the entire reason to use this over browse.wf/warframe.me. On Trending and Ducats it points the new user's attention at a column they are NOT ranking by, so the first thing they learn about the differentiator is attached to the wrong list ordering. A newcomer who lands on or clicks Trending reads a confident explanation of a number that isn't driving the order in front of them.
- **Suggested fix:** Either suppress / re-word the banner when `activePreset` has a non-sell_score defaultSort (e.g. Trending → explain Δ90d, Ducats → explain p/100d), or anchor the banner to whatever the active sort column is. At minimum keep it Default-only.
- **Verifier note:** The cited code is accurate: App.svelte:1151 gates the banner on `results.length > 0 && !scoreExplainerDismissed` with no `activePreset` reference, and Trending (delta_90d_pct, App.svelte:148) and Ducats (plat_per_100d, App.svelte:142) do not sort by sell_score while Default does (App.svelte:134). But the finder overstates impact and severity. (1) The "Score" column is still present and rendered on both Trending and Ducats (columns lists at App.svelte:147 and :139 both include 'sell_score'), so the banner describes a real, visible column — not a phantom. (2) The banner copy is factually correct on every preset: it explains what the Score column means and never claims the list is sorted by Score. It even self-identifies as a per-column explainer ("Click ? on any column header for the same kind of explainer", App.svelte:1158-1159), i.e. a column tooltip, not a sort-order description. Nothing taught is wrong, so "mis-teaching the differentiator" is overstated. (3) First contact is Default (activePreset initialized to 'default', App.svelte:111), where the banner IS correctly aligned with the sell_score sort; the mismatch only arises if the user switches presets before dismissing. This is a contextual-relevance nit (banner would ideally track the active sort), not a blocking or misleading defect. Downgrade major → minor.

#### [🟡 minor] Empty-state quick-fix button silently drops the user off their active preset, and is a no-op when the real cause was a preset filter
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — clicking the 'fix' button in the empty Sell table
- **Evidence:** relaxFilters (App.svelte:643-648) directly mutates minPrice/minOwned/typeFilter/hideAtLvl. The preset-sync effect (App.svelte:185-204) then detects the filters no longer match the active preset and sets activePreset = null. If the table was emptied by a preset's vaultOnly/minVol/minMedian/tag clause (not covered by emptyReason), the mutated primitive doesn't lift that clause, so results stays empty.
- **Why it's friction:** Two compounding surprises: (1) the preset pill the user was on silently goes inactive and the hint flips to 'custom — saved preset cleared', with no notice that their preset just got abandoned; (2) when the genuine cause was the preset's own filter, the button appears to do nothing — the table stays blank — which reads as a broken button. A new user's first interaction with the recovery affordance teaches them the recovery doesn't work.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the empty-state recovery preset-aware: if a preset is active, the primary action should be 'Reset to Default preset' (clears vaultOnly/minVol/minMedian/tags), not a single-primitive relax. If a primitive relax is still offered, surface that it will clear the active preset before doing it.
- **Verifier note:** The cited evidence is accurate at the line level: relaxFilters (App.svelte:643-648) mutates only minPrice/minOwned/typeFilter/hideAtLvl; the preset-sync $effect (185-204) then nulls activePreset; and emptyReason (619-640) only diagnoses those four primitives, ignoring the vaultOnly/minVol/minMedian/tag clauses that computeResults also applies (308-337). Surprise #1 (preset silently goes inactive, hint flips to "custom — saved preset cleared" at line 1082, with no confirm/toast/aria-live) is fully confirmed.

But the finder's core "no-op" claim is OVER-BROAD and wrong for 3 of the 4 clauses it names. computeResults gates vaultOnly/minVol/minMedian on PRESETS[activePreset]?.x (lines 323/330/336). When relaxFilters clears the preset (activePreset -> null), those clauses are LIFTED automatically, so the table does NOT stay empty for the Vaulted or Trending presets — the button works (and actually surfaces rows). The genuine no-op only holds for the TAG clause (Ducats activeTags:['prime'], Sets activeTags:['set']), because activeTags is filtered directly in computeResults (315-319), is NOT preset-gated, and relaxFilters never resets it (it touches only the four primitives). So the no-op is scoped to two tag-distinguished presets in a tag-driven empty state, not the universal "recovery doesn't work" the finder framed.

Net: real bug, but narrower and lower-impact than stated. Surprise #1 is cosmetic (the table still populates). Surprise #2 is a real dead-button but only on Ducats/Sets when the user owns no prime/set items — a specific, recoverable edge, not a journey-blocker. Downgraded major -> minor.

#### [🟡 minor] Set-completion 'flip is better' recommendation can fire on near-dead set markets because it compares raw low_sell totals with no liquidity or volume gate
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — opening the Set picks pane and acting on a 'Complete X for +Np' card
- **Evidence:** deriveSetRecos compares set_low_sell against the sum of part low_sells using raw low_sell only (set-recos.ts:79,95,116-132); there is no volume/vol_48h check on either the set or the missing parts. The card then tells the user to spend real plat buying the missing part(s) and sell the assembled set (App.svelte:1239-1244). The sell-priority module exists precisely because raw low_sell overstates clearable value (sell-priority.ts:1-22), but the set planner doesn't use clearingPrice or any liquidity signal.
- **Why it's friction:** The net-plat headline is an arbitrage that only pays if both the missing part and the assembled set actually trade. On a thin set market the user can spend plat to buy a part, assemble, and then sit on an unsellable set — the opposite of 'measurably better at what to sell'. The card presents a single confident +Np number with no patience/liquidity caveat, the same overstatement the sell-score was built to avoid.
- **Suggested fix:** Gate near-complete recos on minimum 48h volume for the set (and ideally the missing parts), or annotate cards whose set/parts are low-volume with the existing 'patience' framing so the user knows the flip may not clear.
- **Verifier note:** Severity is fair at minor, but the finder slightly under-states the surface: the gap is not only "no volume gate" — set-recos.ts never imports anything from sell-priority.ts (no clearingPrice, no vol), so it also inherits the exact lone-aspirational-ask / troll-undercut distortion that clearingPrice() was written to clamp (sell-priority.ts:42-63). A stale fantasy set ask inflates net_plat; a single 1p troll set ask can wrongly suppress an otherwise-good card. Also worth noting: a missing part with low_sell=0 (no live ask = unbuyable) is treated as free (missingCost line 117), which inflates the flip further and is itself a liquidity blind spot the finder didn't call out. The one partial protection the finder didn't credit is the net>partsLowSellSum-missingCost gate (line 121) and the setLowSell>0 guard (line 116) — these are relative-value gates, not liquidity gates, so they don't refute the claim, but they keep it at minor rather than major.

#### [⚪ polish] No-match name filter dead-ends to a blank table with no message and no clear button
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — user types a name filter that matches nothing
- **Evidence:** emptyReason (App.svelte:618-640) only diagnoses no-market/price/owned/type/kept exclusions and returns null once results.length>0; the name-substring filter is applied downstream in ResultsTable (per live report, ResultsTable.svelte has no empty-row state), so a nonsense filter renders the header '0 rows · sorted by Score' over an empty body with no 'no matches / clear filter' affordance.
- **Why it's friction:** A confusing dead end at the payoff screen — the user can't tell whether their data is broken or the filter is just too narrow, and there's no one-click exit back to results.
- **Suggested fix:** Render an explicit 'No items match "<query>" — clear filter' row (with a clear button) in ResultsTable when the filtered set is empty but the unfiltered set is not.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate and verified. App.svelte:619-640 emptyReason only fires when results.length===0 (the upstream owned/price/type/kept filters) and never accounts for the name substring filter, which lives in ResultsTable. In ResultsTable.svelte the name filter is at lines 237-241 (sorted = results.filter on name/slug includes(f)); the tbody {#each paged} at 351-438 renders nothing when sorted is empty, and the toolbar shows "{sorted.length} rows · sorted by …" (304-308) with no "no matches" text and no clear button. So a nonsense name filter does render an empty table with only a "0 rows" header. However the finder over-rates severity and slightly overstates the confusion: the Filter-by-name input (284-289) stays visible at the top with the user's typed text still bound in it, and the row count updates live as they type, so the recovery path (delete the text they just typed) is in front of them — this is a missing-nicety polish gap, not a true dead-end where the user can't tell what happened. There is also no separate "clear" affordance on the input, confirming the missing one-click exit, but that is a polish item. Downgrading minor -> polish.

#### [⚪ polish] A no-match name filter dead-ends with a blank table and no clear-filter exit
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — filtering the Sell list
- **Evidence:** emptyReason (App.svelte:618-640) only diagnoses zero-results caused by price/owned/type/kept exclusions; it returns null when results>0. The name textbox filter is applied downstream in ResultsTable.svelte (per the live report, no empty-row state), so a nonsense query like 'zzzz' yields a full header reading '0 rows · sorted by Score ↓' over an empty body with no 'no matches / clear filter' affordance.
- **Why it's friction:** A confusing dead end during normal exploration: the user sees columns and a sort label but nothing else, with no obvious way back. Low stakes but it reads as broken.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'no rows match "<query>" — clear filter' empty state with a clear button in ResultsTable.svelte, or feed the name filter into emptyReason.
- **Verifier note:** The technical evidence is fully accurate and verified: emptyReason (App.svelte:619-640) returns null when results.length>0 (line 620) and never inspects the name filter; the name/text filter lives in ResultsTable.svelte (state at line 52, applied at lines 238-240, input "Filter by name…" at line 284-289); the tbody loop {#each paged as r} (line 352) has NO {:else} branch, so a no-match query empties the body while the toolbar still reads "{sorted.length} rows · sorted by ..." (line 305) = "0 rows · sorted by Score ↓", and the pager vanishes (gated on sorted.length > pageSize, line 441). So a dedicated empty-state / clear-filter button is indeed absent. However the finder overstates "no obvious way back": the filter textbox is bound (bind:value={filter}, line 287) and remains visible at the top of the table still showing the user's own query, so clearing is one edit away in the box they just typed into, and "0 rows" gives explicit feedback that the filter (not the app) produced the empty result. That makes this polish, not minor — it is cosmetic friction on a secondary exploration action, not a real blocker, and well outside the onboarding hard-blockers (TTY passphrase, port confusion, Downloads pointer, stale market.json).

#### [⚪ polish] 'Trending' preset ranks low-value percentage spikes above genuinely valuable movers
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Step 6 — clicking the Trending preset to find what's moving
- **Evidence:** Trending sorts purely by delta_90d_pct desc (PRESETS.trending.defaultSort, App.svelte:148) with only minVol 10 / minMedian 5 floors (App.svelte:149-150). Observed live: top rows were 'Pain Points' ▲426% score 70 and 'Meso W5 Relic' ▲100% score 70, ranked ABOVE 'Tempo Royale' (▲76%, score 118) and other higher-plat movers.
- **Why it's friction:** A user clicks 'Trending' expecting 'the valuable things moving right now', but a +426% blip on a 3p→16p item outranks a more valuable, more liquid mover. The percentage column makes cheap, thin items look like the headline opportunity. It's a softer dead-end than a blank table, but it points attention at the wrong rows for the sell decision.
- **Suggested fix:** Tie-break or pre-rank Trending by a value floor (e.g. sort by delta_90d_pct but require sell_score above a threshold, or surface a blended 'momentum × value' score) so low-plat percentage spikes don't crowd out valuable movers.
- **Verifier note:** Code evidence is accurate: trending defaultSort is delta_90d_pct desc (App.svelte:148) with floors minVol 10 / minMedian 5 (App.svelte:149-150), applied at App.svelte:330-337, and sell_score does not influence the trending sort. But the finder over-rated severity and over-stated impact. (1) Severity should be polish, not minor: this is a ranking-philosophy opinion, not friction. A preset literally named 'Trending' with hint 'movers vs 90d median · vol ≥ 10 · baseline ≥ 5p' (App.svelte:146) sorting by movement is doing exactly what it advertises. (2) The result is not a dead-end at all: the table is populated and the sell_score and low_sell columns ARE displayed in the trending column set (App.svelte:147), and the table is re-sortable by header click, so a user wanting value ordering is one click away. (3) The two floors already deliberately exclude the worst penny-junk pumps (comments at App.svelte:327-337 cite Goopolla/fish wash-trade cases); the finder's '3p->16p' example would be filtered by minMedian 5 unless its 90d baseline genuinely cleared 5p, in which case it is a legitimately-priced mover, not noise. For a first-run ONBOARDING audit specifically, this does not block or meaningfully annoy a new user reaching 'what to sell'.

#### [⚪ polish] Sidebar "Sell" nav badge silently rescopes with the active preset (405 → 217), so the persistent count of "what to sell" is not stable
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** Switching presets while glancing at the sidebar Sell count
- **Evidence:** App.svelte:972 renders the Sell nav badge as `{results.length}`, and `results` is recomputed per active preset (computeResults applies preset minVol/minMedian/vaultOnly filters, App.svelte:323-337). Observed live: Default preset shows nav badge 405; clicking Trending changes the SAME sidebar badge to 217; back to Default restores 405.
- **Why it's friction:** A sidebar nav badge reads as a stable inventory-wide fact ('you have 405 things worth selling'). Having it drop to 217 the moment the user explores the Trending pill — with the pill living in a different region of the screen — makes the navigation count feel unreliable and conflates 'total sellable' with 'rows in the current filtered view'. The headline Sellable stat doing this is already logged; the nav badge is a separate persistent surface that compounds it.
- **Suggested fix:** Drive the Sell nav badge from a preset-independent count (full sellable set) and let the in-pane row counter reflect the active preset, so the nav stays a stable orientation cue.
- **Verifier note:** The code evidence is accurate (App.svelte:972 = `{results.length}`; results is preset-filtered via computeResults, minVol/minMedian/vaultOnly at 323-337; Trending sets minVol:10/minMedian:5 at 149-150, Default sets none — so the badge genuinely moves on preset switch). But the finding's framing is wrong on two counts that inflate its severity. (1) The finder claims "The headline Sellable stat doing this is already logged" — it is NOT logged anywhere: not in the punch-list memory (wfm-app-gaps-punchlist.md lists sell-score outliers, $effect read+write, set arbitrage, routines — not a rescoping Sellable count), nor in any CLAUDE.md. The "compounds an already-logged issue" premise is unsupported. (2) The nav badge (972) and the headline Sellable stat card (1051-1052) both read the SAME `results.length` variable and rescope in lockstep — they are two renderings of one number, not "a separate persistent surface that compounds" a different one. The dominant surface is the large "Sellable: 405" stat card directly above the table; the sidebar badge is a tiny mirror. Presets are explicit user actions with visible hint text (e.g. "vol ≥ 10 · baseline ≥ 5p", line 146) signalling the view is filtered, so a count tracking the active filter is defensible behavior rather than a clear bug. Severity drops from minor to polish: real, but a 9px sidebar badge is not a load-bearing orientation cue for a first-run user, and the suggested fix would create the actual inconsistency (badge != headline) it claims to avoid unless the headline is changed too.

#### [⚪ polish] Relic planner and the Sell table give two different, unreconciled 'best relics' answers for the same owned relics
- **Platform:** both · **Step:** 6 — comparing the Relics nav pane against the relics that float to the top of the Sell table
- **Evidence:** Relic planner ranks and headlines by single-crack EPP: deriveRelicPlan sorts candidates by `epp` (relic-planner.ts:95) and the card headlines `p.epp` per-crack (App.svelte:1286). The Sell table ranks the very same relic rows by sell_score (computeResults pushes relics with their full owned count; out.sort by sell_score at App.svelte:424). EPP (expected reward value per crack) and sell_score (plat/day from listing the relic itself) are different metrics with no cross-reference in either view.
- **Why it's friction:** The product's promise is one confident 'sell THIS now' answer. A relic that tops the Sell table (high sell_score — list the relic) can be absent from the Relics pane's top 3 (which says crack it for its drops), and vice versa. Neither view acknowledges the other exists, so a user who notices the disagreement has no way to know which action the tool actually recommends for that relic — list it, or crack it. The relics also dominate the Sell top (already logged) which makes the collision visible immediately.
- **Suggested fix:** On relic rows in the Sell table, show a small 'see Relic planner' affordance (and conversely note the relic's own list price in the planner card), so the two answers are explicitly framed as 'sell the relic for X' vs 'crack it for ~Y expected' rather than two silent, contradictory rankings.
- **Verifier note:** Evidence is accurate and verified: relic-planner.ts:95 sorts candidates by `epp`; App.svelte:1286 headlines `p.epp` p/crack under the verb "Crack" (App.svelte:1277); App.svelte:424 sorts the Sell table by `sell_score`; relics are pushed into the same `out` array with full owned count (App.svelte:386-391) and have 320 live entries in market.json with avg/vol/top_buy, so the same owned relic genuinely appears in both views ranked by two unrelated metrics, with no cross-reference anywhere (confirmed by grep over ResultsTable.svelte and the relic card). One refinement: the relic planner only considers `subtype === 'intact'` relics (relic-planner.ts:54), while the Sell table includes all subtypes — so the overlap set is intact relics specifically. The finder over-rated severity. This belongs at polish, not minor: the two numbers are not actually contradictory — sell-the-relic (~27p) vs crack-for-drops (~Y EPP) are distinct, mutually-exclusive actions, and BOTH numbers are visible to the user, so the information needed to choose is present; it is merely not juxtaposed. The relic pane is explicitly labeled ("Crack", "p/crack", "rewards moving") and is a supplementary planning surface, not a competing "what to sell" verdict. It is a step-6 power-user observation ("a user who notices the disagreement"), not onboarding friction that blocks or annoys a new user, who simply gets a working ranked Sell table.
